\NormalTok{    )}
    
    \CommentTok{\# Register with same version}
\NormalTok{    target\_fs.register\_feature\_view(}
\NormalTok{        feature\_view}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{target\_fv,}
\NormalTok{        version}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{version,}
\NormalTok{    )}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-governance}{%
\section{Governance Considerations}\label{sec-governance}}

\hypertarget{avoiding-duplicate-features}{%
\subsection{Avoiding Duplicate
Features}\label{avoiding-duplicate-features}}

A recurring challenge in fast-moving teams is \textbf{accidentally
re-creating features} that already exist.

\textbf{Recommended Practices}:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Establish team-wide naming standards}
\item
  \textbf{Require meaningful descriptions and tags}
\item
  \textbf{Query existing features before creating new ones}
\end{enumerate}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/feature_discovery.sql}{\texttt{\_code/feature\_discovery.sql}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Search for existing features by name pattern (clickstream{-}aligned)}
\KeywordTok{SELECT} 
\NormalTok{    TABLE\_NAME }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_VIEW,}
\NormalTok{    COLUMN\_NAME }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_NAME,}
    \KeywordTok{COMMENT} \KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ DESCRIPTION}
\KeywordTok{FROM}\NormalTok{ INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.}\KeywordTok{COLUMNS}
\KeywordTok{WHERE}\NormalTok{ TABLE\_CATALOG }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\textquotesingle{}}
  \KeywordTok{AND}\NormalTok{ TABLE\_SCHEMA }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\textquotesingle{}}
  \KeywordTok{AND}\NormalTok{ (}
\NormalTok{      COLUMN\_NAME }\KeywordTok{LIKE} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}\%ORDER\_\%\textquotesingle{}}
      \KeywordTok{OR}\NormalTok{ COLUMN\_NAME }\KeywordTok{LIKE} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}\%EVENT\_\%\textquotesingle{}}
      \KeywordTok{OR} \KeywordTok{COMMENT}\NormalTok{ ILIKE }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}\%order\%\textquotesingle{}}
\NormalTok{  )}
\KeywordTok{ORDER} \KeywordTok{BY}\NormalTok{ TABLE\_NAME, COLUMN\_NAME;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Field Tip}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

This is particularly important when multiple squads work on the same
entity (e.g., multiple USER or SESSION FeatureView pipelines) or when
onboarding new teams unfamiliar with existing feature catalogs.

\end{tcolorbox}

\hypertarget{sec-versioning}{%
\subsection{Feature Versioning}\label{sec-versioning}}

Version FeatureViews to enable safe updates and rollbacks.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-important-color}{\faExclamation}\hspace{0.5em}{Key Insight}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-important-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-important-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

Versioning happens at the \textbf{FeatureView level, not per individual
feature}. A FV version is treated as an immutable bundle of features.
When you change feature definitions, create a new FV version---the
system does not automatically track per-feature deltas between versions.

\end{tcolorbox}

\hypertarget{recommended-version-naming}{%
\subsubsection{Recommended Version
Naming}\label{recommended-version-naming}}

Use \textbf{zero-padded, sequential version identifiers} so
lexicographic order matches creation order:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# RECOMMENDED: Zero{-}padded sequential versions}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V02"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V10"}\NormalTok{)  }\CommentTok{\# Sorts correctly after V09}

\CommentTok{\# ALSO ACCEPTABLE: Environment{-}prefixed versions}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"DEV\_V01"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"PROD\_V03"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{getting-the-latest-version}{%
\subsubsection{Getting the ``Latest''
Version}\label{getting-the-latest-version}}

Feature Store is intentionally not opinionated on version
semantics---there's \textbf{no built-in ``latest version'' alias}.
Create a helper utility:

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/version_utils.py}{\texttt{\_code/version\_utils.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ get\_latest\_feature\_view(}
\NormalTok{    fs: FeatureStore,}
\NormalTok{    feature\_view\_name: }\BuiltInTok{str}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{) }\OperatorTok{{-}\textgreater{}}\NormalTok{ FeatureView:}
    \CommentTok{"""Get the most recent version of a FeatureView."""}
\NormalTok{    versions }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.list\_feature\_views(feature\_view\_name}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{feature\_view\_name)}
    
    \CommentTok{\# Sort by version string (works with zero{-}padded versions)}
\NormalTok{    versions\_sorted }\OperatorTok{=} \BuiltInTok{sorted}\NormalTok{(versions, key}\OperatorTok{=}\KeywordTok{lambda}\NormalTok{ fv: fv.version, reverse}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{)}
    
    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ versions\_sorted[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{] }\ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ versions\_sorted }\ControlFlowTok{else} \VariableTok{None}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{feature-store-ownership-slas}{%
\subsection{Feature Store Ownership \&
SLAs}\label{feature-store-ownership-slas}}

Define clear ownership for each Feature Store or domain:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# feature\_manifest.yaml}
\FunctionTok{feature\_views}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{  }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ }\FunctionTok{name}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ USER\_ORDER\_AGGREGATES}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{owner}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ marketing{-}ds@company.com}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{team}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ Marketing Data Science}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{description}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ Core user behavior from ORDERS and ORDER\_ITEMS (ORDER\_CNT, ORDER\_AMT\_SUM)}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{consumers}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ churn{-}model}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ ltv{-}model}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{sla}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{      }\FunctionTok{refresh\_frequency}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\StringTok{"1 hour"}
\AttributeTok{      }\FunctionTok{max\_latency\_minutes}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\DecValTok{90}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{feature-discovery-search}{%
\subsection{Feature Discovery \&
Search}\label{feature-discovery-search}}

Use metadata queries to find features across the organization:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ search\_features(fs: FeatureStore, search\_term: }\BuiltInTok{str}\NormalTok{) }\OperatorTok{{-}\textgreater{}} \BuiltInTok{list}\NormalTok{:}
    \CommentTok{"""Search for features by name or description."""}
\NormalTok{    all\_fvs }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.list\_feature\_views()}
\NormalTok{    results }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ []}
    
    \ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ fv\_info }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ all\_fvs.collect():}
\NormalTok{        fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.get\_feature\_view(name}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{fv\_info.name, version}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{fv\_info.version)}
        \CommentTok{\# Check name and description}
        \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ search\_term.lower() }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ fv.name.lower():}
\NormalTok{            results.append(fv)}
        \ControlFlowTok{elif}\NormalTok{ fv.desc }\KeywordTok{and}\NormalTok{ search\_term.lower() }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ fv.desc.lower():}
\NormalTok{            results.append(fv)}
    
    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ results}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices}{%
\section{Best Practices}\label{best-practices}}

\hypertarget{start-simple-scale-as-needed}{%
\subsection{1. Start Simple, Scale as
Needed}\label{start-simple-scale-as-needed}}

\begin{verbatim}
Start with:
├── Single database (`FEATURE_STORE_DEMO`)
├── Schema-based environments (DEV/TEST/PROD)
├── Basic RBAC (`FS_ADMIN_ROLE` / `FS_DEV_ROLE` / `FS_CONSUMER_ROLE`)
└── Manual promotion

Scale to:
├── Multiple databases by domain
├── Multi-account for compliance
├── Granular RBAC with environment-specific roles
└── CI/CD automated promotion
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{establish-naming-conventions-early}{%
\subsection{2. Establish Naming Conventions
Early}\label{establish-naming-conventions-early}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3824}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3529}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2647}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Object Type
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Convention
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Example
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Database & \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO} (guide) &
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO} \\
Source data schema & \texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA} & Raw \texttt{USERS},
\texttt{EVENTS}, \texttt{ORDERS}, \ldots{} \\
Schema (env) & \texttt{\textless{}ENV\textgreater{}} & \texttt{DEV},
\texttt{TEST}, \texttt{PROD} \\
Schema (domain) & \texttt{\textless{}DOMAIN\textgreater{}} or
\texttt{\textless{}DOMAIN\textgreater{}\_FEATURES} & \texttt{MARKETING},
\texttt{SHARED\_FEATURES} \\
FeatureView &
\texttt{\textless{}ENTITY\textgreater{}\_\textless{}DOMAIN\textgreater{}\_FV}
& \texttt{USER\_ORDER\_FV}, \texttt{SESSION\_EVENT\_FV} \\
Entity & SCREAMING\_SNAKE singular & \texttt{USER}, \texttt{PRODUCT},
\texttt{SESSION}, \texttt{ORDER} \\
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{separate-compute-by-environment}{%
\subsection{3. Separate Compute by
Environment}\label{separate-compute-by-environment}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Environment{-}specific warehouses with appropriate sizing}
\KeywordTok{CREATE}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE FS\_DEV\_WH      }\KeywordTok{WITH}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE\_SIZE }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}XSMALL\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{ AUTO\_SUSPEND }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{60}\NormalTok{;}
\KeywordTok{CREATE}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE FS\_TEST\_WH     }\KeywordTok{WITH}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE\_SIZE }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}SMALL\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{  AUTO\_SUSPEND }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{120}\NormalTok{;}
\KeywordTok{CREATE}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE FS\_PROD\_WH     }\KeywordTok{WITH}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE\_SIZE }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}MEDIUM\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{ AUTO\_SUSPEND }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{300}\NormalTok{;}
\KeywordTok{CREATE}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE FS\_PROD\_OFT\_WH }\KeywordTok{WITH}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE\_SIZE }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}SMALL\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{ AUTO\_SUSPEND }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{60}\NormalTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{feature-store-health-monitoring}{%
\subsection{4. Feature Store Health
Monitoring}\label{feature-store-health-monitoring}}

Monitor Feature Store health using Snowflake views:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Check Dynamic Table refresh status}
\KeywordTok{SELECT} 
\NormalTok{    NAME,}
\NormalTok{    REFRESH\_MODE,}
\NormalTok{    SCHEDULING\_STATE,}
\NormalTok{    LAST\_COMPLETED\_REFRESH\_START\_TIME }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ LAST\_REFRESH\_START\_TS,}
\NormalTok{    LAST\_REFRESH\_TRIGGER}
\KeywordTok{FROM} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLES())}
\KeywordTok{WHERE}\NormalTok{ TABLE\_CATALOG }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\textquotesingle{}}
  \KeywordTok{AND}\NormalTok{ SCHEMA\_NAME }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\textquotesingle{}}
\KeywordTok{ORDER} \KeywordTok{BY}\NormalTok{ LAST\_COMPLETED\_REFRESH\_START\_TIME }\KeywordTok{DESC}\NormalTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls}{%
\section{Common Pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-no-environment-isolation}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: No Environment
Isolation}\label{pitfall-1-no-environment-isolation}}

\textbf{Problem}: Developers experimenting in production Feature Store.

\textbf{Solution}: Always separate environments with RBAC. Developers
should never have write access to PROD.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-feature-duplication-across-teams}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Feature Duplication Across
Teams}\label{pitfall-2-feature-duplication-across-teams}}

\textbf{Problem}: Multiple teams create similar features independently.

\textbf{Solution}: Implement a shared Feature Store for common entities.
Require feature review before creation.

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-no-promotion-process}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: No Promotion
Process}\label{pitfall-3-no-promotion-process}}

\textbf{Problem}: Features move from dev to prod without validation.

\textbf{Solution}: Implement gated promotion with required tests and
approvals.

\hypertarget{pitfall-4-ignoring-cost-attribution}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 4: Ignoring Cost
Attribution}\label{pitfall-4-ignoring-cost-attribution}}

\textbf{Problem}: Unable to charge back Feature Store costs to teams.

\textbf{Solution}: Use separate warehouses per team/environment. Tag
resources appropriately.

\hypertarget{pitfall-5-over-engineering-early}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 5: Over-Engineering
Early}\label{pitfall-5-over-engineering-early}}

\textbf{Problem}: Building complex multi-account setup for a small team.

\textbf{Solution}: Start simple. Migrate to more complex patterns when
actually needed.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-1}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-1}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Pattern & When to Use & Key Benefit \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Single FS} & Small teams, POC & Simplicity \\
\textbf{Multi-Schema FS} & Multiple teams, domains & Organization \\
\textbf{Multi-Database FS} & Clear domain boundaries & Isolation \\
\textbf{Multi-Account FS} & Regulated industries & Compliance \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Environment Strategy & Isolation Level & Best For \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Schema-based} & Logical & Most teams \\
\textbf{Database-based} & Stronger logical & Growing orgs \\
\textbf{Multi-account} & Physical & Enterprise/Regulated \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{next-steps-2}{%
\section{Next Steps}\label{next-steps-2}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{entities-hierarchies}{Chapter 03:
Entities \& Hierarchies} to learn about entity design patterns, compound
keys, and entity relationships.

\hypertarget{entities-hierarchies}{%
\chapter{Entities \& Hierarchies}\label{entities-hierarchies}}

Entity design patterns, compound keys, and hierarchical relationships

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-3}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-3}}

Entities are the foundational building blocks of a Feature Store. They
define the business objects that features describe and determine how
features can be joined together. This chapter covers entity design
patterns, from simple single-key entities to complex compound keys and
hierarchical relationships.

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-2}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-2}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Design entities that accurately reflect your business domain
\item
  Choose between simple and compound entity keys
\item
  Model entity hierarchies for multi-level aggregations
\item
  Make informed decisions using the entity design framework
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{entity-fundamentals}{%
\section{Entity Fundamentals}\label{entity-fundamentals}}

An \textbf{Entity} represents a business object that features describe.
It defines:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{What} business concept the features relate to (for example
  User, Product, Session)
\item
  \textbf{How} features are retrieved via join keys
\item
  \textbf{Which} FeatureViews can be combined for a given request
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{Entity registration lifecycle}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

Register each entity with the Feature Store using
\texttt{fs.register\_entity(entity)} \textbf{before} you create or
register FeatureViews that reference it. Entities are \textbf{not}
auto-created when you register a FeatureView. If an entity is missing
from the registry, FeatureView registration fails until you register it
explicitly.

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Typical order: define entities, register each, then build FeatureViews}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_entity(visitor\_entity)}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_entity(user\_entity)}
\CommentTok{\# ... other entities ...}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/entity_definitions.py}{\texttt{\_code/entity\_definitions.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ Entity}

\CommentTok{\# Define an entity (register with fs.register\_entity before use in FeatureViews)}
\NormalTok{user\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Registered user in the clickstream platform"}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{entity-components}{%
\subsection{Entity Components}\label{entity-components}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2895}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3421}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3684}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Component
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Requirements
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{name} & Unique identifier within the Feature Store &
SCREAMING\_SNAKE\_CASE, descriptive \\
\texttt{join\_keys} & Column(s) that uniquely identify an instance &
Must exist in spine and FeatureView \\
\texttt{desc} & Human-readable description & Document the business
meaning \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{simple-entity-keys}{%
\section{Simple Entity Keys}\label{simple-entity-keys}}

Simple entities use a single column as the join key. This is the most
common pattern.

\hypertarget{examples}{%
\subsection{Examples}\label{examples}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Visitor (pre{-}login identity)}
\NormalTok{visitor\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"VISITOR"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"VISITOR\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Site visitor before or without login"}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# User entity}
\NormalTok{user\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Registered user with account"}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Household rollup}
\NormalTok{household\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"HOUSEHOLD"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"HOUSEHOLD\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Household containing one or more users"}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Product and category}
\NormalTok{product\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"PRODUCT"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Product in the catalog"}
\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{category\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"CATEGORY"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"CATEGORY\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Product taxonomy category"}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Session entity}
\NormalTok{session\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"SESSION\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"User browsing session"}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{when-to-use-simple-entities}{%
\subsection{When to Use Simple
Entities}\label{when-to-use-simple-entities}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5263}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4737}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Scenario
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Example
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Single business object & Users, products, sessions \\
Natural unique identifier exists & User ID, product ID, session ID \\
Features are always at this granularity & User-level churn prediction \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-compound-keys}{%
\section{Compound Entity Keys}\label{sec-compound-keys}}

Compound entities use multiple columns together as the join key.
Essential for many-to-many relationships.

\hypertarget{why-compound-keys}{%
\subsection{Why Compound Keys?}\label{why-compound-keys}}

\begin{verbatim}
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    PRODUCT-SUPPLIER RELATIONSHIP                        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                         │
│   PRODUCT_ID: P001              PRODUCT_SUPPLIER Table                  │
│   ┌───────────────┐             ┌────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│   │ Widget Pro    │────────────▶│ P001, S001: $10.00, 5 day lead     │  │
│   │               │             │ P001, S002: $9.50,  7 day lead     │  │
│   └───────────────┘             │ P001, S003: $11.00, 3 day lead     │  │
│                                 └────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│                                                                         │
│   To get specific supplier pricing, you need BOTH keys:                 │
│   (PRODUCT_ID, SUPPLIER_ID) → unique row                                │
│                                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{defining-compound-entities}{%
\subsection{Defining Compound
Entities}\label{defining-compound-entities}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/compound_entities.py}{\texttt{\_code/compound\_entities.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Primary compound entity: product–supplier (sourcing / many{-}to{-}many)}
\NormalTok{product\_supplier\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_SUPPLIER"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"SUPPLIER\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Product and supplier combination for sourcing features"}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# User–product affinity (interaction grain)}
\NormalTok{user\_product\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_PRODUCT"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"User{-}product affinity features"}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Order line within an order (USER places ORDER → ORDER\_ITEMS)}
\NormalTok{order\_item\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ITEM"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"LINE\_NUMBER"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Individual line item within an order"}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{when-to-use-compound-entities}{%
\subsection{When to Use Compound
Entities}\label{when-to-use-compound-entities}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2564}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2821}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4615}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Scenario
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Join Keys
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Example Use Case
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Many-to-many relationships & \texttt{{[}A\_ID,\ B\_ID{]}} & User-product
affinity \\
Intersection tables & \texttt{{[}PARENT\_ID,\ CHILD\_ID{]}} &
Product-supplier pricing \\
Sub-entity granularity & \texttt{{[}PARENT\_ID,\ SEQ{]}} & Order line
items \\
Time-partitioned entities & \texttt{{[}ENTITY\_ID,\ DATE{]}} & Daily
snapshots \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-hierarchies}{%
\section{Entity Hierarchies}\label{sec-hierarchies}}

Entities can form hierarchies where one entity ``rolls up'' to another.
This enables multi-level aggregations.

\hypertarget{clickstream-hierarchy-demo-domain}{%
\subsection{Clickstream hierarchy (demo
domain)}\label{clickstream-hierarchy-demo-domain}}

Relationships used throughout this guide (database
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO}, source schema \texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA},
Feature Store schema \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE}, warehouse
\texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}):

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{VISITOR} (\texttt{VISITOR\_ID}) → identified as →
  \textbf{USER} (\texttt{USER\_ID}) → belongs to → \textbf{HOUSEHOLD}
  (\texttt{HOUSEHOLD\_ID})
\item
  \textbf{USER} → has → \textbf{SESSION} (\texttt{SESSION\_ID}) →
  contains events
\item
  \textbf{USER} → places → \textbf{ORDER} → \textbf{ORDER\_ITEM} rows
  (\texttt{ORDER\_ID}, \texttt{LINE\_NUMBER})
\item
  \textbf{PRODUCT} (\texttt{PRODUCT\_ID}) → belongs to →
  \textbf{CATEGORY} (\texttt{CATEGORY\_ID})
\item
  \textbf{PRODUCT\_SUPPLIER} (\texttt{PRODUCT\_ID},
  \texttt{SUPPLIER\_ID}) is the compound key for supplier-specific
  product facts
\end{itemize}

\begin{verbatim}
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                   CLICKSTREAM ENTITY RELATIONSHIPS                       │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                         │
│   VISITOR ──identified as──▶ USER ──belongs to──▶ HOUSEHOLD             │
│                                │                                        │
│                    ┌───────────┴───────────┐                            │
│                    ▼                       ▼                            │
│              SESSION ──▶ events      ORDER ──▶ ORDER_ITEM               │
│                                                                         │
│   PRODUCT ──belongs to──▶ CATEGORY                                      │
│                                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{implementing-hierarchies}{%
\subsection{Implementing Hierarchies}\label{implementing-hierarchies}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/entity_hierarchies.py}{\texttt{\_code/entity\_hierarchies.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ Entity, FeatureView}

\CommentTok{\# Register each entity first: fs.register\_entity(visitor\_entity), etc.}
\NormalTok{visitor\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"VISITOR"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"VISITOR\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{household\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"HOUSEHOLD"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"HOUSEHOLD\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{user\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{session\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"SESSION\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}

\CommentTok{\# FeatureViews at different granularities (version labels: V01, V02, ...)}
\NormalTok{household\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"HOUSEHOLD\_FEATURES"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[household\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{household\_agg\_df,}
\NormalTok{    version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{,}
    \CommentTok{\# timestamp\_col, refresh\_freq, desc, ...}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{user\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_FEATURES"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_agg\_df,}
\NormalTok{    version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{session\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_FEATURES"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[session\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session\_df,}
\NormalTok{    version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{combining-hierarchical-features}{%
\subsection{Combining Hierarchical
Features}\label{combining-hierarchical-features}}

To use features from multiple hierarchy levels, your spine must include
all join keys:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Spine with multi{-}level keys (source tables in CLICKSTREAM\_DATA)}
\NormalTok{spine }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        s.SESSION\_ID,}
\StringTok{        s.USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        u.HOUSEHOLD\_ID,}
\StringTok{        s.SESSION\_START\_TS AS EVENT\_TS}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.SESSIONS s}
\StringTok{    JOIN FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.USERS u}
\StringTok{      ON s.USER\_ID = u.USER\_ID}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Generate dataset with features from all levels}
\NormalTok{dataset }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_dataset(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[session\_fv, user\_fv, household\_fv],}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{entity-design-patterns}{%
\section{Entity Design Patterns}\label{entity-design-patterns}}

\hypertarget{pattern-1-domain-aligned-entities}{%
\subsection{Pattern 1: Domain-Aligned
Entities}\label{pattern-1-domain-aligned-entities}}

Align entities with business domain concepts:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Clickstream / e{-}commerce domain (this guide)}
\NormalTok{USER }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{PRODUCT }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"PRODUCT"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{ORDER }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"ORDER"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}

\CommentTok{\# Financial domain}
\NormalTok{ACCOUNT }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"ACCOUNT"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"ACCOUNT\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{TRANSACTION }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"TRANSACTION"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"TXN\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{MERCHANT }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"MERCHANT"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"MERCHANT\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{pattern-2-interaction-entities}{%
\subsection{Pattern 2: Interaction
Entities}\label{pattern-2-interaction-entities}}

Model relationships between domain entities:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# User–product interaction (same grain as USER\_PRODUCT in compound examples)}
\NormalTok{USER\_PRODUCT }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_PRODUCT"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"User{-}product affinity and behavior"}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# User{-}Merchant interaction}
\NormalTok{USER\_MERCHANT }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_MERCHANT"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"MERCHANT\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"User spending patterns per merchant"}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-1}{%
\section{Best Practices}\label{best-practices-1}}

\hypertarget{use-descriptive-names}{%
\subsection{1. Use Descriptive Names}\label{use-descriptive-names}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# ✅ GOOD: Clear business meaning (SCREAMING\_SNAKE\_CASE, singular)}
\NormalTok{Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_SUPPLIER"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"SUPPLIER\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}

\CommentTok{\# ❌ BAD: Vague or technical names}
\NormalTok{Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"ENTITY1"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"TBL\_KEY"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"K1"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"K2"}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{document-business-context}{%
\subsection{2. Document Business
Context}\label{document-business-context}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Entity(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"HOUSEHOLD"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"HOUSEHOLD\_ID"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Group of users sharing the same billing address. Used for household{-}level targeting and fraud detection."}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{consistent-key-naming}{%
\subsection{3. Consistent Key Naming}\label{consistent-key-naming}}

Use the same column names across tables:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# ✅ GOOD: Consistent USER\_ID everywhere}
\NormalTok{Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\CommentTok{\# FeatureView source: SELECT USER\_ID, ... FROM ...}
\CommentTok{\# Spine: SELECT USER\_ID, ...}

\CommentTok{\# ❌ BAD: Inconsistent naming for the same logical user}
\CommentTok{\# Table A: USER\_ID, Table B: USER\_KEY, Table C: USR\_ID}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-1}{%
\section{Common Pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-1}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-key-column-mismatch}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: Key Column
Mismatch}\label{pitfall-1-key-column-mismatch}}

\textbf{Problem}: Join key column missing from FeatureView or spine.

\textbf{Solution}: Ensure join key columns exist in all relevant
DataFrames.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-wrong-granularity}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Wrong
Granularity}\label{pitfall-2-wrong-granularity}}

\textbf{Problem}: Entity doesn't match feature computation granularity.

\textbf{Solution}: Ensure FeatureView aggregates to entity grain.

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-missing-hierarchy-links}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: Missing Hierarchy
Links}\label{pitfall-3-missing-hierarchy-links}}

\textbf{Problem}: Can't combine features from different hierarchy
levels.

\textbf{Solution}: Include all necessary foreign keys in spine.

\hypertarget{pitfall-4-entity-grain-vs.-query-time-timestamps}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 4: Entity grain vs.~query-time
timestamps}\label{pitfall-4-entity-grain-vs.-query-time-timestamps}}

\textbf{Problem}: Features that must be computed from the \textbf{spine
timestamp} (for example age or tenure as of each training row) cannot
rely on columns that are not in the FeatureView's \texttt{feature\_df}.
The spine timestamp is not injected into FeatureView SQL for you.

\textbf{Solution}: Use an entity grain where the reference time is
already a column in the feature data (for example snapshot rows with
\texttt{SNAPSHOT\_TS} as \texttt{timestamp\_col}), or enrich after
retrieval with the same logic for training and scoring. Event-level
entities (one row per application, session, etc.) can anchor features to
an intrinsic event time. See internal customer notes on SCD2 and
point-in-time--correct derived attributes for a worked banking example.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-2}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-2}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3000}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3667}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3333}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Pattern
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Join Keys
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Use Case
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Simple} & Single column & Standard domain entities \\
\textbf{Compound} & Multiple columns & Many-to-many, intersections \\
\textbf{Hierarchical} & Cascading relationships & Multi-level
aggregations \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{next-steps-3}{%
\section{Next Steps}\label{next-steps-3}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{feature-views}{Chapter 04: Feature Views}
to learn about FeatureView types, versioning, and lifecycle management.

\hypertarget{feature-views}{%
\chapter{Feature Views}\label{feature-views}}

Dynamic Tables vs Views, refresh\_freq modes, versioning, and lifecycle

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-4}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-4}}

A FeatureView is a collection of related features computed from source
data. It defines how features are transformed, stored, and served. This
chapter uses the clickstream sample model
(\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA}: \texttt{VISITORS},
\texttt{USERS}, \texttt{HOUSEHOLDS}, \texttt{PRODUCTS},
\texttt{CATEGORIES}, \texttt{SUPPLIERS}, \texttt{PRODUCT\_SUPPLIER},
\texttt{EVENTS}, \texttt{SESSIONS}, \texttt{ORDERS},
\texttt{ORDER\_ITEMS}) and Feature Store objects in
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE}, warehouse
\texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}.

The \textbf{\texttt{refresh\_freq}} parameter determines whether a
FeatureView is backed by a \textbf{View} (query-time) or a
\textbf{Dynamic Table} (materialized), and whether refresh follows
\textbf{TARGET\_LAG} or a \textbf{CRON-driven Task}.

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-3}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-3}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Interpret the three \texttt{refresh\_freq} behaviors: omitted /
  \texttt{None}, time period, and CRON
\item
  Choose between Dynamic Table and View-based FeatureViews for a
  workload
\item
  Implement versioning strategies (V01, V02, \ldots) for safe updates
\item
  Apply schema-evolution rules: add versions for new features, deprecate
  without breaking consumers, never change a registered FeatureView in
  place
\item
  Manage FeatureView lifecycle (create, register new versions,
  deprecate, remove)
\item
  Configure refresh strategies for freshness vs.~cost
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-refresh-freq-modes}{%
\section{\texorpdfstring{How \texttt{refresh\_freq} Controls
Materialization}{How refresh\_freq Controls Materialization}}\label{sec-refresh-freq-modes}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3810}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3810}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2381}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
\texttt{refresh\_freq}
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Backing object
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Behavior
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{\texttt{None}} (default) or omitted & \textbf{View} & Features
computed at query time; always reflects current source data; no Dynamic
Table storage \\
\textbf{Time period} (e.g.~\texttt{"1\ hour"}, \texttt{"15\ minutes"}) &
\textbf{Dynamic Table} & Materialized result; refresh driven by
\textbf{TARGET\_LAG} for that period \\
\textbf{CRON expression} (e.g.~\texttt{"0\ 8\ *\ *\ *"}) &
\textbf{Dynamic Table + Task} & Dynamic Table is created and receives an
\textbf{initial full refresh}, then is \textbf{suspended} for ongoing
lag-based refresh; a \textbf{Task} runs the refresh on the CRON
schedule \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{CRON vs period strings}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

Snowflake distinguishes a \textbf{schedule string} (CRON) from a
\textbf{time period} (lag). If the value parses as CRON, the platform
uses the Dynamic Table + Task pattern described above---not continuous
TARGET\_LAG refresh.

\end{tcolorbox}

\hypertarget{view-based-featureview-refresh_freq-none}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{View-based FeatureView
(\texttt{refresh\_freq\ =\ None})}{View-based FeatureView (refresh\_freq = None)}}\label{view-based-featureview-refresh_freq-none}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/dynamic_table_fv.py}{\texttt{\_code/dynamic\_table\_fv.py}}
--- \texttt{create\_view\_featureview}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ FeatureView, Entity}

\CommentTok{\# View{-}based: refresh\_freq=None (or omit; default is None)}
\NormalTok{product\_catalog\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_CATALOG\_FV"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[product\_entity],  }\CommentTok{\# PRODUCT entity (e.g. key PRODUCT\_ID)}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session.table(}\StringTok{"FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.PRODUCTS"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"UPDATED\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{None}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"PRODUCT attributes from CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.PRODUCTS — query{-}time View"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\textbf{Characteristics}:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Computed on each query
\item
  No materialization lag from a Dynamic Table refresh cycle (subject to
  source freshness)
\item
  No Dynamic Table storage for the FeatureView output
\item
  Query-time compute cost scales with read volume
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{dynamic-table-featureview-time-period}{%
\subsection{Dynamic Table FeatureView (time
period)}\label{dynamic-table-featureview-time-period}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/dynamic_table_fv.py}{\texttt{\_code/dynamic\_table\_fv.py}}
--- \texttt{create\_dt\_featureview}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ FeatureView, Entity}

\CommentTok{\# Aggregates from ORDERS; use TOTAL\_AMT, \_CNT, \_AVG, \_TS naming}
\NormalTok{user\_order\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        SUM(TOTAL\_AMT) AS ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM,}
\StringTok{        COUNT(ORDER\_ID) AS ORDER\_CNT,}
\StringTok{        AVG(TOTAL\_AMT) AS ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_AVG,}
\StringTok{        MAX(ORDER\_TS) AS LAST\_ORDER\_TS}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS}
\StringTok{    GROUP BY USER\_ID}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{user\_order\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],  }\CommentTok{\# USER entity (e.g. key USER\_ID)}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_order\_df,}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Dynamic Table with TARGET\_LAG}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER order behavior from CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\textbf{Characteristics}:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Pre-computed and stored in a Dynamic Table
\item
  Refreshes on a lag target derived from the period string
\item
  Strong fit for high read volume and predictable freshness needs
\item
  Ongoing compute cost for refreshes
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{dynamic-table-task-cron}{%
\subsection{Dynamic Table + Task (CRON)}\label{dynamic-table-task-cron}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/dynamic_table_fv.py}{\texttt{\_code/dynamic\_table\_fv.py}}
--- \texttt{create\_cron\_featureview}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Same feature\_df as above; CRON schedule for batch{-}aligned refresh (e.g. daily 08:00)}
\NormalTok{user\_order\_fv\_cron }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_order\_df,}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"0 8 * * *"}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# CRON: DT initial refresh, then suspended; Task on schedule}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER order features — scheduled batch refresh"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\textbf{Characteristics}:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Use when features should refresh on a \textbf{calendar schedule}
  rather than continuous lag
\item
  Operational model: initial DT build, then \textbf{Task-owned}
  refreshes per CRON
\item
  Document the schedule and timezone expectations for consumers
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{choosing-between-modes}{%
\subsection{Choosing Between Modes}\label{choosing-between-modes}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1026}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2051}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3205}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3718}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Factor
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
View (\texttt{None})
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Dynamic Table (period)
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Dynamic Table + Task (CRON)
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Query frequency} & Lower or sporadic & High & High (after batch
landing) \\
\textbf{Freshness} & As-of query time & Lag-bound (e.g.~≤ 1 hour) & Next
scheduled run \\
\textbf{Cost shape} & Pay per query & Pay for refresh + storage & Pay
for scheduled runs \\
\textbf{Orchestration} & Optional external prep of sources & Native lag
refresh & Native Task schedule \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-versioning}{%
\section{Versioning Strategies}\label{sec-versioning}}

FeatureView versions enable safe updates and rollbacks.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-important-color}{\faExclamation}\hspace{0.5em}{Key insight}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-important-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-important-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

Versioning happens at the \textbf{FeatureView level}, not per individual
feature. A FeatureView version is an immutable bundle of features and
definitions.

\end{tcolorbox}

\hypertarget{recommended-version-naming-1}{%
\subsection{Recommended Version
Naming}\label{recommended-version-naming-1}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/versioning.py}{\texttt{\_code/versioning.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Zero{-}padded sequential versions (recommended for production)}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V02"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V10"}\NormalTok{)  }\CommentTok{\# Sorts correctly lexicographically}

\CommentTok{\# Environment{-}prefixed variants (optional)}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"DEV\_V01"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"PROD\_V03"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Prefer \textbf{V01}, \textbf{V02}, \ldots{} for operational clarity and
sorting. Other schemes (semantic versions, date stamps) are possible but
should be agreed team-wide.

\hypertarget{sec-schema-evolution}{%
\subsection{Schema Evolution and
Deprecation}\label{sec-schema-evolution}}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-warning-color}{\faExclamationTriangle}\hspace{0.5em}{Breaking changes require a new version}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-warning-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-warning-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

\textbf{Do not} alter a registered FeatureView in place (same name +
version) when semantics change. Register a \textbf{new version} (or a
new FeatureView name) instead.

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5200}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4800}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Change type
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
What to do
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Adding new features} & Create and register a \textbf{new
version} (e.g.~\textbf{V02}) that includes the new columns; keep
\textbf{V01} until consumers opt in. \\
\textbf{Deprecating features} & Leave the old version
\textbf{registered} and documented as deprecated; remove columns only in
a \textbf{new} version so existing training and serving jobs keep
working. \\
\textbf{Breaking changes} (rename column, change type or meaning, change
entity keys, change \texttt{timestamp\_col} semantics) & Always ship a
\textbf{new version} (or new FeatureView name). Never overwrite
\textbf{V01} with incompatible definitions. \\
\textbf{Consumers} & Point new pipelines to \textbf{V02}; migrate models
and batch jobs on your timeline; retire \textbf{V01} only after usage
drops to zero. \\
\end{longtable}

Workflow summary:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{V01} --- current production bundle.
\item
  \textbf{V02} --- add columns or fix logic; train new models against
  \textbf{V02}.
\item
  Deprecate \textbf{V01} in docs and catalog; delete \textbf{V01} only
  when no remaining dependencies.
\end{enumerate}

\hypertarget{version-lifecycle}{%
\subsection{Version Lifecycle}\label{version-lifecycle}}

\begin{verbatim}
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    FEATUREVIEW VERSION LIFECYCLE                        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                         │
│  V01 (Initial)         V02 (Update)          V03 (Current)              │
│  ┌──────────────────┐  ┌──────────────────┐  ┌──────────────────┐   │
│  │ORDER_TOTAL_AMT_SUM│  │ORDER_TOTAL_AMT_SUM│  │ORDER_TOTAL_AMT_SUM│   │
│  │ ORDER_CNT         │  │ ORDER_CNT         │  │ ORDER_CNT         │   │
│  │                   │  │ORDER_TOTAL_AMT_AVG│  │ORDER_TOTAL_AMT_AVG│   │
│  │                   │  │                   │  │ ORDERS_7D_CNT     │   │
│  └──────────────────┘  └──────────────────┘  └──────────────────┘   │
│                                                                         │
│  Status: DEPRECATED    Status: ACTIVE      Status: ACTIVE               │
│  Models: legacy_v1     Models: prod_v2     Models: new_models           │
│                                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{managing-versions}{%
\subsection{Managing Versions}\label{managing-versions}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# List all versions of a FeatureView}
\NormalTok{versions }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.list\_feature\_views(feature\_view\_name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Get a specific version}
\NormalTok{v2\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.get\_feature\_view(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}\NormalTok{, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V02"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Delete an old version only after all consumers have migrated}
\NormalTok{fs.delete\_feature\_view(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}\NormalTok{, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-refresh}{%
\section{Refresh Configuration}\label{sec-refresh}}

\hypertarget{refresh-frequency-examples-time-period-mode}{%
\subsection{Refresh Frequency Examples (time-period
mode)}\label{refresh-frequency-examples-time-period-mode}}

When using a \textbf{period} string (not CRON), you are configuring
\textbf{TARGET\_LAG}-style refresh for the backing Dynamic Table.

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Frequency & Example use case & Cost impact \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{1\ minute} & Tight operational or fraud signals & Very high \\
\texttt{15\ minutes} & Operational dashboards & High \\
\texttt{1\ hour} & Standard batch ML features & Medium \\
\texttt{1\ day} & Daily analytics features & Low \\
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{best-practices-for-refresh}{%
\subsection{Best Practices for
Refresh}\label{best-practices-for-refresh}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Align period with how often upstream CLICKSTREAM\_DATA tables land meaningful deltas}
\NormalTok{fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"4 hours"}\NormalTok{,}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# For Online Feature Tables, OFT sync frequency should be \textless{}= FeatureView refresh cadence}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{featureview-ownership-slas}{%
\section{FeatureView Ownership \&
SLAs}\label{featureview-ownership-slas}}

Define clear ownership for production FeatureViews:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# feature\_manifest.yaml}
\FunctionTok{feature\_views}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{  }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ }\FunctionTok{name}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ USER\_ORDER\_FV}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{version}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ V03}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{owner}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ ml{-}platform@company.com}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{team}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ ML Platform}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{source\_database}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{source\_schema}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ CLICKSTREAM\_DATA}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{source\_tables}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ ORDERS}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{warehouse}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ FS\_DEV\_WH}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{sla}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{      }\FunctionTok{refresh\_frequency}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\StringTok{"1 hour"}
\AttributeTok{      }\FunctionTok{max\_latency\_minutes}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\DecValTok{90}
\AttributeTok{      }\FunctionTok{availability}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\StringTok{"99.9\%"}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{consumers}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ churn{-}model{-}v2}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ ltv{-}model{-}v1}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-2}{%
\section{Best Practices}\label{best-practices-2}}

\hypertarget{use-consistent-naming}{%
\subsection{1. Use Consistent Naming}\label{use-consistent-naming}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Pattern: \textless{}ENTITY\textgreater{}\_\textless{}DOMAIN\textgreater{}\_FV (SCREAMING\_SNAKE\_CASE)}
\CommentTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}
\CommentTok{"PRODUCT\_CATALOG\_FV"}
\CommentTok{"SESSION\_ENGAGEMENT\_FV"}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Entity keys and table names should stay \textbf{singular}
SCREAMING\_SNAKE\_CASE where applicable (\texttt{USER},
\texttt{PRODUCT}, \ldots). Prefer aggregate suffixes
\textbf{\texttt{\_CNT}}, \textbf{\texttt{\_SUM}},
\textbf{\texttt{\_AVG}}, \textbf{\texttt{\_TS}}, boolean prefixes
\textbf{\texttt{IS\_}}, and monetary columns like
\textbf{\texttt{TOTAL\_AMT}} (not \texttt{AMOUNT}).

\hypertarget{document-feature-definitions}{%
\subsection{2. Document Feature
Definitions}\label{document-feature-definitions}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    USER{-}level order features from CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS for propensity models.}

\StringTok{    Features:}
\StringTok{    {-} ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM: Sum of TOTAL\_AMT across orders}
\StringTok{    {-} ORDER\_CNT: Count of orders}
\StringTok{    {-} ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_AVG: Average order TOTAL\_AMT}
\StringTok{    {-} LAST\_ORDER\_TS: Latest ORDER\_TS (point{-}in{-}time column)}

\StringTok{    SLA: Refreshed hourly (TARGET\_LAG), max 90 min lag}
\StringTok{    Owner: ml{-}platform@company.com}
\StringTok{    """}\NormalTok{,}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{version-on-any-consumer-visible-change}{%
\subsection{3. Version on Any Consumer-Visible
Change}\label{version-on-any-consumer-visible-change}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# V01: Initial column set}
\CommentTok{\# V02: Added ORDERS\_7D\_CNT}
\CommentTok{\# V03: Changed aggregation logic (breaking) — new version, never in{-}place edit}

\CommentTok{\# Increment version when you:}
\CommentTok{\# {-} Add or remove features}
\CommentTok{\# {-} Change calculations or filters}
\CommentTok{\# {-} Change entity keys or timestamp semantics}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-2}{%
\section{Common Pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-2}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-no-versioning}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: No Versioning}\label{pitfall-1-no-versioning}}

\textbf{Problem}: Registering changes under the same version breaks
dependent models.

\textbf{Solution}: Always register \textbf{new versions} (V02, V03,
\ldots) for consumer-visible changes.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-modifying-a-registered-featureview-in-place}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Modifying a Registered FeatureView In
Place}\label{pitfall-2-modifying-a-registered-featureview-in-place}}

\textbf{Problem}: Overwriting definitions for an existing name/version
breaks replay and training reproducibility.

\textbf{Solution}: Treat each registered version as \textbf{immutable};
publish a new version instead.

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-over-refreshing}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3:
Over-Refreshing}\label{pitfall-3-over-refreshing}}

\textbf{Problem}: Refreshing faster than \texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA} (or
other sources) actually updates.

\textbf{Solution}: Match refresh period or CRON schedule to upstream
load frequency.

\hypertarget{pitfall-4-no-documentation}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 4: No
Documentation}\label{pitfall-4-no-documentation}}

\textbf{Problem}: Teams cannot trust or reuse features.

\textbf{Solution}: Use the \texttt{desc} parameter and keep a feature
catalog in sync with \textbf{V01}, \textbf{V02}, \ldots{}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-3}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-3}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4091}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5909}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Concept
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{View FeatureView} & \texttt{refresh\_freq=None} (default):
query-time computation \\
\textbf{Dynamic Table (period)} & \texttt{refresh\_freq="1\ hour"}
(etc.): materialized; TARGET\_LAG refresh \\
\textbf{Dynamic Table + Task (CRON)} &
\texttt{refresh\_freq="0\ 8\ *\ *\ *"}: initial DT refresh, then Task on
schedule \\
\textbf{Version (V01, V02, \ldots)} & Immutable snapshot of feature
definitions per registration \\
\textbf{Schema evolution} & New features and breaking changes → new
version; deprecate old versions gradually \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{next-steps-4}{%
\section{Next Steps}\label{next-steps-4}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{feature-pipelines}{Chapter 05: Feature
Pipelines} to learn about pipeline architectures and orchestration
patterns.

\part{Feature Engineering}

\hypertarget{feature-pipelines}{%
\chapter{Feature Pipelines}\label{feature-pipelines}}

External orchestration, Dynamic Tables, and Temporal Aggregation API

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-5}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-5}}

Feature pipelines are the workflows that transform raw data into
features ready for ML consumption. They are the ``plumbing'' that
connects your source data to your Feature Store. Snowflake supports
multiple pipeline architectures, each with distinct trade-offs for
freshness, cost, complexity, and flexibility.

This chapter covers three primary approaches:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{External Orchestration} - DBT, Airflow, or other tools
  managing transformations
\item
  \textbf{Internal Management} - Dynamic Table-based pipelines fully
  managed by Snowflake
\item
  \textbf{Temporal Aggregation API} - The new Feature class for
  time-windowed features with tiling
\end{enumerate}

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-4}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-4}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Choose the right pipeline architecture for your requirements
\item
  Implement DBT-managed feature pipelines with View-based FeatureViews
\item
  Build internally-managed pipelines using Dynamic Tables
\item
  Configure refresh strategies for optimal freshness vs.~cost
\item
  Understand when to use the Temporal Aggregation API
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{pipeline-architecture-patterns}{%
\section{Pipeline Architecture
Patterns}\label{pipeline-architecture-patterns}}

\hypertarget{the-feature-pipeline-landscape}{%
\subsection{The Feature Pipeline
Landscape}\label{the-feature-pipeline-landscape}}

\begin{verbatim}
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                     FEATURE PIPELINE ARCHITECTURES                         │
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                    EXTERNAL ORCHESTRATION                           │   │
│  │                                                                     │   │
│  │  ┌──────────┐    ┌──────────┐    ┌──────────┐    ┌──────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │  Source  │───▶│   DBT    │───▶│  Tables/ │───▶│ View-based   │   │   │
│  │  │  Tables  │    │  Models  │    │  Views   │    │ FeatureView  │   │   │
│  │  └──────────┘    └──────────┘    └──────────┘    └──────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                     │   │
│  │  Orchestrated by: DBT Cloud, Airflow, Dagster, Prefect              │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                    INTERNAL MANAGEMENT                              │   │
│  │                                                                     │   │
│  │  ┌──────────┐              ┌──────────────────────────────────────┐ │   │
│  │  │  Source  │─────────────▶│    Dynamic Table-based FeatureView   │ │   │
│  │  │  Tables  │              │    (transformation + storage)        │ │   │
│  │  └──────────┘              └──────────────────────────────────────┘ │   │
│  │                                                                     │   │
│  │  Managed by: Snowflake (automatic refresh, incremental compute)     │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                            │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │                    TEMPORAL AGGREGATION API                         │   │
│  │                                                                     │   │
│  │  ┌──────────┐    ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │   │
│  │  │  Source  │───▶│  Tiled FeatureView with Feature aggregations │   │   │
│  │  │  Tables  │    │  (automatic window computation + tiling)     │   │   │
│  │  └──────────┘    └──────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │   │
│  │                                                                     │   │
│  │  Managed by: Snowflake (optimized temporal aggregation engine)      │   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                            │
└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{architecture-comparison}{%
\subsection{Architecture Comparison}\label{architecture-comparison}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1096}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3288}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3699}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1918}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Aspect
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
External (DBT/Airflow)
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Internal (Dynamic Tables)
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Temporal API
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Orchestration} & External tool & Snowflake managed & Snowflake
managed \\
\textbf{FeatureView Type} & View-based & DT-based & DT-based (tiled) \\
\textbf{Refresh Trigger} & Scheduled jobs & \texttt{refresh\_freq} &
\texttt{refresh\_freq} \\
\textbf{Typical Freshness} & Minutes to hours & Seconds to minutes &
Configurable \\
\textbf{Operational Complexity} & Higher & Lower & Lowest \\
\textbf{Cost Model} & Job-based compute & Continuous compute &
Continuous compute \\
\textbf{Best For} & Existing DBT shops & New implementations &
Time-windowed features \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-dbt}{%
\section{External Orchestration (DBT/Airflow)}\label{sec-dbt}}

\hypertarget{when-to-use-external-orchestration}{%
\subsection{When to Use External
Orchestration}\label{when-to-use-external-orchestration}}

External orchestration is ideal when you:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Have an existing DBT or Airflow investment
\item
  Need complex multi-step transformations
\item
  Want full control over scheduling and dependencies
\item
  Require transformations beyond SQL (Python, Spark)
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{dbt-implementation-pattern}{%
\subsection{DBT Implementation
Pattern}\label{dbt-implementation-pattern}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/dbt_pattern.py}{\texttt{\_code/dbt\_pattern.py}}
\end{quote}

\hypertarget{step-1-create-dbt-feature-models}{%
\subsubsection{Step 1: Create DBT Feature
Models}\label{step-1-create-dbt-feature-models}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} models/features/user\_purchase\_features.sql}
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Source: FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS (ORDER\_TS, TOTAL\_AMT, USER\_ID, ORDER\_ID)}
\NormalTok{\{\{ config(}
    \KeywordTok{materialized}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}table\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
    \KeywordTok{schema}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    tags}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}feature\_store\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}user\_features\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{) \}\}}

\KeywordTok{WITH}\NormalTok{ order\_stats }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ (}
    \KeywordTok{SELECT} 
\NormalTok{        USER\_ID,}
        \FunctionTok{COUNT}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{DISTINCT}\NormalTok{ ORDER\_ID) }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ ORDER\_CNT,}
        \FunctionTok{SUM}\NormalTok{(TOTAL\_AMT) }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ SPEND\_SUM,}
        \FunctionTok{AVG}\NormalTok{(TOTAL\_AMT) }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ AVG\_ORDER\_AMT,}
        \FunctionTok{MAX}\NormalTok{(ORDER\_TS) }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ LAST\_ORDER\_TS}
    \KeywordTok{FROM}\NormalTok{ \{\{ }\FunctionTok{ref}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}stg\_orders\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{) \}\}}
    \KeywordTok{GROUP} \KeywordTok{BY}\NormalTok{ USER\_ID}
\NormalTok{)}

\KeywordTok{SELECT} \OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{,}
    \FunctionTok{CURRENT\_TIMESTAMP}\NormalTok{() }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ \_DBT\_UPDATED\_TS}
\KeywordTok{FROM}\NormalTok{ order\_stats}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{step-2-register-as-view-based-featureview}{%
\subsubsection{Step 2: Register as View-Based
FeatureView}\label{step-2-register-as-view-based-featureview}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ FeatureStore, FeatureView, Entity}

\CommentTok{\# Reference the DBT{-}created table as a View{-}based FeatureView}
\NormalTok{user\_features\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.table(}
    \StringTok{"FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE.USER\_PURCHASE\_FEATURES"}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{user\_purchase\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_PURCHASE\_FEATURES"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_features\_df,}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"\_DBT\_UPDATED\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
    \CommentTok{\# refresh\_freq omitted / None → View{-}based FeatureView (DBT handles refresh)}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"User purchase features {-} managed by DBT"}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(feature\_view}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_purchase\_fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Field Tip}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

You can use Feature Store to assemble datasets, then export to external
environments. The \texttt{snowflake-ml-python} package can be installed
externally to simplify data retrieval.

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-dynamic-tables}{%
\section{Internal Management (Dynamic
Tables)}\label{sec-dynamic-tables}}

\hypertarget{when-to-use-dynamic-tables}{%
\subsection{When to Use Dynamic
Tables}\label{when-to-use-dynamic-tables}}

Dynamic Tables are ideal when you:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Want Snowflake to manage the entire pipeline
\item
  Need low-latency feature freshness (seconds to minutes)
\item
  Prefer declarative over imperative pipeline definition
\item
  Are building new feature pipelines from scratch
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{dynamic-table-implementation}{%
\subsection{Dynamic Table
Implementation}\label{dynamic-table-implementation}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/dynamic_table_pattern.py}{\texttt{\_code/dynamic\_table\_pattern.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ FeatureStore, FeatureView, Entity}

\CommentTok{\# CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS: ORDER\_TS, TOTAL\_AMT, USER\_ID, ORDER\_ID}
\NormalTok{user\_purchase\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT }
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        COUNT(DISTINCT ORDER\_ID) AS ORDER\_CNT,}
\StringTok{        SUM(TOTAL\_AMT) AS SPEND\_SUM,}
\StringTok{        AVG(TOTAL\_AMT) AS AVG\_ORDER\_AMT,}
\StringTok{        MAX(ORDER\_TS) AS LAST\_ORDER\_TS}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS}
\StringTok{    GROUP BY USER\_ID}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Create Dynamic Table{-}backed FeatureView}
\NormalTok{user\_purchase\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
