\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_PURCHASE\_STATS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_purchase\_df,}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"15 minutes"}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Dynamic Table with TARGET\_LAG}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"User purchase statistics {-} auto{-}refreshed"}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Register and wait for initial materialization}
\NormalTok{registered\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.register\_feature\_view(}
\NormalTok{    feature\_view}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_purchase\_fv,}
\NormalTok{    version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    block}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{how-refresh_freq-selects-the-backing-object}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{How \texttt{refresh\_freq} Selects the
Backing
Object}{How refresh\_freq Selects the Backing Object}}\label{how-refresh_freq-selects-the-backing-object}}

\texttt{refresh\_freq} on \texttt{FeatureView} determines whether
Snowflake builds a \textbf{view} or a \textbf{Dynamic Table}, and how
refresh is scheduled:

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1875}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5000}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3125}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Mode
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
\texttt{refresh\_freq}
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Behavior
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{View-based FeatureView} & \texttt{None} or omitted & No Dynamic
Table. The \texttt{feature\_df} is registered as a view; \textbf{you}
refresh upstream tables (DBT, Airflow, manual loads). \\
\textbf{Dynamic Table (lag)} & Time period (e.g.~\texttt{"1\ hour"},
\texttt{"15\ minutes"}) & Snowflake creates a Dynamic Table with
\textbf{TARGET\_LAG} matching that interval. \\
\textbf{Dynamic Table (scheduled)} & CRON expression
(e.g.~\texttt{"0\ 8\ *\ *\ *"}) & Dynamic Table refresh driven by a
\textbf{Task} (or equivalent schedule) for fixed clock-time runs. \\
\end{longtable}

For tiled temporal features, you still pass \texttt{timestamp\_col},
\texttt{feature\_granularity}, and \texttt{features};
\texttt{refresh\_freq} follows the same idea (lag vs schedule) for how
often tiles are updated.

\hypertarget{refresh-configuration-options-lag-based-dynamic-tables}{%
\subsection{Refresh Configuration Options (lag-based Dynamic
Tables)}\label{refresh-configuration-options-lag-based-dynamic-tables}}

When using a \textbf{time period} for \texttt{refresh\_freq}, typical
choices balance freshness and cost:

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Refresh Freq & Use Case & Cost Impact \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{1\ minute} & Near real-time, critical features & High \\
\texttt{15\ minutes} & Standard operational & Medium \\
\texttt{1\ hour} & Balanced freshness/cost & Low \\
\texttt{1\ day} & Slowly-changing features & Minimal \\
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{monitoring-dynamic-table-refresh}{%
\subsection{Monitoring Dynamic Table
Refresh}\label{monitoring-dynamic-table-refresh}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/monitoring.sql}{\texttt{\_code/monitoring.sql}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Check refresh history}
\KeywordTok{SELECT} 
\NormalTok{    NAME,}
\NormalTok{    STATE,}
\NormalTok{    REFRESH\_START\_TIME,}
\NormalTok{    REFRESH\_END\_TIME,}
    \KeywordTok{STATISTICS}\CharTok{:numInsertedRows}\NormalTok{:}\CharTok{:INT} \KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ ROWS\_INSERTED}
\KeywordTok{FROM} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLE\_REFRESH\_HISTORY(}
\NormalTok{    NAME }\OperatorTok{=\textgreater{}} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE.USER\_PURCHASE\_STATS$V01\textquotesingle{}}
\NormalTok{))}
\KeywordTok{ORDER} \KeywordTok{BY}\NormalTok{ REFRESH\_START\_TIME }\KeywordTok{DESC}
\KeywordTok{LIMIT} \DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-temporal-api}{%
\section{Temporal Aggregation Pipelines}\label{sec-temporal-api}}

\hypertarget{when-to-use-temporal-aggregation-api}{%
\subsection{When to Use Temporal Aggregation
API}\label{when-to-use-temporal-aggregation-api}}

The Temporal Aggregation API (Feature class) is ideal when you:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Need time-windowed aggregations (7-day sum, 30-day count, etc.)
\item
  Want optimal performance through feature tiling
\item
  Have high-cardinality entities with frequent updates
\item
  Need multiple window sizes for the same base metric
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{understanding-feature-tiling}{%
\subsection{Understanding Feature
Tiling}\label{understanding-feature-tiling}}

\begin{verbatim}
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                         FEATURE TILING CONCEPT                              │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Traditional Approach (recomputes entire window each refresh):              │
│                                                                             │
│  Day 1    Day 2    Day 3    Day 4    Day 5    Day 6    Day 7                │
│  ├────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┤           │
│  │████████████████████████████████████████████████████████████│ 7-day SUM   │
│  │        Recompute ALL 7 days on each refresh                │             │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘             │
│                                                                             │
│  Tiled Approach (pre-computes tiles, combines at query time):               │
│                                                                             │
│  Day 1    Day 2    Day 3    Day 4    Day 5    Day 6    Day 7                │
│  ├────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┼────────┤           │
│  │ Tile 1 │ Tile 2 │ Tile 3 │ Tile 4 │ Tile 5 │ Tile 6 │ Tile 7 │           │
│  │  $100  │  $50   │  $75   │  $200  │  $0    │  $150  │  $80   │           │
│  └────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┴────────┘           │
│                                                                             │
│  7-day SUM = Tile1 + Tile2 + ... + Tile7 = $655                             │
│  Only refresh the latest tile(s), combine existing tiles                    │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{feature-class-api}{%
\subsection{Feature Class API}\label{feature-class-api}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/temporal_api.py}{\texttt{\_code/temporal\_api.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ Feature, FeatureView}

\CommentTok{\# Window arguments are duration strings ("7d", "30d", "24h"), not calendar dates}
\NormalTok{features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"SPEND\_SUM\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"30d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"SPEND\_SUM\_30D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_CNT\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"30d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_CNT\_30D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.avg(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"24h"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_VALUE\_AVG\_24H"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.approx\_count\_distinct(}\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"UNIQUE\_PRODUCTS\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.last\_n(}\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{, n}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"RECENT\_PRODUCTS"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{]}

\CommentTok{\# Tiled FeatureView: timestamp\_col, refresh\_freq, feature\_granularity, features}
\NormalTok{user\_temporal\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_TEMPORAL\_AGGREGATES"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session.table(}\StringTok{"FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    feature\_granularity}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{features,}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"User purchase aggregations with multiple time windows"}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{🆕 New in snowflake-ml 1.21+}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

The Feature class and tiled aggregation are new capabilities. See
\protect\hyperlink{aggregations-api}{Chapter 07: Aggregations API} for
the complete reference.

\end{tcolorbox}

\hypertarget{available-aggregation-functions}{%
\subsection{Available Aggregation
Functions}\label{available-aggregation-functions}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3125}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4062}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2812}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Function
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Example
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{Feature.sum(col,\ window)} & Sum over window &
\texttt{Feature.sum("AMOUNT",\ "7d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.count(col,\ window)} & Count over window &
\texttt{Feature.count("ORDER\_ID",\ "30d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.approx\_count\_distinct(col,\ window)} & Approximate
distinct count &
\texttt{Feature.approx\_count\_distinct("PRODUCT\_ID",\ "7d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.avg(col,\ window)} & Average over window &
\texttt{Feature.avg("AMOUNT",\ "7d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.min(col,\ window)} & Minimum over window &
\texttt{Feature.min("AMOUNT",\ "30d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.max(col,\ window)} & Maximum over window &
\texttt{Feature.max("AMOUNT",\ "30d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.last\_n(col,\ window,\ n)} & Last N values &
\texttt{Feature.last\_n("PRODUCT\_ID",\ "7d",\ n=5)} \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-selection}{%
\section{Pipeline Selection Framework}\label{sec-selection}}

\hypertarget{decision-tree}{%
\subsection{Decision Tree}\label{decision-tree}}

\begin{verbatim}
What is your primary requirement?
│
├── Already have DBT/Airflow infrastructure?
│   ├── YES → Do you need sub-hour freshness?
│   │         ├── YES → Consider migrating critical features to DT
│   │         └── NO  → External Orchestration (keep DBT)
│   │
│   └── NO  → Are features time-windowed aggregations?
│             ├── YES → Temporal Aggregation API
│             └── NO  → Internal Management (Dynamic Tables)
│
└── Need real-time features (<1 min latency)?
    ├── YES → Dynamic Tables + Online Feature Tables
    └── NO  → Any approach works, optimize for cost
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{selection-matrix}{%
\subsection{Selection Matrix}\label{selection-matrix}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Requirement & Recommended Approach \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Existing DBT investment & External Orchestration \\
Minimal operational overhead & Internal (Dynamic Tables) \\
Time-windowed aggregations & Temporal Aggregation API \\
Sub-minute freshness & Dynamic Tables (short refresh) \\
Complex multi-step transforms & External Orchestration \\
New Feature Store implementation & Internal (Dynamic Tables) \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-3}{%
\section{Best Practices}\label{best-practices-3}}

\hypertarget{match-refresh-to-source-update-frequency}{%
\subsection{1. Match Refresh to Source Update
Frequency}\label{match-refresh-to-source-update-frequency}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# GOOD: Source updates hourly, refresh hourly}
\NormalTok{hourly\_source\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"HOURLY\_FEATURES"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# WASTEFUL: Source updates daily, refreshing every 5 minutes}
\NormalTok{wasteful\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"DAILY\_FEATURES"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"5 minutes"}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Unnecessary compute!}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{use-appropriate-tile-sizes}{%
\subsection{2. Use Appropriate Tile
Sizes}\label{use-appropriate-tile-sizes}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# High{-}frequency events: smaller tiles}
\NormalTok{clickstream\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    feature\_granularity}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Fine{-}grained}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Daily batch data: larger tiles}
\NormalTok{daily\_batch\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    feature\_granularity}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 day"}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Coarse{-}grained}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{pipeline-ownership-slas}{%
\subsection{3. Pipeline Ownership \&
SLAs}\label{pipeline-ownership-slas}}

Define clear ownership for each pipeline:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# feature\_manifest.yaml}
\FunctionTok{feature\_views}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{  }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ }\FunctionTok{name}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ USER\_TEMPORAL\_AGGREGATES}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{pattern}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\StringTok{"Temporal API"}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{version}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\StringTok{"V01"}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{refresh}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\StringTok{"1 hour"}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{owner}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ ml{-}platform@company.com}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{sla}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{      }\FunctionTok{max\_latency\_minutes}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\DecValTok{90}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{pipeline-health-monitoring}{%
\subsection{4. Pipeline Health
Monitoring}\label{pipeline-health-monitoring}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Create alerting for stale features}
\KeywordTok{CREATE}\NormalTok{ ALERT feature\_staleness\_alert}
\NormalTok{  WAREHOUSE }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FS\_DEV\_WH}
\NormalTok{  SCHEDULE }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}USING CRON 0 * * * * UTC\textquotesingle{}}
  \ControlFlowTok{IF}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{EXISTS}\NormalTok{ (}
    \KeywordTok{SELECT} \OperatorTok{*} 
    \KeywordTok{FROM} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLES())}
    \KeywordTok{WHERE}\NormalTok{ SCHEMA\_NAME }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\textquotesingle{}}
      \KeywordTok{AND}\NormalTok{ TIMESTAMPDIFF(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}minute\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, DATA\_TIMESTAMP, }\FunctionTok{CURRENT\_TIMESTAMP}\NormalTok{()) }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}} \DecValTok{60}
\NormalTok{  ))}
  \ControlFlowTok{THEN}
    \KeywordTok{CALL}\NormalTok{ SYSTEM$SEND\_EMAIL(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}ml{-}alerts@company.com\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Stale Features\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Alert\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{);}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-3}{%
\section{Common Pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-3}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-over-engineering-simple-features}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: Over-Engineering Simple
Features}\label{pitfall-1-over-engineering-simple-features}}

\textbf{Problem}: Using complex pipeline for simple lookups.

\textbf{Solution}: Use View-based FeatureView directly on source for
static data.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-ignoring-incremental-refresh-compatibility}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Ignoring Incremental Refresh
Compatibility}\label{pitfall-2-ignoring-incremental-refresh-compatibility}}

\textbf{Problem}: Using SQL patterns that prevent incremental refresh
(e.g., \texttt{RANDOM()}, self-referential queries).

\textbf{Solution}: Use deterministic SQL compatible with DT incremental
refresh.

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-mismatched-freshness-expectations}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: Mismatched Freshness
Expectations}\label{pitfall-3-mismatched-freshness-expectations}}

\textbf{Problem}: Pipeline refresh doesn't match business SLA.

\textbf{Solution}: Align refresh frequency with business requirements.

\hypertarget{pitfall-4-no-monitoring-or-alerting}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 4: No Monitoring or
Alerting}\label{pitfall-4-no-monitoring-or-alerting}}

\textbf{Problem}: Stale features go undetected.

\textbf{Solution}: Implement monitoring and alerting for pipeline
health.

\hypertarget{pitfall-5-wrong-feature-window-syntax}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{❌ Pitfall 5: Wrong \texttt{Feature} Window
Syntax}{❌ Pitfall 5: Wrong Feature Window Syntax}}\label{pitfall-5-wrong-feature-window-syntax}}

\textbf{Problem}: The Temporal Aggregation \texttt{Feature} API does
\textbf{not} take fixed calendar dates or timestamp literals. Windows
are \textbf{relative durations} (rolling lookbacks from each entity's
event time), expressed as strings like \texttt{"7d"}, \texttt{"30d"},
\texttt{"24h"}.

\textbf{Wrong} (date literals or non-duration strings---these are not
valid window arguments):

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Do NOT pass hard{-}coded dates or arbitrary date strings as the window}
\NormalTok{Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"2024{-}01{-}01"}\NormalTok{)       }\CommentTok{\# invalid pattern}
\NormalTok{Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"2024{-}01{-}01/2024{-}01{-}31"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\textbf{Correct} (duration strings + \texttt{.alias(...)} for output
names):

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"SPEND\_SUM\_7D"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"30d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_CNT\_30D"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{Feature.avg(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"24h"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_VALUE\_AVG\_24H"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{Feature.last\_n(}\StringTok{"PRODUCT\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{, n}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"RECENT\_PRODUCTS"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\textbf{Solution}: Use only supported duration forms for the second
argument (e.g.~days/hours as shown in
\protect\hyperlink{aggregations-api}{Chapter 07: Aggregations API}), and
list tiled features under \texttt{FeatureView(...,\ features={[}...{]})}
together with \texttt{timestamp\_col}, \texttt{refresh\_freq}, and
\texttt{feature\_granularity}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-4}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-4}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3333}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2778}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2037}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1852}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Pipeline Pattern
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Orchestration
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Freshness
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Best For
\end{minipage} \\

\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{External (DBT)} & External tool & Minutes-hours & Existing DBT
shops \\

implementations \\

\hypertarget{next-steps-5}{%
\section{Next Steps}\label{next-steps-5}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{temporal-features}{Chapter 06: Temporal
Features} to learn about point-in-time correctness, ASOF joins, and
preventing data leakage.

\hypertarget{temporal-features}{%
\chapter{Temporal Features}\label{temporal-features}}

Point-in-time correctness, ASOF joins, and data leakage prevention

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-6}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-6}}

Temporal correctness is critical for ML systems. When training a model,
you must ensure features are computed using only data that would have
been available at the time of prediction. Using future data (``data
leakage'') leads to artificially good training metrics but poor
production performance.

This chapter uses the \textbf{clickstream} sample shape: source data in
database \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO}, schema
\texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA} (tables \texttt{EVENTS}, \texttt{SESSIONS},
\texttt{ORDERS}), Feature Store metadata in schema
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE}, warehouse \texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}. FeatureView
registrations use version strings in \textbf{\texttt{V01} format} (for
example \texttt{version="V01"}).

The chapter covers how Snowflake Feature Store ensures temporal
correctness through point-in-time (PIT) retrieval and ASOF joins, how to
\textbf{backfill} materialized features, and how to avoid \textbf{silent
errors} when features are \emph{derived} from timestamps that only exist
on the spine---not inside the FeatureView SQL.

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-5}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-5}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Understand why point-in-time correctness matters
\item
  Configure FeatureViews for temporal retrieval using \texttt{EVENTS} /
  \texttt{ORDERS} and \texttt{timestamp\_col}
\item
  Generate training datasets without data leakage
\item
  Debug and validate temporal correctness
\item
  Handle late-arriving data in feature pipelines
\item
  Run manual refresh / backfill for Dynamic Table-backed FeatureViews
\item
  Recognize when derived time-dependent features must be computed after
  retrieval (or via snapshot materialization)
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{why-temporal-correctness-matters}{%
\section{Why Temporal Correctness
Matters}\label{why-temporal-correctness-matters}}

\hypertarget{the-data-leakage-problem}{%
\subsection{The Data Leakage Problem}\label{the-data-leakage-problem}}

\begin{verbatim}
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                         DATA LEAKAGE PROBLEM                                │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  ❌ WITHOUT Point-in-Time Correctness:                                      │
│                                                                             │
│  Training Label:                                                            │
│  "Did user churn on Jan 15?"  ──────────────────────────┐                   │
│                                                         │                   │
│  Features Used:                                         │                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐│                   │
│  │ User's purchase history including Jan 16-31 data   ││ ← LEAKAGE!        │
│  │ (Future data used to predict past event)           ││                   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘│                   │
│                                                         │                   │
│  Result: Model learns from "future" → inflated metrics  │                   │
│                                                                             │
│  ✅ WITH Point-in-Time Correctness:                                         │
│                                                                             │
│  Training Label:                                                            │
│  "Did user churn on Jan 15?"  ──────────────────────────┐                   │
│                                                         │                   │
│  Features Used:                                         │                   │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐│                   │
│  │ User's purchase history ONLY through Jan 14        ││ ← CORRECT!        │
│  │ (Only past data available at prediction time)      ││                   │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘│                   │
│                                                         │                   │
│  Result: Model learns realistic patterns → accurate metrics                 │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{real-world-impact}{%
\subsection{Real-World Impact}\label{real-world-impact}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3030}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3939}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3030}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Scenario
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Without PIT
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
With PIT
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Training AUC} & 0.95 (looks great!) & 0.82 (realistic) \\
\textbf{Production AUC} & 0.72 (unexpected drop) & 0.80 (matches
training) \\
\textbf{Business Impact} & Model fails in production & Model performs as
expected \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{how-feature-store-ensures-pit-correctness}{%
\section{How Feature Store Ensures PIT
Correctness}\label{how-feature-store-ensures-pit-correctness}}

\hypertarget{the-spine-timestamp_col-pattern}{%
\subsection{The Spine + timestamp\_col
Pattern}\label{the-spine-timestamp_col-pattern}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/pit_retrieval.py}{\texttt{\_code/pit\_retrieval.py}}
\end{quote}

The training spine uses \textbf{\texttt{SESSIONS}}:
\texttt{SESSION\_START\_TS} is the instant you want features ``as of'';
\texttt{IS\_CONVERTED} is the label. User-level features come from
\textbf{\texttt{EVENTS}}, with \texttt{timestamp\_col} set to the latest
event time per user (\texttt{LAST\_EVENT\_TS}) so the ASOF join is
well-defined.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ FeatureStore, FeatureView, Entity}

\NormalTok{user\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{], desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Clickstream user"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# 1. FeatureView: aggregates from EVENTS; timestamp\_col = last event time (PIT axis)}
\NormalTok{user\_event\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        COUNT(EVENT\_ID) AS EVENT\_CNT,}
\StringTok{        COUNT(DISTINCT PRODUCT\_ID) AS PRODUCT\_DISTINCT\_CNT,}
\StringTok{        MAX(EVENT\_TS) AS LAST\_EVENT\_TS}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.EVENTS}
\StringTok{    GROUP BY USER\_ID}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{user\_event\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_EVENT\_STATS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_event\_df,}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_EVENT\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# 2. Register at version V01}
\NormalTok{registered\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.register\_feature\_view(}
\NormalTok{    feature\_view}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_event\_fv,}
\NormalTok{    version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    block}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# 3. Spine: entity + when + label (SESSIONS)}
\NormalTok{training\_spine }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        s.USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        s.SESSION\_START\_TS AS EVENT\_TS,}
\StringTok{        s.IS\_CONVERTED::NUMBER AS LABEL}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.SESSIONS s}
\StringTok{    WHERE s.USER\_ID IS NOT NULL}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# 4. Training set: ASOF join on EVENT\_TS}
\NormalTok{training\_set }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_dataset(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{training\_spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[registered\_fv],}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"EVENT\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{how-asof-joins-work}{%
\subsection{How ASOF Joins Work}\label{how-asof-joins-work}}

The Feature Store uses \textbf{ASOF joins} (temporal joins) to retrieve
the most recent feature row \textbf{on or before} each spine timestamp,
per entity:

\begin{verbatim}
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                           ASOF JOIN MECHANICS                               │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                             │
│  Spine (SESSIONS)                  FeatureView (from EVENTS)                 │
│  ─────────────────                 ─────────────────────────                │
│                                                                             │
│  USER_ID │ EVENT_TS               USER_ID │ LAST_EVENT_TS │ EVENT_CNT       │
│  ────────┼──────────               ────────┼─────────────┼──────────        │
│  usr_001 │ Jan 15                 usr_001 │ Jan 10      │ 42              │
│  usr_001 │ Jan 20                 usr_001 │ Jan 14      │ 58              │
│  usr_002 │ Jan 18                 usr_001 │ Jan 18      │ 71              │
│                                   usr_002 │ Jan 12      │ 9               │
│                                   usr_002 │ Jan 17      │ 22              │
│                                                                             │
│  ASOF Join Result:                                                          │
│  ─────────────────                                                          │
│                                                                             │
│  USER_ID │ EVENT_TS │ LAST_EVENT_TS │ EVENT_CNT                              │
│  ────────┼──────────┼───────────────┼──────────                              │
│  usr_001 │ Jan 15   │ Jan 14        │ 58       ← latest row before Jan 15   │
│  usr_001 │ Jan 20   │ Jan 18        │ 71       ← latest row before Jan 20   │
│  usr_002 │ Jan 18   │ Jan 17        │ 22       ← latest row before Jan 18   │
│                                                                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
\end{verbatim}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{derived-features-and-point-in-time-correctness}{%
\section{Derived features and point-in-time
correctness}\label{derived-features-and-point-in-time-correctness}}

\texttt{timestamp\_col} is used for the \textbf{ASOF join} to pick the
correct historical row. It is \textbf{not} automatically available
inside \texttt{feature\_df} as the spine's prediction time. If you need
values such as ``tenure as of the spine date'' or ``age as of
\texttt{EVENT\_TS}'', you cannot, in general, compute them only from
columns in the FeatureView definition using the spine timestamp---there
is no placeholder for the spine time in \texttt{feature\_df}.

\textbf{Risk:} Computing \texttt{DATEDIFF} relative to the wrong
reference (for example an SCD2 validity start, or
\texttt{CURRENT\_TIMESTAMP()}) \textbf{runs without error} but can be
\textbf{silently wrong} at training or at Dynamic Table refresh time.

\textbf{When computation inside the FeatureView \emph{is} PIT-correct:}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Snapshot features:} The snapshot grain (for example
  \texttt{SNAPSHOT\_TS}) is both in the row and used as
  \texttt{timestamp\_col}; derived columns computed from that same
  timestamp are consistent with the ASOF-selected row.
\item
  \textbf{Event-anchored features:} The reference time is a column on
  the event-level record (for example per \texttt{APPLICATION\_ID}), and
  the entity keys match that grain.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When logic must live outside the FeatureView (or in a denser
materialization):}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Shared enrichment after retrieval:} Store raw attributes in
  the FeatureView; after \texttt{generate\_dataset} /
  \texttt{retrieve\_feature\_values}, apply the same function for
  training and scoring using the spine's \texttt{EVENT\_TS} (or
  \texttt{AS\_OF\_DATE}) column.
\item
  \textbf{Dense snapshot FeatureView:} Materialize one row per entity
  per calendar day (or month) with derived fields precomputed for that
  date; register with \texttt{timestamp\_col} equal to that date column.
  This trades storage for keeping logic inside Snowflake and the
  standard retrieval API.
\item
  \textbf{Centralized SQL UDFs or Model Registry wrappers:} Keep
  governed, versioned logic in Snowflake or the registry, still applied
  \textbf{after} retrieval if the spine timestamp is required.
\end{itemize}

This pattern matches production lessons from large Feature Store
deployments (slow-changing dimensions and time-relative attributes).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{configuring-featureviews-for-temporal-retrieval}{%
\section{Configuring FeatureViews for Temporal
Retrieval}\label{configuring-featureviews-for-temporal-retrieval}}

\hypertarget{timestamp_col-requirements}{%
\subsection{timestamp\_col
Requirements}\label{timestamp_col-requirements}}

The \texttt{timestamp\_col} should represent when the feature
\textbf{row} is valid for ASOF selection.

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/timestamp_patterns.py}{\texttt{\_code/timestamp\_patterns.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Pattern 1: Last event time from EVENTS (common for clickstream aggregates)}
\NormalTok{user\_event\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_EVENT\_STATS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{        SELECT}
\StringTok{            USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{            COUNT(EVENT\_ID) AS EVENT\_CNT,}
\StringTok{            MAX(EVENT\_TS) AS LAST\_EVENT\_TS}
\StringTok{        FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.EVENTS}
\StringTok{        GROUP BY USER\_ID}
\StringTok{    """}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_EVENT\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Pattern 2: Order aggregates — use TOTAL\_AMT, ORDER\_TS; naming \_SUM, \_CNT, \_AVG, \_TS}
\NormalTok{user\_order\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_STATS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{        SELECT}
\StringTok{            USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{            SUM(TOTAL\_AMT) AS ORDER\_TOTAL\_SUM,}
\StringTok{            COUNT(ORDER\_TS) AS ORDER\_CNT,}
\StringTok{            AVG(TOTAL\_AMT) AS ORDER\_TOTAL\_AVG,}
\StringTok{            MAX(ORDER\_TS) AS LAST\_ORDER\_TS}
\StringTok{        FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS}
\StringTok{        GROUP BY USER\_ID}
\StringTok{    """}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Pattern 3: Periodic snapshots — timestamp\_col = snapshot grain (e.g. SNAPSHOT\_TS)}
\NormalTok{user\_snapshot\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_DAILY\_SNAPSHOT"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session.table(}\StringTok{"FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE.USER\_DAILY\_SNAPSHOT"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SNAPSHOT\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
    \CommentTok{\# refresh\_freq omitted =\textgreater{} View{-}backed, or set for Dynamic Table}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{late-arriving-data}{%
\section{Late-arriving data}\label{late-arriving-data}}

\hypertarget{the-challenge}{%
\subsection{The Challenge}\label{the-challenge}}

In real systems, data often arrives late. A click that occurred at 10:00
might only land in \texttt{EVENTS} at 10:15.

\hypertarget{solutions}{%
\subsection{Solutions}\label{solutions}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/late_data.py}{\texttt{\_code/late\_data.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Option 1: Event timestamp (business time) — timestamp\_col = EVENT\_TS on detailed rows}
\CommentTok{\# Late rows still carry the true event time; the next Dynamic Table refresh incorporates them.}

\CommentTok{\# Option 2: Processing timestamp — timestamp\_col = RECORDED\_TS when you must reflect}
\CommentTok{\# "when we knew it" rather than "when it happened" (requires that column on the source).}

\CommentTok{\# Option 3: Conservative spine — shift the ASOF cutoff earlier than the label time}
\NormalTok{conservative\_spine }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        e.USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        e.EVENT\_TS,}
\StringTok{        DATEADD(\textquotesingle{}hour\textquotesingle{}, {-}2, e.EVENT\_TS) AS FEATURE\_CUTOFF\_TS,}
\StringTok{        CASE WHEN e.EVENT\_NAME = \textquotesingle{}Order Completed\textquotesingle{} THEN 1 ELSE 0 END AS LABEL}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.EVENTS e}
\StringTok{    WHERE e.USER\_ID IS NOT NULL}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}
\CommentTok{\# Use FEATURE\_CUTOFF\_TS as spine\_timestamp\_col when generating the dataset if that}
\CommentTok{\# matches your governance rule (tradeoff: features may be slightly stale).}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\textbf{Dynamic Tables:} For materialized FeatureViews,
\textbf{late-arriving facts} are picked up on the \textbf{next refresh
cycle} (and you can \textbf{manually refresh}---see
\protect\hyperlink{backfill-operations}{Backfill operations}).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{backfill-operations}{%
\section{Backfill operations}\label{backfill-operations}}

Backfill matters when you \textbf{add new features} and need historical
rows materialized, when you fix upstream pipelines and must
\textbf{recompute} stored features, or when you want to \textbf{force} a
Dynamic Table refresh outside its schedule.

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/backfill_operations.py}{\texttt{\_code/backfill\_operations.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Manual refresh (triggers Dynamic Table refresh for registered materialized FV)}
\NormalTok{fs.refresh\_feature\_view(registered\_fv)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5238}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4762}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Situation
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Guidance
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{New features on historical data} & After deploying a new
\texttt{feature\_df}, register a new version (for example \texttt{V02})
or re-register; run \texttt{refresh\_feature\_view} (and/or wait for
\texttt{refresh\_freq}) so back periods fill in. \\
\textbf{Late-arriving data} & Usually no special backfill: the next
\textbf{scheduled} Dynamic Table refresh includes new rows. Use
\textbf{manual refresh} if you cannot wait. \\
\textbf{Bad pipeline run / logic bug} & \textbf{Drop} the broken
FeatureView version and \textbf{re-register} (same or new
\texttt{version}), or cut \textbf{\texttt{V02}} with corrected SQL;
refresh so consumers do not read stale wrong values. \\
\end{longtable}

View-backed FeatureViews (no \texttt{refresh\_freq}) compute from source
at query time---\textbf{backfill} in that case means fixing source
tables or spine SQL, not refreshing a DT.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{validating-temporal-correctness}{%
\section{Validating Temporal
Correctness}\label{validating-temporal-correctness}}

\hypertarget{data-leakage-detection}{%
\subsection{Data Leakage Detection}\label{data-leakage-detection}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/validation.py}{\texttt{\_code/validation.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.snowpark }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ functions }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ F}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ validate\_no\_data\_leakage(}
\NormalTok{    training\_df,}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col: }\BuiltInTok{str}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    feature\_timestamp\_col: }\BuiltInTok{str}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{) }\OperatorTok{{-}\textgreater{}} \BuiltInTok{dict}\NormalTok{:}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Validate that no features have timestamps after the spine timestamp.}

\CommentTok{    For clickstream examples, feature\_timestamp\_col is often LAST\_EVENT\_TS or}
\CommentTok{    LAST\_ORDER\_TS; spine\_timestamp\_col is EVENT\_TS from SESSIONS (or EVENTS).}
\CommentTok{    """}
\NormalTok{    leakage\_check }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ training\_df.}\BuiltInTok{filter}\NormalTok{(}
\NormalTok{        F.col(feature\_timestamp\_col) }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}}\NormalTok{ F.col(spine\_timestamp\_col)}
\NormalTok{    )}

\NormalTok{    leakage\_count }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ leakage\_check.count()}

    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ \{}
        \StringTok{"valid"}\NormalTok{: leakage\_count }\OperatorTok{==} \DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{,}
        \StringTok{"leakage\_count"}\NormalTok{: leakage\_count,}
        \StringTok{"total\_rows"}\NormalTok{: training\_df.count(),}
\NormalTok{    \}}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-4}{%
\section{Best Practices}\label{best-practices-4}}

\hypertarget{always-define-timestamp_col}{%
\subsection{1. Always Define
timestamp\_col}\label{always-define-timestamp_col}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# ✅ GOOD: timestamp\_col defined (EVENTS{-}driven example)}
\NormalTok{fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_EVENT\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# ❌ BAD: No timestamp\_col — PIT retrieval / ASOF semantics are not defined}
\NormalTok{fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
    \CommentTok{\# timestamp\_col missing!}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{use-meaningful-timestamps}{%
\subsection{2. Use Meaningful
Timestamps}\label{use-meaningful-timestamps}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# ✅ GOOD: Timestamp reflects feature row validity for ASOF}
\NormalTok{timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_EVENT\_TS"}   \CommentTok{\# from EVENTS}
\NormalTok{timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_ORDER\_TS"}   \CommentTok{\# from ORDERS}

\CommentTok{\# ❌ BAD: Timestamp that does not match how you want "as of" to behave}
\NormalTok{timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"ROW\_INSERTED\_TS"}  \CommentTok{\# unless ingest{-}time semantics are intentional}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{validate-before-training}{%
\subsection{3. Validate Before
Training}\label{validate-before-training}}

Always run leakage detection before training models on generated
datasets.

\hypertarget{version-featureviews-consistently}{%
\subsection{4. Version FeatureViews
consistently}\label{version-featureviews-consistently}}

Use \textbf{\texttt{V01}, \texttt{V02}, \ldots{}} when registering so
promotions and rollbacks stay explicit.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-4}{%
\section{Common Pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-4}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-missing-timestamp_col}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: Missing
timestamp\_col}\label{pitfall-1-missing-timestamp_col}}

\textbf{Problem:} Features retrieved without temporal context.

\textbf{Solution:} Always define \texttt{timestamp\_col} in FeatureViews
used for offline / historical retrieval.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-wrong-timestamp-semantics}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Wrong Timestamp
Semantics}\label{pitfall-2-wrong-timestamp-semantics}}

\textbf{Problem:} Using processing time when event time is needed (or
vice versa).

\textbf{Solution:} Align \texttt{timestamp\_col} with your governance
definition of ``as of.''

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-derived-time-features-inside-featureview-without-a-reference-column}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: Derived time features inside FeatureView
without a reference
column}\label{pitfall-3-derived-time-features-inside-featureview-without-a-reference-column}}

\textbf{Problem:} Computing ``as of spine'' deltas inside
\texttt{feature\_df} when only the spine carries that time ---
\textbf{silent wrong values}.

\textbf{Solution:} Enrich after retrieval, use snapshot/dense
materialization, or keep the reference time on the row (snapshot or
event entity).

\hypertarget{pitfall-4-not-validating}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 4: Not
Validating}\label{pitfall-4-not-validating}}

\textbf{Problem:} Data leakage goes undetected until production.

\textbf{Solution:} Implement leakage detection in your training
pipeline.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-5}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-5}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4091}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5909}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Concept
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Point-in-Time (PIT)} & Retrieve features as they existed at a
specific time \\
\textbf{timestamp\_col} & Column defining feature \textbf{row} validity
for ASOF selection \\
\textbf{ASOF Join} & Temporal join picking the latest feature row on or
before the spine timestamp \\
\textbf{Data Leakage} & Using future data to predict past events \\
\textbf{Backfill / refresh} &
\texttt{fs.refresh\_feature\_view(registered\_fv)}; new versions or
re-register after fixes \\
\textbf{Derived temporal features} & Often require post-retrieval
enrichment or snapshot materialization \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{next-steps-6}{%
\section{Next Steps}\label{next-steps-6}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{aggregations-api}{Chapter 07:
Aggregations API} to learn about the Feature class for declarative
time-windowed aggregations.

\hypertarget{aggregations-api}{%
\chapter{Aggregations API}\label{aggregations-api}}

The Feature class for declarative time-windowed aggregations

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-7}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-7}}

The Aggregations API provides a declarative way to define time-windowed
features using the \texttt{Feature} class. Instead of writing complex
SQL with window functions, you specify what aggregations you want and
the Feature Store handles the efficient computation.

Examples in this chapter use the canonical demo layout: database
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO}, Feature Store schema
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE}, clickstream source schema
\texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA}, warehouse \texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}, and tables
such as \texttt{ORDERS} (\texttt{ORDER\_TS}, \texttt{ORDER\_ID},
\texttt{USER\_ID}, \texttt{TOTAL\_AMT}).

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{🆕 New in snowflake-ml 1.21+}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

The Feature class and tiled aggregation are new capabilities requiring
\texttt{snowflake-ml-python\ \textgreater{}=\ 1.21.0}.

\end{tcolorbox}

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-6}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-6}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Use the Feature class to define time-windowed aggregations
\item
  Understand tiling for efficient incremental computation
\item
  Configure feature granularity and refresh frequencies
\item
  Apply feature column prefixing for disambiguation
\item
  Name aggregated features following best practices
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{the-feature-class}{%
\section{The Feature Class}\label{the-feature-class}}

\hypertarget{basic-usage}{%
\subsection{Basic Usage}\label{basic-usage}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/feature_class.py}{\texttt{\_code/feature\_class.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ FeatureStore, Feature, FeatureView, Entity}

\CommentTok{\# Define time{-}windowed aggregations declaratively (aliases: \_SUM, \_CNT, \_AVG, …)}
\NormalTok{features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"30d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_30D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.avg(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_AVG\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{max}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"30d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_MAX\_30D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{]}

\CommentTok{\# Create tiled FeatureView (source: canonical clickstream ORDERS)}
\NormalTok{orders\_fqn }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{"FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS"}
\NormalTok{user\_agg\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_PURCHASE\_AGGREGATES"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session.table(orders\_fqn),}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    feature\_granularity}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Tile size}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{features,}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# After creation, register with a zero{-}padded version string, e.g. V01}
\CommentTok{\# fs.register\_feature\_view(feature\_view=user\_agg\_fv, version="V01", block=True)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{available-aggregation-functions-1}{%
\subsection{Available Aggregation
Functions}\label{available-aggregation-functions-1}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3125}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4062}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2812}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Function
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Example
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{Feature.sum(col,\ window)} & Sum over window &
\texttt{Feature.sum("TOTAL\_AMT",\ "7d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.min(col,\ window)} & Minimum over window &
\texttt{Feature.min("TOTAL\_AMT",\ "30d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.max(col,\ window)} & Maximum over window &
\texttt{Feature.max("TOTAL\_AMT",\ "30d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.count(col,\ window)} & Count over window &
\texttt{Feature.count("ORDER\_ID",\ "30d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.avg(col,\ window)} & Average over window &
\texttt{Feature.avg("TOTAL\_AMT",\ "7d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.std(col,\ window)} & Standard deviation &
\texttt{Feature.std("TOTAL\_AMT",\ "30d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.var(col,\ window)} & Variance &
\texttt{Feature.var("TOTAL\_AMT",\ "30d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.last\_n(col,\ window,\ n=N)} & N most recent values &
\texttt{Feature.last\_n("PRODUCT\_ID",\ "7d",\ n=5)} \\
\texttt{Feature.first\_n(col,\ window,\ n=N)} & N oldest values &
\texttt{Feature.first\_n("PRODUCT\_ID",\ "7d",\ n=5)} \\
\texttt{Feature.last\_distinct\_n(col,\ window,\ n=N)} & N most recent
unique values &
\texttt{Feature.last\_distinct\_n("PRODUCT\_ID",\ "7d",\ n=5)} \\
\texttt{Feature.first\_distinct\_n(col,\ window,\ n=N)} & N oldest
unique values &
\texttt{Feature.first\_distinct\_n("PRODUCT\_ID",\ "7d",\ n=5)} \\
\texttt{Feature.approx\_count\_distinct(col,\ window)} & HLL distinct
count &
\texttt{Feature.approx\_count\_distinct("PRODUCT\_ID",\ "7d")} \\
\texttt{Feature.approx\_percentile(col,\ window,\ percentile=0.5)} &
Approximate percentile &
\texttt{Feature.approx\_percentile("TOTAL\_AMT",\ "30d",\ percentile=0.5)} \\
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{window-specifications}{%
\subsection{Window Specifications}\label{window-specifications}}

Windows can be specified using shorthand notation:

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Notation & Meaning \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{"1h"} or \texttt{"1\ hour"} & 1 hour \\
\texttt{"24h"} & 24 hours \\
\texttt{"7d"} or \texttt{"7\ day"} & 7 days \\
\texttt{"30d"} & 30 days \\
\texttt{"1w"} or \texttt{"1\ week"} & 1 week \\
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{window-offset}{%
\subsection{Window offset}\label{window-offset}}

Pass \texttt{offset} to shift the aggregation window backward in time
(for example, ``previous week'' vs ``current week''):

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{, offset}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_PREV\_WEEK"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Use \texttt{.alias("NAME")} on each \texttt{Feature} to set the output
column name.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-naming}{%
\section{Naming Aggregated Features}\label{sec-naming}}

\hypertarget{best-practice-descriptive-aliases}{%
\subsection{Best Practice: Descriptive
Aliases}\label{best-practice-descriptive-aliases}}

Always use \texttt{.alias()} to give features meaningful names:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# ✅ GOOD: Suffix metric role (\_SUM, \_CNT, \_AVG) and window}
\NormalTok{features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"30d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_30D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{]}

\CommentTok{\# ❌ BAD: Auto{-}generated names are hard to interpret}
\NormalTok{features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{),  }\CommentTok{\# opaque default name}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"30d"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-prefixing}{%
\section{Feature Column Prefixing for
Disambiguation}\label{sec-prefixing}}

When joining features from multiple FeatureViews, column name collisions
can occur. Feature Store provides two mechanisms for disambiguation.

\hypertarget{the-problem}{%
\subsection{The Problem}\label{the-problem}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Accidental name collision: both views expose the same alias}
\NormalTok{user\_orders\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDERS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D"}\NormalTok{)],}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{user\_sessions\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_SESSIONS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[Feature.count(}\StringTok{"SESSION\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D"}\NormalTok{)],  }\CommentTok{\# Wrong: same alias!}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Without prefixing, collision occurs}
\NormalTok{dataset }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_dataset(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_orders\_fv, user\_sessions\_fv],  }\CommentTok{\# Which ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D?}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Prefer distinct aliases (for example \texttt{SESSION\_ID\_CNT\_7D} on
the sessions view) so semantics stay clear even when prefixing is off.

\hypertarget{solution-1-auto-prefix}{%
\subsection{Solution 1: Auto-Prefix}\label{solution-1-auto-prefix}}

Use \texttt{auto\_prefix=True} to automatically prefix columns with
FeatureView name:

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/prefixing.py}{\texttt{\_code/prefixing.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{dataset }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_dataset(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_orders\_fv, user\_sessions\_fv],}
\NormalTok{    auto\_prefix}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Columns become USER\_ORDERS\_\_ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D, etc.}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Result columns:}
\CommentTok{\# {-} USER\_ORDERS\_\_ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D}
\CommentTok{\# {-} USER\_SESSIONS\_\_SESSION\_ID\_CNT\_7D}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{solution-2-custom-prefixes-with-.with_name}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{Solution 2: Custom Prefixes with
\texttt{.with\_name()}}{Solution 2: Custom Prefixes with .with\_name()}}\label{solution-2-custom-prefixes-with-.with_name}}

For more control, use \texttt{.with\_name()} on individual FeatureViews
or slices:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{dataset }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_dataset(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}
\NormalTok{        user\_orders\_fv.with\_name(}\StringTok{"orders"}\NormalTok{),      }\CommentTok{\# Prefix: orders\_\_}
\NormalTok{        user\_sessions\_fv.with\_name(}\StringTok{"sessions"}\NormalTok{),  }\CommentTok{\# Prefix: sessions\_\_}
\NormalTok{    ],}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Result columns:}
\CommentTok{\# {-} orders\_\_ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D}
\CommentTok{\# {-} sessions\_\_SESSION\_ID\_CNT\_7D}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{solution-3-combining-both-approaches}{%
\subsection{Solution 3: Combining Both
Approaches}\label{solution-3-combining-both-approaches}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{dataset }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_dataset(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}
\NormalTok{        user\_orders\_fv.with\_name(}\StringTok{"orders"}\NormalTok{),  }\CommentTok{\# Custom prefix}
\NormalTok{        user\_sessions\_fv,                     }\CommentTok{\# Will use auto\_prefix}
\NormalTok{    ],}
\NormalTok{    auto\_prefix}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{Priority}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

\texttt{.with\_name()} takes precedence over \texttt{auto\_prefix}. If a
FeatureView has \texttt{.with\_name()} set, that prefix is used
regardless of \texttt{auto\_prefix} setting.

\end{tcolorbox}

\hypertarget{choosing-a-prefixing-strategy}{%
\subsection{Choosing a Prefixing
Strategy}\label{choosing-a-prefixing-strategy}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3846}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.6154}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Scenario
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Recommendation
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Single FeatureView & No prefix needed \\
Multiple FVs, unique column names & No prefix needed \\
Multiple FVs, potential collisions & Use \texttt{auto\_prefix=True} \\
Want short, custom prefixes & Use \texttt{.with\_name()} \\
Consistent naming across projects & Define naming convention +
\texttt{.with\_name()} \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-tiling}{%
\section{Feature Granularity (Tiling)}\label{sec-tiling}}

\hypertarget{how-tiling-works}{%
\subsection{How Tiling Works}\label{how-tiling-works}}

The \texttt{feature\_granularity} parameter sets the tile size for
incremental computation:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Hourly tiles for high{-}frequency data}
\NormalTok{fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    feature\_granularity}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Each tile covers 1 hour}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"15 minutes"}\NormalTok{,      }\CommentTok{\# Refresh every 15 minutes}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{tile-size-recommendations}{%
\subsection{Tile Size Recommendations}\label{tile-size-recommendations}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Data Pattern & Recommended Tile & Reason \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Clickstream (high frequency) & \texttt{1\ hour} & Many events per
hour \\
Transactions (medium) & \texttt{1\ day} & Daily aggregation patterns \\
Weekly metrics & \texttt{1\ week} & Coarse granularity sufficient \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{multi-window-features}{%
\section{Multi-Window Features}\label{multi-window-features}}

Define features with multiple time windows efficiently:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"1d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_1D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"30d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_30D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"90d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_90D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"30d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_30D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{]}

\CommentTok{\# Single FeatureView efficiently computes all windows (required FV args shown above)}
\NormalTok{multi\_window\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_MULTI\_WINDOW"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session.table(}\StringTok{"FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 day"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{features,}
\NormalTok{    feature\_granularity}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 day"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-5}{%
\section{Best Practices}\label{best-practices-5}}

\hypertarget{use-consistent-naming-conventions}{%
\subsection{1. Use Consistent Naming
Conventions}\label{use-consistent-naming-conventions}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Pattern: \textless{}COL\_OR\_ENTITY\textgreater{}\_\textless{}ROLE\textgreater{}\_\textless{}WINDOW\textgreater{} (roles: \_SUM, \_CNT, \_AVG, …)}
\NormalTok{features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"30d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_30D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.avg(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_AVG\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{match-tile-size-to-data-frequency}{%
\subsection{2. Match Tile Size to Data
Frequency}\label{match-tile-size-to-data-frequency}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# High{-}frequency: smaller tiles}
\NormalTok{clickstream\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    feature\_granularity}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Low{-}frequency: larger tiles}
\NormalTok{weekly\_metrics\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    feature\_granularity}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 day"}\NormalTok{,}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{group-related-features}{%
\subsection{3. Group Related Features}\label{group-related-features}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# ✅ GOOD: Related features in same FeatureView}
\NormalTok{purchase\_features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.count(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"ORDER\_ID\_CNT\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    Feature.avg(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{).alias(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_AVG\_7D"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{]}

\CommentTok{\# ❌ BAD: Unrelated features mixed together}
\NormalTok{mixed\_features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}
\NormalTok{    Feature.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{),  }\CommentTok{\# Purchase feature}
\NormalTok{    Feature.count(}\StringTok{"EVENT\_ID"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"7d"}\NormalTok{),  }\CommentTok{\# Clickstream feature (different grain / entity!)}
\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-rollup}{%
\section{Entity rollup (clickstream)}\label{sec-rollup}}

Clickstream-style hierarchies often roll up \textbf{VISITOR} (anonymous
or device-level activity) → \textbf{USER} (authenticated customer) →
\textbf{HOUSEHOLD} (shared economic unit). Source tables such as
\texttt{EVENTS} (\texttt{EVENT\_TS}, \texttt{USER\_ID},
\texttt{SESSION\_ID}, \texttt{PRODUCT\_ID}, \texttt{EVENT\_TYPE}),
\texttt{SESSIONS}, \texttt{ORDERS}, \texttt{USERS}, and
\texttt{PRODUCTS} tie facts to those keys.

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Define entities} that match the grain of each FeatureView (for
  example, visitor-level tiles on \texttt{EVENTS}, user-level aggregates
  on \texttt{ORDERS} keyed by \texttt{USER\_ID}).
\item
  \textbf{Reuse the same aggregation patterns} (\texttt{Feature.sum},
  \texttt{Feature.count}, \ldots) at each level; change the spine entity
  and join keys when moving from visitor to user to household.
\item
  \textbf{Keep aliases explicit} (\texttt{USER\_ID\_CNT\_7D} vs
  \texttt{VISITOR\_ID\_CNT\_7D},
  \texttt{HOUSEHOLD\_TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM\_30D}, \ldots) so rolled-up
  datasets remain interpretable when multiple levels appear in one
  training set.
\end{itemize}

Rollup is primarily an \textbf{entity and join design} concern; the
Feature class syntax is the same at every level---only the source
\texttt{feature\_df}, \texttt{entities}, and \texttt{timestamp\_col}
change.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-5}{%
\section{Common Pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-5}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-no-alias}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: No Alias}\label{pitfall-1-no-alias}}

\textbf{Problem}: Auto-generated names are unclear.

\textbf{Solution}: Always use \texttt{.alias()} with descriptive names.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-wrong-tile-size}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Wrong Tile
Size}\label{pitfall-2-wrong-tile-size}}

\textbf{Problem}: Tile size doesn't match data frequency.

\textbf{Solution}: Use smaller tiles for high-frequency data.

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-column-collisions}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: Column
Collisions}\label{pitfall-3-column-collisions}}

\textbf{Problem}: Same column names from different FeatureViews.

\textbf{Solution}: Use \texttt{auto\_prefix=True} or
\texttt{.with\_name()}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-6}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-6}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4091}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5909}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Concept
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Feature class} & Declarative API for time-windowed aggregations
(\texttt{Feature.sum}, \texttt{Feature.count}, \ldots) \\
\textbf{Window} & Time period for aggregation (e.g., \texttt{"7d"},
\texttt{"30d"}); optional \texttt{offset} shifts the window back \\
\textbf{Tile (feature\_granularity)} & Pre-computation unit for
efficiency \\
\textbf{Required FV args} & \texttt{timestamp\_col},
\texttt{refresh\_freq}, \texttt{feature\_granularity}, \texttt{features}
(plus \texttt{name}, \texttt{entities}, \texttt{feature\_df}) \\
\textbf{Version} & Register with zero-padded strings such as
\texttt{"V01"}, \texttt{"V02"} \\
\textbf{auto\_prefix} & Automatic column prefixing with FV name \\
\texttt{.with\_name()} & Custom column prefixing \\
\textbf{Rollup} & Same Feature patterns at VISITOR → USER → HOUSEHOLD
with different entities and sources \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{next-steps-7}{%
\section{Next Steps}\label{next-steps-7}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{online-features}{Chapter 08: Online
Features} to learn about Online Feature Tables for real-time serving.

\part{Production}

\hypertarget{online-features}{%
\chapter{Online Features}\label{online-features}}

Online Feature Tables for real-time serving

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-8}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-8}}

Online Feature Tables (OFTs) enable low-latency feature serving for
real-time ML inference. Snowflake treats an OFT as a \textbf{first-class
object}: it combines a \textbf{Hybrid Table} for key-value lookups with
\textbf{incremental refresh} driven by a \textbf{Stream} on the offline
FeatureView source and a \textbf{Task} that runs \textbf{MERGE} SQL into
the Hybrid Table on a schedule controlled by \textbf{TARGET\_LAG}.

This chapter uses the \textbf{clickstream} sample model: database
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO}, source schema \texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA}
(for example \texttt{ORDERS}, \texttt{USERS}, \texttt{SESSIONS}),
Feature Store schema \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE}, warehouse
\texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}. FeatureView registrations use version strings in
\textbf{\texttt{V01} format} (for example \texttt{version="V01"}).

Official references:
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/sql-reference/sql/create-online-feature-table}{CREATE
ONLINE FEATURE TABLE},
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/developer-guide/snowflake-ml/feature-store/create-and-serve-online-features-python}{Create
and serve online features (Python)}.

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-7}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-7}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Explain how Stream, Task, Hybrid Table, and TARGET\_LAG fit together
  in the OFT architecture
\item
  Enable online serving with \texttt{online\_config} on a FeatureView
  (not deprecated builder patterns)
\item
  Tune \texttt{target\_lag} and reason about storage and compute costs
\item
  Retrieve online features via the Feature Store Python API and
  integrate with serving layers
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{what-is-an-online-feature-table}{%
\section{What is an Online Feature
Table?}\label{what-is-an-online-feature-table}}

An Online Feature Table is a managed object that exposes the
\textbf{current (latest) values} per entity for low-latency retrieval.
Physically, online serving uses a \textbf{Hybrid Table} keyed by your
entity columns. Freshness from the \textbf{offline} FeatureView (Dynamic
Table or View) is maintained by:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  A \textbf{Stream} on that offline object, capturing new and changed
  rows.
\item
  A \textbf{Task} that runs on an interval derived from
  \textbf{TARGET\_LAG} (minimum \textbf{10 seconds}, maximum \textbf{8
  days}).
\item
  \textbf{MERGE} (or equivalent incremental logic) into the Hybrid Table
  so only deltas are applied when the Stream has data; when the Stream
  is empty, the Task can finish quickly with \textbf{minimal compute}.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-important-color}{\faExclamation}\hspace{0.5em}{Key Concept}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-important-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-important-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

OFTs store only the \textbf{latest feature values} --- they do not
