retain historical values. For point-in-time historical retrieval, use
the offline FeatureView and training APIs.

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{TARGET\_LAG vs offline \texttt{refresh\_freq}}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

\texttt{refresh\_freq} on the FeatureView controls how often the
\textbf{offline} Dynamic Table (or related materialization) refreshes.
\texttt{OnlineConfig.target\_lag} controls how often the \textbf{online}
sync Task runs. They are \textbf{independent}; end-to-end staleness is
roughly the sum of both paths. See the
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/developer-guide/snowflake-ml/feature-store/create-and-serve-online-features-python}{Python
online features} documentation.

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{verbatim}
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                 ONLINE FEATURE TABLE (OFT) — INTERNAL VIEW                 │
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                            │
│   Offline FeatureView              Stream  +  Task (TARGET_LAG)            │
│   (Dynamic Table or View)          ───────▶  MERGE into Hybrid Table       │
│   ┌─────────────────────────┐         │                                  │
│   │ e.g. USER order stats   │         └──▶  ┌─────────────────────────┐   │
│   │ from CLICKSTREAM_DATA   │              │ Hybrid Table            │   │
│   │ .ORDERS                 │              │ (latest row per key)    │   │
│   └─────────────────────────┘              │ USER_ID │ features…      │   │
│                                            └─────────────────────────┘   │
│                                            Low-latency reads              │
│                                                                            │
└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
\end{verbatim}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{creating-online-feature-tables}{%
\section{Creating Online Feature
Tables}\label{creating-online-feature-tables}}

\hypertarget{enable-online-serving-with-online_config}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{Enable online serving with
\texttt{online\_config}}{Enable online serving with online\_config}}\label{enable-online-serving-with-online_config}}

Enable online features on the \textbf{FeatureView} using
\texttt{online\_config}, not deprecated helpers such as
\texttt{with\_online\_enabled()}.

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/online_feature_tables.py}{\texttt{\_code/online\_feature\_tables.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.snowpark }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ Session}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ FeatureStore, FeatureView, Entity}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ feature\_view}

\NormalTok{session }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Session.builder.configs(...).create()}
\NormalTok{fs }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureStore(}
\NormalTok{    session}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session,}
\NormalTok{    database}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    schema}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"FEATURE\_STORE"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    default\_warehouse}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"FS\_DEV\_WH"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{user\_entity }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Entity(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER"}\NormalTok{, join\_keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}

\NormalTok{feature\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        SUM(TOTAL\_AMT) AS ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM,}
\StringTok{        COUNT(ORDER\_ID) AS ORDER\_CNT,}
\StringTok{        AVG(TOTAL\_AMT) AS ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_AVG,}
\StringTok{        MAX(ORDER\_TS) AS LAST\_ORDER\_TS}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS}
\StringTok{    GROUP BY USER\_ID}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{online\_config }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ feature\_view.OnlineConfig(}
\NormalTok{    enable}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    target\_lag}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"10s"}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Task schedule bound; default in docs/examples often 10 seconds minimum}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_ONLINE\_FV"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{feature\_df,}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_mode}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"AUTO"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER order aggregates from CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS; online + offline"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    online\_config}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{online\_config,}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.register\_feature\_view(feature\_view}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Snowflake creates and wires the OFT infrastructure (Hybrid Table,
Stream, Task) as part of serving enablement; \textbf{TARGET\_LAG} in SQL
corresponds to \textbf{\texttt{OnlineConfig.target\_lag}} in Python.

\hypertarget{sql-equivalent-illustrative}{%
\subsection{SQL equivalent
(illustrative)}\label{sql-equivalent-illustrative}}

For visibility into the object model, the SQL shape mirrors
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/sql-reference/sql/create-online-feature-table}{CREATE
ONLINE FEATURE TABLE}:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{CREATE} \KeywordTok{OR} \KeywordTok{REPLACE} \KeywordTok{ONLINE}\NormalTok{ FEATURE }\KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE.USER\_ORDER\_ONLINE\_OFT}
  \KeywordTok{PRIMARY} \KeywordTok{KEY}\NormalTok{ (USER\_ID)}
\NormalTok{  TIMESTAMP\_COLUMN }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ LAST\_ORDER\_TS}
\NormalTok{  TARGET\_LAG }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}10 seconds\textquotesingle{}}
\NormalTok{  WAREHOUSE }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FS\_DEV\_WH}
\NormalTok{  REFRESH\_MODE }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ AUTO}
\KeywordTok{FROM}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE.}\OperatorTok{\textless{}}\NormalTok{your\_offline\_dynamic\_table\_or\_view}\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}}\NormalTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

(The Python API typically manages object names and wiring when you
register the FeatureView with \texttt{online\_config}.)

\hypertarget{updating-an-existing-featureview}{%
\subsection{Updating an existing
FeatureView}\label{updating-an-existing-featureview}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{fs.update\_feature\_view(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_ONLINE\_FV"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    online\_config}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{feature\_view.OnlineConfig(enable}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{, target\_lag}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"30 seconds"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{retrieving-online-features}{%
\section{Retrieving Online Features}\label{retrieving-online-features}}

Use \texttt{read\_feature\_view} with
\texttt{store\_type=StoreType.ONLINE} and explicit feature names. Keys
are provided as a list of key tuples (one per lookup row).

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ StoreType}

\NormalTok{features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.read\_feature\_view(}
\NormalTok{    feature\_view}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{fv,}
\NormalTok{    keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[[}\StringTok{"user\_001"}\NormalTok{], [}\StringTok{"user\_002"}\NormalTok{]],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_names}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}
        \StringTok{"ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM"}\NormalTok{,}
        \StringTok{"ORDER\_CNT"}\NormalTok{,}
        \StringTok{"ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_AVG"}\NormalTok{,}
        \StringTok{"LAST\_ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    ],}
\NormalTok{    store\_type}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{StoreType.ONLINE,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

For a single entity, pass one inner list, for example
\texttt{keys={[}{[}"user\_001"{]}{]}}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{cost-estimation-qualitative}{%
\section{Cost estimation
(qualitative)}\label{cost-estimation-qualitative}}

Online Feature Tables draw cost from \textbf{storage}, \textbf{refresh
compute}, and \textbf{serving compute}. Treat the following as planning
heuristics; use
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/developer-guide/snowflake-ml/feature-store/create-and-serve-online-features-python}{account
usage views} and your warehouse size for real numbers.

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1818}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2424}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5758}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Area
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Driver
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Qualitative notes
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Hybrid Table storage} & Entity count × feature columns × row
width & Scales with distinct keys you serve and column footprint; Hybrid
Table storage is priced per GB (higher than standard table storage). \\
\textbf{Refresh compute} & \texttt{target\_lag} cadence × MERGE work &
The Task runs on the TARGET\_LAG schedule; \textbf{incremental} refresh
(Stream with new rows) is usually cheap. If the Stream has \textbf{no}
pending data, runs can be very light. \\
\textbf{Offline refresh} & FeatureView \texttt{refresh\_freq} & Separate
from online \texttt{target\_lag}; both contribute to how stale features
can be. \\
\textbf{Online reads} & Lookup volume × warehouse & Each
\texttt{read\_feature\_view(...,\ ONLINE)} uses warehouse resources;
larger warehouses cost more per time. (Check current Snowflake pricing
notes for Hybrid Table request metering.) \\
\end{longtable}

\textbf{Tips:} Prefer \textbf{AUTO} or \textbf{INCREMENTAL} refresh
where supported, right-size \textbf{TARGET\_LAG} to the business SLA,
and avoid setting online sync tighter than your offline FeatureView can
actually refresh.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{performance-tuning}{%
\section{Performance tuning}\label{performance-tuning}}

\hypertarget{batch-key-lookups}{%
\subsection{Batch key lookups}\label{batch-key-lookups}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# ❌ BAD: one round{-}trip per user}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ uid }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ user\_ids:}
\NormalTok{    fs.read\_feature\_view(}
\NormalTok{        feature\_view}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{fv,}
\NormalTok{        keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[[uid]],}
\NormalTok{        feature\_names}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{FEATURE\_NAMES,}
\NormalTok{        store\_type}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{StoreType.ONLINE,}
\NormalTok{    )}

\CommentTok{\# ✅ GOOD: one batched call}
\NormalTok{fs.read\_feature\_view(}
\NormalTok{    feature\_view}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{fv,}
\NormalTok{    keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[[uid] }\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ uid }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ user\_ids],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_names}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{FEATURE\_NAMES,}
\NormalTok{    store\_type}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{StoreType.ONLINE,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{target_lag-trade-offs-online-sync}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{\texttt{target\_lag} trade-offs (online
sync)}{target\_lag trade-offs (online sync)}}\label{target_lag-trade-offs-online-sync}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3425}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1507}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3288}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1781}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
\texttt{target\_lag} (examples)
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Freshness
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Relative refresh cost
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Typical use
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{10\ seconds} \ldots{} \texttt{1\ minute} & Tightest & Higher
Task frequency & Fraud, real-time guards \\
\texttt{1\ minute} \ldots{} \texttt{5\ minutes} & Low & Moderate &
Recommendations, ranking \\
\texttt{15\ minutes} \ldots{} \texttt{1\ hour} & Relaxed & Lower &
Marketing, less critical paths \\
\end{longtable}

Match \textbf{offline} \texttt{refresh\_freq} to upstream
\textbf{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA} landing latency so online sync is not chasing
data that does not exist yet.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{integration-with-external-services}{%
\section{Integration with external
services}\label{integration-with-external-services}}

\hypertarget{fastapi-example}{%
\subsection{FastAPI example}\label{fastapi-example}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/fastapi_serving.py}{\texttt{\_code/fastapi\_serving.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ fastapi }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ FastAPI}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ FeatureStore, StoreType}

\NormalTok{app }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FastAPI()}

\NormalTok{FEATURE\_NAMES }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}
    \StringTok{"ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM"}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{"ORDER\_CNT"}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{"ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_AVG"}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{"LAST\_ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{]}

\AttributeTok{@app.post}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"/features"}\NormalTok{)}
\ControlFlowTok{async} \KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ get\_features(user\_id: }\BuiltInTok{str}\NormalTok{):}
    \CommentTok{"""Latest USER order features from the OFT."""}
\NormalTok{    features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.read\_feature\_view(}
\NormalTok{        feature\_view}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_order\_fv,}
\NormalTok{        keys}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[[user\_id]],}
\NormalTok{        feature\_names}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{FEATURE\_NAMES,}
\NormalTok{        store\_type}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{StoreType.ONLINE,}
\NormalTok{    )}
    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ features.to\_pandas().to\_dict(orient}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"records"}\NormalTok{)[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-6}{%
\section{Best practices}\label{best-practices-6}}

\hypertarget{right-size-target_lag}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{1. Right-size
\texttt{target\_lag}}{1. Right-size target\_lag}}\label{right-size-target_lag}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Tight online sync for high{-}stakes scoring}
\NormalTok{fraud\_online }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ feature\_view.OnlineConfig(enable}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{, target\_lag}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"30 seconds"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Relaxed sync where minutes of lag are acceptable}
\NormalTok{reco\_online }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ feature\_view.OnlineConfig(enable}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{, target\_lag}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"5 minutes"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{monitor-oft-health}{%
\subsection{2. Monitor OFT health}\label{monitor-oft-health}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Refresh / sync history (names may vary by release; use INFORMATION\_SCHEMA as documented for your account)}
\KeywordTok{SELECT} \OperatorTok{*}
\KeywordTok{FROM} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.ONLINE\_FEATURE\_STORE\_HISTORY())}
\KeywordTok{ORDER} \KeywordTok{BY}\NormalTok{ SYNC\_START\_TIME }\KeywordTok{DESC}
\KeywordTok{LIMIT} \DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{use-a-serving-warehouse-appropriately}{%
\subsection{3. Use a serving warehouse
appropriately}\label{use-a-serving-warehouse-appropriately}}

Run Feature Store sessions used for \textbf{online} reads on a warehouse
sized for \textbf{latency and concurrency} (often \texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}
in development, a dedicated production warehouse in real deployments).
The \textbf{TARGET\_LAG} Task uses the warehouse you configure on the
OFT / Feature Store setup.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-6}{%
\section{Common pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-6}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-expecting-historical-data}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: Expecting historical
data}\label{pitfall-1-expecting-historical-data}}

\textbf{Problem:} OFTs only store current values, not history.

\textbf{Solution:} Use offline FeatureViews and temporal retrieval for
training and PIT correctness.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-ignoring-refresh_freq-while-tuning-target_lag}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{❌ Pitfall 2: Ignoring
\texttt{refresh\_freq} while tuning
\texttt{target\_lag}}{❌ Pitfall 2: Ignoring refresh\_freq while tuning target\_lag}}\label{pitfall-2-ignoring-refresh_freq-while-tuning-target_lag}}

\textbf{Problem:} Setting \texttt{target\_lag="10s"} while the offline
Dynamic Table refreshes hourly.

\textbf{Solution:} Align offline refresh, source data latency, and
\texttt{target\_lag} so expectations match reality.

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-per-entity-api-chatter}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: Per-entity API
chatter}\label{pitfall-3-per-entity-api-chatter}}

\textbf{Problem:} Calling \texttt{read\_feature\_view} once per key in a
tight loop.

\textbf{Solution:} Batch keys in one \texttt{keys={[}...{]}} list.

\hypertarget{pitfall-4-using-deprecated-online-enablement-apis}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 4: Using deprecated online enablement
APIs}\label{pitfall-4-using-deprecated-online-enablement-apis}}

\textbf{Problem:} Code or docs that call
\texttt{with\_online\_enabled()} or assume a separate
\texttt{create\_online\_feature\_table} Python flow as the only path.

\textbf{Solution:} Use
\texttt{online\_config=feature\_view.OnlineConfig(...)} on the
FeatureView (or \texttt{update\_feature\_view}).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-7}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-7}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4091}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5909}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Concept
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Online Feature Table} & First-class object: Hybrid Table +
Stream on offline FV + Task (MERGE), driven by \textbf{TARGET\_LAG} \\
\textbf{\texttt{OnlineConfig.target\_lag}} & Python knob for maximum lag
of online table behind source (10s--8d); Task frequency \\
\textbf{\texttt{refresh\_freq}} (FeatureView) & Offline Dynamic Table
refresh; independent of \texttt{target\_lag} \\
\textbf{\texttt{read\_feature\_view(...,\ StoreType.ONLINE)}} &
Low-latency retrieval of latest values \\
\textbf{Current values only} & No historical timeline in the OFT \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{next-steps-8}{%
\section{Next Steps}\label{next-steps-8}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{preprocessing}{Chapter 09: Preprocessing}
to learn about model-dependent transformations and preprocessing
patterns.

\hypertarget{preprocessing}{%
\chapter{Preprocessing}\label{preprocessing}}

Model-dependent transformations, encoding, and scaling

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-9}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-9}}

Model-Dependent Transformations (MDT) are preprocessing steps that
depend on training data statistics or are specific to particular models.
Unlike Model-Independent Transformations (MIT) stored in FeatureViews,
MDTs are stored with the model and applied consistently during training
and inference.

Examples in this chapter use the \textbf{clickstream} sample context:
database \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO}, schema \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE},
source \texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA}, warehouse \texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}.
Training features often come from a FeatureView whose version label
follows \textbf{\texttt{V01}} (not \texttt{v1}).

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-8}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-8}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Distinguish between MIT and MDT transformations
\item
  Choose between \textbf{\texttt{sklearn.pipeline.Pipeline}} and
  \textbf{\texttt{snowflake.ml.modeling.pipeline.Pipeline}}, and prefer
  open-source scikit-learn with Model Registry for most new work
\item
  Apply encoding techniques (one-hot, ordinal) on clickstream
  categoricals
\item
  Implement scaling (standard, min-max) on numeric session/order fields
\item
  Log a fitted estimator or full sklearn pipeline with
  \texttt{Registry.log\_model()} so training and serving stay aligned
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{transformation-taxonomy}{%
\section{Transformation Taxonomy}\label{transformation-taxonomy}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1622}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2703}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2973}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2703}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Type
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Location
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Stored In
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Examples
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{MIT} & Feature Pipeline & FeatureView & Aggregations, joins,
derived columns \\
\textbf{MDT} & Training Pipeline & Model Registry & Scaling, encoding,
imputation \\
\textbf{ODT} & Inference Time & Not stored & Request-time
calculations \\
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{decision-guide}{%
\subsection{Decision Guide}\label{decision-guide}}

\begin{verbatim}
Is the transformation reusable across multiple models?
├── YES → MIT (store in FeatureView)
└── NO  → Does it depend on training data statistics?
          ├── YES → MDT (store with model)
          └── NO  → ODT (compute at inference)
\end{verbatim}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{pipeline-classes-scikit-learn-vs-snowflake-ml-e5}{%
\section{Pipeline classes: scikit-learn vs Snowflake ML
(E5)}\label{pipeline-classes-scikit-learn-vs-snowflake-ml-e5}}

Two different classes are both named \texttt{Pipeline}; they are
\textbf{not} interchangeable.

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2500}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2857}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4643}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Class
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Module
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Typical use
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{\texttt{sklearn.pipeline.Pipeline}} & scikit-learn & Local
training, notebooks, open-source frameworks, and \textbf{recommended}
paths where you fit on pandas or in-memory data and register the
artifact. \\
\textbf{\texttt{snowflake.ml.modeling.pipeline.Pipeline}} & Snowflake ML
& Distributed pipeline orchestration \textbf{inside} Snowflake ML's
modeling stack. \\
\end{longtable}

\textbf{Recommendation for new development:} build preprocessing and
models with \textbf{open-source scikit-learn} (and related ecosystem
libraries), then persist the fitted model or \textbf{full sklearn
pipeline} (preprocessing + estimator) to the Snowflake Model Registry
using \texttt{Registry.log\_model()}. That keeps preprocessing and model
versioned together and avoids training/serving skew.

The \textbf{\texttt{snowflake.ml.modeling}} estimators and pipeline are
\textbf{discouraged for new development} in favor of sklearn equivalents
plus Model Registry logging, unless you have a specific requirement to
stay on the distributed Snowflake ML modeling API.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.pipeline }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ Pipeline }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ SklearnPipeline}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.compose }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ ColumnTransformer}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.preprocessing }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ OneHotEncoder, OrdinalEncoder, StandardScaler}

\CommentTok{\# Example: preprocess + estimator wrapped in a single sklearn Pipeline, then log\_model(pipeline, ...)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{encoding-techniques}{%
\section{Encoding Techniques}\label{encoding-techniques}}

\hypertarget{one-hot-encoding}{%
\subsection{One-Hot Encoding}\label{one-hot-encoding}}

Nominal columns from clickstream entities (no natural order):
\textbf{\texttt{EVENT\_TYPE}} (from \texttt{EVENTS}),
\textbf{\texttt{PAYMENT\_METHOD}} (from \texttt{ORDERS}),
\textbf{\texttt{DEVICE\_TYPE}} (from \texttt{USERS} or
\texttt{SESSIONS}). Expanded binary columns should follow your naming
standard; this guide uses the \textbf{\texttt{\_OHE}} suffix for one-hot
outputs (for example \texttt{EVENT\_TYPE\_click\_OHE} after you align
names with \texttt{get\_feature\_names\_out()} or your own prefix
rules).

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/encoding.py}{\texttt{\_code/encoding.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.preprocessing }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ OneHotEncoder}

\NormalTok{encoder }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ OneHotEncoder(}
\NormalTok{    drop}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"first"}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Avoid multicollinearity}
\NormalTok{    sparse\_output}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{False}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    handle\_unknown}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"ignore"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Fit on training data only — columns e.g. EVENT\_TYPE, PAYMENT\_METHOD, DEVICE\_TYPE}
\NormalTok{encoder.fit(train\_df[[}\StringTok{"EVENT\_TYPE"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"PAYMENT\_METHOD"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DEVICE\_TYPE"}\NormalTok{]])}

\NormalTok{train\_ohe }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ encoder.transform(train\_df[[}\StringTok{"EVENT\_TYPE"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"PAYMENT\_METHOD"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DEVICE\_TYPE"}\NormalTok{]])}
\NormalTok{inference\_ohe }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ encoder.transform(inference\_df[[}\StringTok{"EVENT\_TYPE"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"PAYMENT\_METHOD"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DEVICE\_TYPE"}\NormalTok{]])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{ordinal-encoding}{%
\subsection{Ordinal Encoding}\label{ordinal-encoding}}

Use when categories have a \textbf{fixed order}. Clickstream examples:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{\texttt{SUBSCRIPTION\_STATUS}} (\texttt{USERS}): \texttt{none}
  \textless{} \texttt{basic} \textless{} \texttt{premium}
\item
  \textbf{\texttt{INCOME\_BRACKET}} (when present on user or profile
  features): \texttt{low} \textless{} \texttt{medium} \textless{}
  \texttt{high} \textless{} \texttt{premium}
\end{itemize}

Store integer outputs with the \textbf{\texttt{\_ENCODED}} suffix (for
example \texttt{SUBSCRIPTION\_STATUS\_ENCODED}).

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.preprocessing }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ OrdinalEncoder}

\NormalTok{encoder }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ OrdinalEncoder(}
\NormalTok{    categories}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}
\NormalTok{        [}\StringTok{"none"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"basic"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"premium"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{        [}\StringTok{"low"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"medium"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"high"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"premium"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{    ],}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{encoder.fit(}
\NormalTok{    train\_df[[}\StringTok{"SUBSCRIPTION\_STATUS"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"INCOME\_BRACKET"}\NormalTok{]]}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{scaling-techniques}{%
\section{Scaling Techniques}\label{scaling-techniques}}

\hypertarget{standard-scaling-z-score}{%
\subsection{Standard Scaling (Z-score)}\label{standard-scaling-z-score}}

Scale numeric fields such as \textbf{\texttt{TOTAL\_AMT}} (orders),
\textbf{\texttt{DURATION\_SEC}} (sessions), and
\textbf{\texttt{ITEM\_CNT}} (baskets or line items). Use clear scaled
names (for example \texttt{TOTAL\_AMT} → column you feed to the model
after scaling, often via \texttt{ColumnTransformer} feature names).

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.preprocessing }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ StandardScaler}

\NormalTok{scaler }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ StandardScaler()}

\NormalTok{scaler.fit(train\_df[[}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DURATION\_SEC"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"ITEM\_CNT"}\NormalTok{]])}
\NormalTok{train\_scaled }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ scaler.transform(train\_df[[}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DURATION\_SEC"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"ITEM\_CNT"}\NormalTok{]])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{min-max-scaling}{%
\subsection{Min-Max Scaling}\label{min-max-scaling}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.preprocessing }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ MinMaxScaler}

\NormalTok{scaler }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ MinMaxScaler()}

\NormalTok{scaler.fit(train\_df[[}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DURATION\_SEC"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"ITEM\_CNT"}\NormalTok{]])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{when-to-use-each}{%
\subsection{When to Use Each}\label{when-to-use-each}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3793}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3448}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2759}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Technique
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Use When
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Models
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Standard} & Features are roughly normal or you want zero mean /
unit variance & Linear, SVM, Neural Networks \\
\textbf{Min-Max} & Need bounded range {[}0,1{]} & Neural Networks,
KNN \\
\textbf{None} & Tree-based models & XGBoost, Random Forest \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{preprocessing-pipeline}{%
\section{Preprocessing Pipeline}\label{preprocessing-pipeline}}

\hypertarget{building-a-pipeline-recommended-sklearn}{%
\subsection{Building a Pipeline (recommended:
sklearn)}\label{building-a-pipeline-recommended-sklearn}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/preprocessing_pipeline.py}{\texttt{\_code/preprocessing\_pipeline.py}}
\end{quote}

Combine one-hot, ordinal, and numeric scaling with
\textbf{\texttt{sklearn.compose.ColumnTransformer}} and wrap the result
in \textbf{\texttt{sklearn.pipeline.Pipeline}} together with your
estimator. Log \textbf{that} object with the registry so inference
replays the same steps.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.compose }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ ColumnTransformer}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.pipeline }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ Pipeline}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.preprocessing }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ OneHotEncoder, OrdinalEncoder, StandardScaler}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.linear\_model }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ LogisticRegression}

\NormalTok{onehot\_cols }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{"EVENT\_TYPE"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"PAYMENT\_METHOD"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DEVICE\_TYPE"}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{ordinal\_cols }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{"SUBSCRIPTION\_STATUS"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"INCOME\_BRACKET"}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{numeric\_cols }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DURATION\_SEC"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"ITEM\_CNT"}\NormalTok{]}

\NormalTok{preprocess }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ ColumnTransformer(}
\NormalTok{    transformers}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}
\NormalTok{        (}
            \StringTok{"ohe"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{            OneHotEncoder(drop}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"first"}\NormalTok{, sparse\_output}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{False}\NormalTok{, handle\_unknown}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"ignore"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{            onehot\_cols,}
\NormalTok{        ),}
\NormalTok{        (}
            \StringTok{"ord"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{            OrdinalEncoder(}
\NormalTok{                categories}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}
\NormalTok{                    [}\StringTok{"none"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"basic"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"premium"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{                    [}\StringTok{"low"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"medium"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"high"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"premium"}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{                ]}
\NormalTok{            ),}
\NormalTok{            ordinal\_cols,}
\NormalTok{        ),}
\NormalTok{        (}\StringTok{"scale"}\NormalTok{, StandardScaler(), numeric\_cols),}
\NormalTok{    ],}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{full\_pipeline }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Pipeline(}
\NormalTok{    steps}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}
\NormalTok{        (}\StringTok{"preprocess"}\NormalTok{, preprocess),}
\NormalTok{        (}\StringTok{"clf"}\NormalTok{, LogisticRegression(max\_iter}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{1000}\NormalTok{)),}
\NormalTok{    ]}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{full\_pipeline.fit(train\_df, train\_df[}\StringTok{"IS\_CONVERTED"}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{snowflake-ml-pipeline-not-the-default-for-new-work}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{Snowflake ML \texttt{Pipeline} (not the
default for new
work)}{Snowflake ML Pipeline (not the default for new work)}}\label{snowflake-ml-pipeline-not-the-default-for-new-work}}

If you maintain legacy jobs built on
\textbf{\texttt{snowflake.ml.modeling.pipeline.Pipeline}}, keep using
that stack consistently for those jobs---but \textbf{do not} assume it
behaves like sklearn's \texttt{Pipeline}. For new projects, prefer the
sklearn pattern above and \textbf{\texttt{log\_model()}} the sklearn
pipeline.

\hypertarget{saving-with-model-registry}{%
\subsection{Saving with Model
Registry}\label{saving-with-model-registry}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.registry }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ Registry}

\NormalTok{registry }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Registry(session}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session)}

\CommentTok{\# Log the full sklearn pipeline (preprocessing + model) or the fitted estimator}
\NormalTok{registry.log\_model(}
\NormalTok{    model}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{full\_pipeline,}
\NormalTok{    model\_name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"session\_conversion\_model"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    version\_name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    comment}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Clickstream FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE; sklearn preprocessing + classifier"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{preprocessing-ownership-slas}{%
\section{Preprocessing Ownership \&
SLAs}\label{preprocessing-ownership-slas}}

Define ownership for preprocessing transformations:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# preprocessing\_manifest.yaml}
\FunctionTok{preprocessing}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{  }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ }\FunctionTok{model}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ session\_conversion\_model\_V01}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{owner}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ ds{-}team@company.com}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{warehouse}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ FS\_DEV\_WH}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{source}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ CLICKSTREAM\_DATA}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{transformations}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ }\FunctionTok{type}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ OneHotEncoder}
\AttributeTok{        }\FunctionTok{columns}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\KeywordTok{[}\AttributeTok{EVENT\_TYPE}\KeywordTok{,}\AttributeTok{ PAYMENT\_METHOD}\KeywordTok{,}\AttributeTok{ DEVICE\_TYPE}\KeywordTok{]}
\AttributeTok{        }\FunctionTok{naming}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ \_OHE}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ }\FunctionTok{type}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ OrdinalEncoder}
\AttributeTok{        }\FunctionTok{columns}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\KeywordTok{[}\AttributeTok{SUBSCRIPTION\_STATUS}\KeywordTok{,}\AttributeTok{ INCOME\_BRACKET}\KeywordTok{]}
\AttributeTok{        }\FunctionTok{naming}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ \_ENCODED}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ }\FunctionTok{type}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ StandardScaler}
\AttributeTok{        }\FunctionTok{columns}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ }\KeywordTok{[}\AttributeTok{TOTAL\_AMT}\KeywordTok{,}\AttributeTok{ DURATION\_SEC}\KeywordTok{,}\AttributeTok{ ITEM\_CNT}\KeywordTok{]}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{validation}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ }\FunctionTok{check}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ no\_nulls\_after\_encoding}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ }\FunctionTok{check}\KeywordTok{:}\AttributeTok{ scaled\_values\_bounded}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-7}{%
\section{Best Practices}\label{best-practices-7}}

\hypertarget{fit-on-training-data-only}{%
\subsection{1. Fit on Training Data
Only}\label{fit-on-training-data-only}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# ✅ GOOD: Fit on training, transform both}
\NormalTok{scaler.fit(train\_df[[}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DURATION\_SEC"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"ITEM\_CNT"}\NormalTok{]])}
\NormalTok{train\_scaled }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ scaler.transform(train\_df[[}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DURATION\_SEC"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"ITEM\_CNT"}\NormalTok{]])}
\NormalTok{test\_scaled }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ scaler.transform(test\_df[[}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"DURATION\_SEC"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"ITEM\_CNT"}\NormalTok{]])}

\CommentTok{\# ❌ BAD: Fitting on test data (data leakage)}
\NormalTok{scaler.fit(test\_df)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{store-transformations-with-model}{%
\subsection{2. Store Transformations with
Model}\label{store-transformations-with-model}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Preprocessing becomes part of model artifact}
\CommentTok{\# Ensures consistency between training and inference}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{choose-right-transformation-for-model}{%
\subsection{3. Choose Right Transformation for
Model}\label{choose-right-transformation-for-model}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Tree models: no scaling needed}
\CommentTok{\# Linear models: scaling important}
\CommentTok{\# Neural networks: both encoding and scaling}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-7}{%
\section{Common Pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-7}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-trainingserving-skew}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: Training/Serving
Skew}\label{pitfall-1-trainingserving-skew}}

\textbf{Problem}: Different preprocessing in training vs.~inference.

\textbf{Solution}: Use one sklearn \texttt{Pipeline} (or equivalent) and
log it with \texttt{Registry.log\_model()}.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-fitting-on-test-data}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Fitting on Test
Data}\label{pitfall-2-fitting-on-test-data}}

\textbf{Problem}: Fitting scaler on test data leaks information.

\textbf{Solution}: Always fit on training data only.

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-wrong-transformation-for-model}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: Wrong Transformation for
Model}\label{pitfall-3-wrong-transformation-for-model}}

\textbf{Problem}: Using scaling for tree-based models (unnecessary).

\textbf{Solution}: Match transformation to model requirements.

\hypertarget{pitfall-4-confusing-the-two-pipeline-classes}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{❌ Pitfall 4: Confusing the two
\texttt{Pipeline}
classes}{❌ Pitfall 4: Confusing the two Pipeline classes}}\label{pitfall-4-confusing-the-two-pipeline-classes}}

\textbf{Problem}: Importing or serializing the wrong \texttt{Pipeline}
so steps or \texttt{fit} behavior do not match expectations.

\textbf{Solution}: Prefer
\texttt{from\ sklearn.pipeline\ import\ Pipeline} for new work; treat
\texttt{snowflake.ml.modeling.pipeline.Pipeline} as a separate,
legacy/distributed API.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-8}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-8}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3750}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2250}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4000}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Transformation
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Purpose
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Store Location
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{OneHotEncoder} & Categorical → binary columns (\texttt{\_OHE}) &
Model Registry (via logged sklearn pipeline) \\
\textbf{OrdinalEncoder} & Ordered categorical → integer
(\texttt{\_ENCODED}) & Model Registry \\
\textbf{StandardScaler} & Normalize (z-score) numeric features & Model
Registry \\
\textbf{MinMaxScaler} & Scale to {[}0,1{]} & Model Registry \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{next-steps-9}{%
\section{Next Steps}\label{next-steps-9}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{training-inference}{Chapter 10: Training
\& Inference} to learn about generating training datasets and inference
workflows.

\hypertarget{training-inference}{%
\chapter{Training \& Inference}\label{training-inference}}

Generating datasets, spine design, and Model Registry integration

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-10}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-10}}

This chapter covers the end-to-end workflow for using Feature Store in
ML pipelines: from designing spines and generating training datasets to
batch and online inference.

This guide uses the \textbf{clickstream} sample shape: database
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO}, source schema \texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA}
(tables \texttt{SESSIONS}, \texttt{EVENTS}, \texttt{ORDERS},
\texttt{USERS}), Feature Store schema \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE}, warehouse
\texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}. FeatureView registrations use version strings in
\textbf{\texttt{V01} format} (for example \texttt{version="V01"}).

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-9}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-9}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Design effective spines for training and inference
\item
  Choose between \texttt{generate\_dataset()} and
  \texttt{generate\_training\_set()} for your workload
\item
  Generate training data with point-in-time correctness
\item
  Apply feature column prefixing for disambiguation
\item
  Integrate with Snowflake Model Registry using open-source estimators
\item
  Implement batch and online inference workflows
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{spine-design}{%
\section{Spine Design}\label{spine-design}}

The \textbf{spine} defines which entities need features and when. Its
structure differs between training and inference.

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Use Case & Required Columns & Optional Columns \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Training} & Entity keys, Timestamp & Label (target) \\
\textbf{Batch Inference} & Entity keys, Timestamp & --- \\
\textbf{Online Inference} & Entity keys only & --- \\
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{training-spine-1}{%
\subsection{Training Spine}\label{training-spine-1}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/spine_design.py}{\texttt{\_code/spine\_design.py}}
\end{quote}

Use \textbf{\texttt{SESSION\_START\_TS}} from \texttt{SESSIONS} as the
point-in-time column so its name matches what you pass to
\texttt{spine\_timestamp\_col}. If you alias it (for example
\texttt{SESSION\_START\_TS\ AS\ EVENT\_TS}), the original name is no
longer in the DataFrame---downstream code and
\texttt{spine\_timestamp\_col} must use the aliased name consistently.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Training spine: USER\_ID + PIT timestamp + label (conversion from session)}
\NormalTok{training\_spine }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        SESSION\_START\_TS,}
\StringTok{        IS\_CONVERTED AS LABEL}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.SESSIONS}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{inference-spine}{%
\subsection{Inference Spine}\label{inference-spine}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Inference spine: no label column; score active users as of now}
\NormalTok{inference\_spine }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        CURRENT\_TIMESTAMP() AS SESSION\_START\_TS}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.USERS}
\StringTok{    WHERE IS\_ACTIVE = TRUE}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{generate_dataset-vs-generate_training_set}{%
\section{\texorpdfstring{\texttt{generate\_dataset()} vs
\texttt{generate\_training\_set()}}{generate\_dataset() vs generate\_training\_set()}}\label{generate_dataset-vs-generate_training_set}}

Both methods accept \texttt{spine\_df}, \texttt{features}, and
\texttt{spine\_timestamp\_col} and perform point-in-time correct feature
retrieval. They target different downstream workflows.

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.0517}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4310}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5172}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
\texttt{fs.generate\_dataset()}
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
\texttt{fs.generate\_training\_set()}
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Returns} & A versioned Snowflake ML \textbf{Dataset} (Parquet
files in a stage) & A \textbf{Snowpark DataFrame} (not a versioned
Dataset object) \\
\textbf{Versioning} & Supports a \texttt{version} parameter for the
Dataset & No Dataset versioning; optionally persist with
\texttt{save\_as} \\
\textbf{Typical use} & Deep learning (TensorFlow, PyTorch) and pipelines
that consume the Dataset API & Classic ML (scikit-learn, XGBoost),
especially training inside a Virtual Warehouse via Python stored
procedures / UDFs \\
\textbf{Persist} & Dataset lifecycle is managed as a registered Dataset
& Pass \texttt{save\_as} to write the joined result to a table \\
\end{longtable}

See the Snowflake ML Dataset documentation:
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/developer-guide/snowflake-ml/dataset}{Snowflake
ML Dataset}.

\hypertarget{versioned-dataset-deep-learning}{%
\subsection{Versioned Dataset (deep
learning)}\label{versioned-dataset-deep-learning}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{dataset }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_dataset(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{training\_spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_order\_fv, user\_session\_fv],}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\CommentTok{\# Consume Parquet{-}backed Dataset per Snowflake ML Dataset docs (e.g. TensorFlow / PyTorch).}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{snowpark-dataframe-classic-ml}{%
\subsection{Snowpark DataFrame (classic
ML)}\label{snowpark-dataframe-classic-ml}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{training\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_training\_set(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{training\_spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_order\_fv, user\_session\_fv],}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    save\_as}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE.TRAINING\_SET\_CONVERSION\_V01"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\CommentTok{\# training\_df is a Snowpark DataFrame; use in Snowpark or convert for sklearn / XGBoost as needed.}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{generating-training-datasets}{%
\section{Generating Training
Datasets}\label{generating-training-datasets}}

\hypertarget{basic-usage-snowpark-classic-ml}{%
\subsection{Basic usage (Snowpark / classic
ML)}\label{basic-usage-snowpark-classic-ml}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{training\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_training\_set(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{training\_spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_order\_fv, user\_session\_fv],}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{multi-featureview-joins}{%
\subsection{Multi-FeatureView joins}\label{multi-featureview-joins}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{training\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_training\_set(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{training\_spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}
\NormalTok{        user\_order\_fv,}
\NormalTok{        user\_session\_fv,}
\NormalTok{        user\_profile\_fv,}
\NormalTok{    ],}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-prefixing}{%
\section{Feature Column Prefixing}\label{sec-prefixing}}

When joining multiple FeatureViews, column name collisions can occur.

\hypertarget{using-auto_prefix}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{Using
\texttt{auto\_prefix}}{Using auto\_prefix}}\label{using-auto_prefix}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{training\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_training\_set(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{training\_spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_orders\_fv, user\_sessions\_fv],}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    auto\_prefix}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Result columns (example):}
\CommentTok{\# USER\_ORDERS\_\_TOTAL\_SPEND\_7D}
\CommentTok{\# USER\_SESSIONS\_\_SESSION\_CNT\_7D}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{using-.with_name}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{Using
\texttt{.with\_name()}}{Using .with\_name()}}\label{using-.with_name}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{training\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_training\_set(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{training\_spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}
\NormalTok{        user\_orders\_fv.with\_name(}\StringTok{"ord"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        user\_sessions\_fv.with\_name(}\StringTok{"sess"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    ],}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Result columns (example):}
\CommentTok{\# ord\_\_TOTAL\_SPEND\_7D}
\CommentTok{\# sess\_\_SESSION\_CNT\_7D}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{choosing-a-strategy}{%
\subsection{Choosing a strategy}\label{choosing-a-strategy}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Scenario & Recommendation \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Single FeatureView & No prefix needed \\
Multiple FVs, unique names & No prefix needed \\
Multiple FVs, potential collisions & Use \texttt{auto\_prefix=True} \\
Want custom short prefixes & Use \texttt{.with\_name()} \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{model-registry-integration}{%
\section{Model Registry integration}\label{model-registry-integration}}

Prefer \textbf{open-source libraries} (scikit-learn, XGBoost, and so on)
for model fitting. The \texttt{snowflake.ml.modeling} estimators are
discouraged for new development. Fit with your library of choice, then
log the trained object with \textbf{\texttt{Registry.log\_model()}}.

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/model_registry.py}{\texttt{\_code/model\_registry.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.registry }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ Registry}

\NormalTok{reg }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Registry(}
\NormalTok{    session}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{session,}
\NormalTok{    database\_name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    schema\_name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"MODEL\_REGISTRY"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{reg.log\_model(}
\NormalTok{    model,}
\NormalTok{    model\_name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"churn\_model"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    version\_name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    comment}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Trained with USER\_ORDER\_FV V01, USER\_SESSION\_FV V01; spine SESSIONS + SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{lineage-flow}{%
\subsection{Lineage flow}\label{lineage-flow}}

\begin{verbatim}
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                        END-TO-END LINEAGE                               │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                         │
│  Source Tables → FeatureViews → Training artifact → Model → Predictions │
│                                                                         │
│  ORDERS     →  USER_ORDER_FV     →  TRAINING_SET / Dataset  →  V01  → … │
│  SESSIONS   →  USER_SESSION_FV   ↗                                      │
│                                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
\end{verbatim}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{batch-inference}{%
\section{Batch inference}\label{batch-inference}}

\hypertarget{workflow}{%
\subsection{Workflow}\label{workflow}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# 1. Inference spine (entities to score)}
\NormalTok{inference\_spine }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        CURRENT\_TIMESTAMP() AS SESSION\_START\_TS}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.USERS}
\StringTok{    WHERE IS\_ACTIVE = TRUE}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# 2. Point{-}in{-}time features as Snowpark DataFrame}
\NormalTok{inference\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_training\_set(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{inference\_spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_order\_fv, user\_session\_fv],}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# 3. Score with your framework (e.g. bring features to the client, or run in a stored procedure)}
\CommentTok{\# predictions = model.predict(inference\_df.to\_pandas().drop(columns=[...]))}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

For frameworks that consume a Snowflake ML Dataset instead, build a
spine the same way and use \texttt{generate\_dataset()} with an
appropriate \texttt{version}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-8}{%
\section{Best practices}\label{best-practices-8}}

\hypertarget{spine-design-1}{%
\subsection{1. Spine design}\label{spine-design-1}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# ✅ GOOD: Timestamp column name is explicit and matches spine\_timestamp\_col}
\NormalTok{spine }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        SESSION\_START\_TS,}
\StringTok{        IS\_CONVERTED AS LABEL}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.SESSIONS}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}
\CommentTok{\# Use spine\_timestamp\_col="SESSION\_START\_TS"}

\CommentTok{\# ⚠️ If you must rename the timestamp, document it—original name is gone for downstream code}
\NormalTok{spine }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        SESSION\_START\_TS AS EVENT\_TS,}
\StringTok{        IS\_CONVERTED AS LABEL}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.SESSIONS}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}
\CommentTok{\# Must use spine\_timestamp\_col="EVENT\_TS" everywhere after this point}

\CommentTok{\# ❌ BAD: Ambiguous timestamp column}
\NormalTok{spine }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        SOME\_DATE}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.SESSIONS}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{feature-selection}{%
\subsection{2. Feature selection}\label{feature-selection}}

Registered FeatureViews expose
\textbf{\texttt{.slice({[}"col1",\ "col2"{]})}} to restrict columns. Do
not assume \texttt{.select()} on the FeatureView object.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{training\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_training\_set(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{training\_spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}
\NormalTok{        user\_order\_fv.}\BuiltInTok{slice}\NormalTok{([}\StringTok{"TOTAL\_SPEND\_7D"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"ORDER\_CNT\_30D"}\NormalTok{]),}
\NormalTok{    ],}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{validate-before-training-1}{%
\subsection{3. Validate before
training}\label{validate-before-training-1}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Check for data issues (column names depend on your spine / FVs)}
\ControlFlowTok{assert}\NormalTok{ training\_df.}\BuiltInTok{filter}\NormalTok{(F.col(}\StringTok{"LABEL"}\NormalTok{).isNull()).count() }\OperatorTok{==} \DecValTok{0}
\ControlFlowTok{assert}\NormalTok{ training\_df.count() }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}} \DecValTok{1000}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-8}{%
\section{Common pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-8}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-no-timestamp-column}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: No timestamp
column}\label{pitfall-1-no-timestamp-column}}

\textbf{Problem}: PIT retrieval does not work without a timestamp.

\textbf{Solution}: Always include a spine timestamp and set
\texttt{spine\_timestamp\_col} to its name.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-feature-leakage}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Feature
leakage}\label{pitfall-2-feature-leakage}}

\textbf{Problem}: Using features computed from future data relative to
the spine row.

\textbf{Solution}: Use \texttt{spine\_timestamp\_col} and validate
cutoff behavior.

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-column-collisions-1}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: Column
collisions}\label{pitfall-3-column-collisions-1}}

\textbf{Problem}: Same feature names from multiple FeatureViews.

\textbf{Solution}: Use \texttt{auto\_prefix} or \texttt{.with\_name()}.

\hypertarget{pitfall-4-wrong-api-for-the-framework}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 4: Wrong API for the
framework}\label{pitfall-4-wrong-api-for-the-framework}}

\textbf{Problem}: Expecting a Snowpark DataFrame from
\texttt{generate\_dataset()} or Dataset Parquet from
\texttt{generate\_training\_set()}.

\textbf{Solution}: Use the comparison table above; match the method to
DL (Dataset) vs classic ML (DataFrame / \texttt{save\_as}).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-9}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-9}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4091}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5909}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Concept
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Spine} & DataFrame defining entities and timestamps (and label
for training) \\
\texttt{generate\_dataset()} & Versioned Snowflake ML Dataset (Parquet
on a stage); strong fit for deep learning \\
\texttt{generate\_training\_set()} & Snowpark DataFrame; optional
\texttt{save\_as}; strong fit for classic ML in Snowflake \\
\texttt{auto\_prefix} & Automatic column prefixing across
FeatureViews \\
\texttt{.with\_name()} & Custom column prefixing \\
\texttt{.slice({[}...{]})} & Restrict features from a registered
FeatureView \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{next-steps-10}{%
\section{Next steps}\label{next-steps-10}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{operations}{Chapter 11: Operations} to
learn about monitoring, data quality, and operational management.

\part{Operations \& Advanced}

\hypertarget{operations}{%
\chapter{Operations}\label{operations}}

Monitoring, data quality, lineage, and operational management

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-11}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-11}}

Operational excellence is critical for production Feature Stores. This
chapter covers monitoring, data quality, lineage tracking, and
day-to-day operational management.

Examples use the \textbf{clickstream} sample layout: database
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO}, Feature Store schema
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE}, source schema \texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA},
warehouse \texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}, and FeatureView version labels in
\textbf{\texttt{V01}} format (for example \texttt{version="V01"},
dynamic table suffix \texttt{\$V01}).

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-10}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-10}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Monitor Feature Store health and performance
\item
  Implement data quality checks
\item
  Track data lineage end-to-end
\item
  Manage costs and compute resources
\item
  Troubleshoot common issues
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{metadata-and-information_schema}{%
\section{Metadata and
INFORMATION\_SCHEMA}\label{metadata-and-information_schema}}

Entity and FeatureView definitions live in the \textbf{Snowflake ML
Feature Store} service; they are \textbf{not} rows in non-existent views
such as \texttt{INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.MODELS},
\texttt{INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.MODEL\_DATASETS}, or
\texttt{INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DATASET\_FEATURE\_VIEWS} --- \textbf{those
views do not exist}.

Use this instead:

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2727}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.7273}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Need
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Where to look
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Physical columns behind features & \texttt{INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.COLUMNS}
(and \texttt{TABLES} / \texttt{VIEWS} for object types) \\
Dynamic Table refresh / lag &
\texttt{TABLE(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLE\_REFRESH\_HISTORY(...))},
\texttt{TABLE(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLES())} \\
Model Registry models & \texttt{INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.MODEL\_VERSIONS}
(not \texttt{MODELS}) \\
Python API catalog & \texttt{FeatureStore.list\_feature\_views()},
\texttt{get\_feature\_view()} \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{refresh-monitoring}{%
\section{Refresh Monitoring}\label{refresh-monitoring}}

\hypertarget{dynamic-table-refresh-status}{%
\subsection{Dynamic Table Refresh
Status}\label{dynamic-table-refresh-status}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/monitoring.sql}{\texttt{\_code/monitoring.sql}}
\end{quote}

Refresh history is exposed by the \textbf{table function}
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/sql-reference/functions/dynamic_table_refresh_history}{\texttt{DYNAMIC\_TABLE\_REFRESH\_HISTORY}}
(invoke via
\texttt{TABLE(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLE\_REFRESH\_HISTORY(...))}).

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Check refresh history for a registered FeatureView backed by a Dynamic Table}
\KeywordTok{SELECT}
\NormalTok{    NAME,}
\NormalTok{    STATE,}
\NormalTok{    REFRESH\_START\_TIME,}
\NormalTok{    REFRESH\_END\_TIME,}
    \KeywordTok{STATISTICS}\CharTok{:numInsertedRows}\NormalTok{:}\CharTok{:INT} \KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ ROWS\_INSERTED}
\KeywordTok{FROM} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLE\_REFRESH\_HISTORY(}
\NormalTok{    NAME }\OperatorTok{=\textgreater{}} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE.USER\_ORDER\_FV$V01\textquotesingle{}}
\NormalTok{))}
\KeywordTok{ORDER} \KeywordTok{BY}\NormalTok{ REFRESH\_START\_TIME }\KeywordTok{DESC}
\KeywordTok{LIMIT} \DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{;}

\CommentTok{{-}{-} Check current lag}
\KeywordTok{SELECT}
\NormalTok{    NAME,}
\NormalTok{    TARGET\_LAG,}
\NormalTok{    SCHEDULING\_STATE,}
\NormalTok{    DATA\_TIMESTAMP,}
\NormalTok{    TIMESTAMPDIFF(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}minute\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, DATA\_TIMESTAMP, }\FunctionTok{CURRENT\_TIMESTAMP}\NormalTok{()) }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ LAG\_MINUTES}
\KeywordTok{FROM} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLES())}
\KeywordTok{WHERE}\NormalTok{ DATABASE\_NAME }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\textquotesingle{}}
  \KeywordTok{AND}\NormalTok{ SCHEMA\_NAME }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{manual-refresh-python-api}{%
\subsection{Manual refresh (Python
API)}\label{manual-refresh-python-api}}

To trigger a refresh outside the scheduled \texttt{refresh\_freq}, use
the registered FeatureView object with
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/developer-guide/snowflake-ml/feature-store/overview}{\texttt{refresh\_feature\_view}}
(see also Chapter 6 backfill patterns):

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.get\_feature\_view(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}\NormalTok{, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{fs.refresh\_feature\_view(fv)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{alerting-for-stale-features}{%
\subsection{Alerting for Stale
Features}\label{alerting-for-stale-features}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Create alert for stale features (\textgreater{}60 min lag)}
\KeywordTok{CREATE}\NormalTok{ ALERT feature\_staleness\_alert}
\NormalTok{  WAREHOUSE }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FS\_DEV\_WH}
\NormalTok{  SCHEDULE }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}USING CRON 0 * * * * UTC\textquotesingle{}}
  \ControlFlowTok{IF}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{EXISTS}\NormalTok{ (}
    \KeywordTok{SELECT} \OperatorTok{*}
    \KeywordTok{FROM} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLES())}
    \KeywordTok{WHERE}\NormalTok{ DATABASE\_NAME }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\textquotesingle{}}
      \KeywordTok{AND}\NormalTok{ SCHEMA\_NAME }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\textquotesingle{}}
      \KeywordTok{AND}\NormalTok{ TIMESTAMPDIFF(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}minute\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, DATA\_TIMESTAMP, }\FunctionTok{CURRENT\_TIMESTAMP}\NormalTok{()) }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}} \DecValTok{60}
\NormalTok{  ))}
  \ControlFlowTok{THEN}
    \KeywordTok{CALL}\NormalTok{ SYSTEM$SEND\_EMAIL(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}ml{-}alerts@company.com\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Stale Features\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Alert\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{);}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{online-feature-table-oft-monitoring}{%
\section{Online Feature Table (OFT)
Monitoring}\label{online-feature-table-oft-monitoring}}

For \textbf{online feature tables} (hybrid tables), use:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Refresh history:}
  \href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/sql-reference/functions/online-feature-table-refresh-history}{\texttt{ONLINE\_FEATURE\_TABLE\_REFRESH\_HISTORY}}
  ---
  \texttt{TABLE(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.ONLINE\_FEATURE\_TABLE\_REFRESH\_HISTORY(...))}.
\item
  \textbf{Storage:}
  \href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/sql-reference/account-usage/hybrid_tables}{\texttt{SNOWFLAKE.ACCOUNT\_USAGE.HYBRID\_TABLES}}.
\item
  \textbf{Usage:}
  \href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/sql-reference/account-usage/hybrid_table_usage_history}{\texttt{SNOWFLAKE.ACCOUNT\_USAGE.HYBRID\_TABLE\_USAGE\_HISTORY}}.
\end{enumerate}

See \href{_code/monitoring.sql}{\texttt{\_code/monitoring.sql}} for
example \texttt{ONLINE\_FEATURE\_TABLE\_REFRESH\_HISTORY} query.

\section{Feature Discovery \&

📁 \textbf{Full code:}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# List all FeatureViews}
\NormalTok{feature\_views }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.list\_feature\_views()}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(feature\_views.to\_pandas())}

\CommentTok{\# Get specific FeatureView details}
\NormalTok{fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.get\_feature\_view(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}\NormalTok{, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Name: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{fv}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{name}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Entities: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{fv}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{entities}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}

\hypertarget{sql-metadata-queries}{%
\subsection{SQL metadata queries}\label{sql-metadata-queries}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Describe FeatureView structure (example: USER order features from CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS)}
\NormalTok{DESCRIBE FEATURE }\KeywordTok{VIEW}\NormalTok{ USER\_ORDER\_FV$V01;}

\CommentTok{{-}{-} List columns for objects in the Feature Store schema}
\KeywordTok{SELECT}
\NormalTok{    TABLE\_NAME }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_VIEW,}
\NormalTok{    COLUMN\_NAME }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ FEATURE,}
\NormalTok{    DATA\_TYPE,}
    \KeywordTok{COMMENT}
\KeywordTok{FROM}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.}\KeywordTok{COLUMNS}
\KeywordTok{WHERE}\NormalTok{ TABLE\_SCHEMA }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{searching-columns-without-sql-injection}{%
\subsection{Searching columns without SQL
injection}\label{searching-columns-without-sql-injection}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/discovery.py}{\texttt{\_code/discovery.py}} ---
\texttt{search\_feature\_columns()}
\end{quote}

Do \textbf{not} build \texttt{INFORMATION\_SCHEMA} SQL with f-strings
from user input. Prefer Snowpark \textbf{DataFrame filters} (literals
via \texttt{lit}, \texttt{lower} + \texttt{like} for case-insensitive
search) or validated identifiers. Example API:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.snowpark }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ Session}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ discovery }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ search\_feature\_columns}

\NormalTok{rows }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ search\_feature\_columns(session, }\StringTok{"ORDER"}\NormalTok{, limit}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{50}\NormalTok{)}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ r }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ rows:}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(r[}\StringTok{"FEATURE\_VIEW"}\NormalTok{], r[}\StringTok{"FEATURE\_NAME"}\NormalTok{], r[}\StringTok{"DESCRIPTION"}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}
