\hypertarget{data-quality-monitoring}{%
\section{Data Quality Monitoring}\label{data-quality-monitoring}}

\hypertarget{data-metric-functions-dmfs}{%
\subsection{Data Metric Functions
(DMFs)}\label{data-metric-functions-dmfs}}

Snowflake \textbf{system} DMFs (for example
\texttt{SNOWFLAKE.CORE.NULL\_COUNT}, \texttt{NULL\_PERCENT},
\texttt{ROW\_COUNT}) are documented under
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/sql-reference/functions-data-metric}{Data
metric functions}. Overview:
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/user-guide/data-quality-intro}{Introduction
to data quality checks}.

\textbf{Custom} DMFs must declare \textbf{\texttt{RETURNS\ NUMBER}} (not
\texttt{DECIMAL}); associate them with \textbf{\texttt{ALTER\ TABLE}} /
\textbf{\texttt{ALTER\ VIEW}} using
\texttt{ADD\ DATA\ METRIC\ FUNCTION}, and set schedules with
\texttt{SET\ DATA\_METRIC\_SCHEDULE}
(\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/user-guide/data-quality-working}{working
with DMFs in SQL}).

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Custom DMF: null rate for a string column (RETURNS NUMBER per CREATE DATA METRIC FUNCTION)}
\KeywordTok{CREATE} \KeywordTok{OR} \KeywordTok{REPLACE} \KeywordTok{DATA}\NormalTok{ METRIC }\KeywordTok{FUNCTION}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE.NULL\_RATE\_STRING(}
\NormalTok{  t }\KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{(col }\DataTypeTok{VARCHAR}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{RETURNS }\DataTypeTok{NUMBER}
\NormalTok{LANGUAGE SQL}
\KeywordTok{AS}
\NormalTok{$$}
  \KeywordTok{SELECT} \FunctionTok{COALESCE}\NormalTok{(}
    \FunctionTok{SUM}\NormalTok{(IFF(col }\KeywordTok{IS} \KeywordTok{NULL}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{)) }\OperatorTok{/} \FunctionTok{NULLIF}\NormalTok{(}\FunctionTok{COUNT}\NormalTok{(}\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{), }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{),}
    \DecValTok{0}
\NormalTok{  ):}\CharTok{:NUMBER}
  \KeywordTok{FROM}\NormalTok{ t}
\NormalTok{$$;}

\CommentTok{{-}{-} Prefer system DMF when it fits — e.g. NULL\_COUNT on a feature column}
\KeywordTok{ALTER} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE.}\OtherTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV$V01"}
  \KeywordTok{ADD} \KeywordTok{DATA}\NormalTok{ METRIC }\KeywordTok{FUNCTION}\NormalTok{ SNOWFLAKE.CORE.NULL\_COUNT }\KeywordTok{ON}\NormalTok{ (USER\_ID);}

\KeywordTok{ALTER} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE.}\OtherTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV$V01"}
  \KeywordTok{SET}\NormalTok{ DATA\_METRIC\_SCHEDULE }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}USING CRON 0 * * * * UTC\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Dynamic tables support DMFs as table objects; use
\textbf{\texttt{ALTER\ TABLE}} with the fully qualified dynamic table
name (quote the identifier if it contains \texttt{\$}).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{feature-store-health-monitoring-1}{%
\section{Feature Store Health
Monitoring}\label{feature-store-health-monitoring-1}}

\hypertarget{key-metrics}{%
\subsection{Key Metrics}\label{key-metrics}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Feature Store health dashboard query}
\KeywordTok{WITH}\NormalTok{ fv\_health }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ (}
    \KeywordTok{SELECT}
\NormalTok{        NAME,}
\NormalTok{        SCHEDULING\_STATE,}
\NormalTok{        TIMESTAMPDIFF(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}minute\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, DATA\_TIMESTAMP, }\FunctionTok{CURRENT\_TIMESTAMP}\NormalTok{()) }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ LAG\_MINUTES,}
        \ControlFlowTok{CASE}
            \ControlFlowTok{WHEN}\NormalTok{ SCHEDULING\_STATE }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}RUNNING\textquotesingle{}}
                 \KeywordTok{AND}\NormalTok{ TIMESTAMPDIFF(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}minute\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, DATA\_TIMESTAMP, }\FunctionTok{CURRENT\_TIMESTAMP}\NormalTok{()) }\OperatorTok{\textless{}} \DecValTok{60} \ControlFlowTok{THEN} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}HEALTHY\textquotesingle{}}
            \ControlFlowTok{WHEN}\NormalTok{ TIMESTAMPDIFF(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}minute\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, DATA\_TIMESTAMP, }\FunctionTok{CURRENT\_TIMESTAMP}\NormalTok{()) }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}=} \DecValTok{60} \ControlFlowTok{THEN} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}STALE\textquotesingle{}}
            \ControlFlowTok{ELSE} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}WARNING\textquotesingle{}}
        \ControlFlowTok{END} \KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ STATUS}
    \KeywordTok{FROM} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{(INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLES())}
    \KeywordTok{WHERE}\NormalTok{ DATABASE\_NAME }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\textquotesingle{}}
      \KeywordTok{AND}\NormalTok{ SCHEMA\_NAME }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}FEATURE\_STORE\textquotesingle{}}
\NormalTok{)}
\KeywordTok{SELECT}
\NormalTok{    STATUS,}
    \FunctionTok{COUNT}\NormalTok{(}\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{) }\KeywordTok{AS} \FunctionTok{COUNT}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    ARRAY\_AGG(NAME) }\KeywordTok{AS}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_VIEWS}
\KeywordTok{FROM}\NormalTok{ fv\_health}
\KeywordTok{GROUP} \KeywordTok{BY}\NormalTok{ STATUS;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-9}{%
\section{Best Practices}\label{best-practices-9}}

\hypertarget{monitor-proactively}{%
\subsection{1. Monitor Proactively}\label{monitor-proactively}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Set up alerts before issues impact users}
\KeywordTok{CREATE}\NormalTok{ ALERT }\OperatorTok{..}\NormalTok{.}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{track-lineage}{%
\subsection{2. Track Lineage}\label{track-lineage}}

Document feature sources and consumers:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    Sources: FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS}
\StringTok{    Consumers: churn\_model\_v1, ltv\_model\_v2}
\StringTok{    Owner: ml{-}platform@company.com}
\StringTok{    """}\NormalTok{,}
    \CommentTok{\# ...}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{regular-health-checks}{%
\subsection{3. Regular Health Checks}\label{regular-health-checks}}

Schedule weekly reviews:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  FeatureView refresh status
\item
  Data quality metrics
\item
  Compute costs
\item
  Unused features
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-9}{%
\section{Common Pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-9}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-no-monitoring}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: No Monitoring}\label{pitfall-1-no-monitoring}}

\textbf{Problem}: Issues discovered when models fail.

\textbf{Solution}: Implement proactive alerting.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-missing-lineage}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Missing
Lineage}\label{pitfall-2-missing-lineage}}

\textbf{Problem}: Can't trace feature issues to source.

\textbf{Solution}: Use OBJECT\_DEPENDENCIES and document.

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-stale-features}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: Stale
Features}\label{pitfall-3-stale-features}}

\textbf{Problem}: Models using outdated features.

\textbf{Solution}: Monitor lag and set appropriate refresh.

\hypertarget{pitfall-4-non-existent-information_schema-views}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 4: Non-existent INFORMATION\_SCHEMA
views}\label{pitfall-4-non-existent-information_schema-views}}

\textbf{Problem}: Queries fail or docs drift when assuming
\texttt{INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.MODELS} / \texttt{MODEL\_DATASETS} /
\texttt{DATASET\_FEATURE\_VIEWS}.

\textbf{Solution}: Use \texttt{COLUMNS} / \texttt{TABLES} /
\texttt{VIEWS}, Dynamic Table functions, \texttt{MODEL\_VERSIONS}, and
the Feature Store Python API as in this chapter.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-10}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-10}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4286}}

\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright

\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Implementation
\end{minipage} \\

\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Refresh Monitoring} &
\texttt{INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.DYNAMIC\_TABLE\_REFRESH\_HISTORY},
\texttt{DYNAMIC\_TABLES} \\
\textbf{Manual refresh} & \texttt{fs.refresh\_feature\_view(fv)} \\

\texttt{ONLINE\_FEATURE\_TABLE\_REFRESH\_HISTORY},
\texttt{HYBRID\_TABLES}, \texttt{HYBRID\_TABLE\_USAGE\_HISTORY} \\

\texttt{DESCRIBE\ FEATURE\ VIEW},

\hypertarget{next-steps-11}{%
\section{Next Steps}\label{next-steps-11}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{advanced-patterns}{Chapter 12: Advanced
Patterns} to learn about streaming, multi-Feature Store, and CI/CD
patterns.

\hypertarget{advanced-patterns}{%
\chapter{Advanced Patterns}\label{advanced-patterns}}

Streaming, multi-Feature Store, CI/CD, testing, and advanced
architectures

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-12}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-12}}

This chapter covers advanced Feature Store patterns for enterprise-scale
deployments, including streaming features, multi-Feature Store
architectures, CI/CD integration, \textbf{testing strategies},
\textbf{multi-region and DR considerations}, and complex use cases.

Examples follow the \textbf{clickstream} sample layout: database
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO}, Feature Store schema
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE}, source schema \texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA},
warehouse \texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}, and tables such as \texttt{EVENTS},
\texttt{SESSIONS}, \texttt{ORDERS}, \texttt{USERS}, and
\texttt{PRODUCTS}. Register FeatureViews with version strings in
\textbf{\texttt{V01}} format (for example \texttt{version="V01"}).
Prefer aggregate column suffixes such as \texttt{\_CNT}, \texttt{\_SUM},
\texttt{\_AVG}, timestamp columns ending in \texttt{\_TS}, boolean
prefixes \texttt{IS\_}, and monetary fields such as \texttt{TOTAL\_AMT}.

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-11}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-11}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Design streaming feature architectures and interpret platform roadmap
  status
\item
  Implement multi-Feature Store patterns and outline multi-region
  concerns
\item
  Integrate Feature Store with CI/CD pipelines
\item
  Apply structured testing: unit logic, PIT correctness, and schema
  validation
\item
  Handle complex entity relationships
\item
  Optimize for large-scale deployments
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{platform-capabilities-and-preview-status-march-2026}{%
\section{Platform capabilities and preview status (March
2026)}\label{platform-capabilities-and-preview-status-march-2026}}

Several capabilities were previously described as \textbf{private
preview} with general availability (GA) expected around \textbf{March
2026}. As of \textbf{late March 2026}, treat the following as
\textbf{may be GA or in public preview depending on region and
account}---always confirm in
\href{https://docs.snowflake.com/en/release-notes/new-features}{Snowflake
release notes} and your account's feature bundle before planning
production work.

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.6000}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4000}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Capability
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Notes
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{RollupConfig} (hierarchical aggregations) & Verify current
availability; API names may evolve. \\
\textbf{Time-aggregated FeatureViews} (Temporal Aggregation /
\texttt{Feature} class) & Same guidance---confirm preview vs GA in
documentation. \\
\textbf{Feature tiling} & Performance optimization for windowed
aggregates; confirm support status. \\
\textbf{Streaming FeatureViews} & Rollout may extend into
\textbf{March--April 2026}; near-term options remain short Dynamic Table
refresh or Snowpipe → staging → View-based FVs. \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{Note}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

graduate---timelines shift. Re-check Snowflake documentation before
committing architecture.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{multi-region-and-disaster-recovery}{%
\section{Multi-region and disaster
recovery}\label{multi-region-and-disaster-recovery}}

Enterprise deployments often require \textbf{multiple regions} and
\textbf{disaster recovery (DR)}. At a high level:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Database replication:} Snowflake \textbf{database replication}
  can replicate databases that hold Feature Store schemas (for example
  \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO} / \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE}), subject to
  replication rules, edition, and licensing.
\item
  \textbf{Feature definitions:} \textbf{FeatureViews} and related
  metadata can be promoted via \textbf{clone}, \textbf{CI/CD redeploy
  from repository definitions}, or replication-oriented workflows;
  choose based on whether secondary regions must own writable primaries
  or read-only copies.
\item
  \textbf{Online Feature Tables:} \textbf{Online Feature Tables require
  separate provisioning per region} (and separate serving paths);
  replication alone does not replace regional online stores or cache
  layers.
\item
  \textbf{Scope:} \textbf{Full multi-region and DR planning is beyond
  this guide.} Use current Snowflake documentation on replication,
  failover, and business continuity, and involve your platform team for
  RPO/RTO targets.
\end{itemize}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Structured notes:}
\href{_code/multi_region_dr.py}{\texttt{\_code/multi\_region\_dr.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

│                                                                         │
│  ┌─────────────────┐  ┌─────────────────┐  ┌─────────────────┐          │

│  │                 │  │                 │  │                 │          │
│  │ CAMPAIGN_FV     │  │ TRANSACTION_FV  │  │ USER_BASE_FV    │          │
│  │ SEGMENT_FV      │  │ DEVICE_FV       │  │ PRODUCT_FV      │          │
│  └────────┬────────┘  └────────┬────────┘  └────────┬────────┘          │
│           │                    │                    │                   │
│           └────────────────────┼────────────────────┘                   │
│                                │                                        │
│                                ▼                                        │
│                    ┌─────────────────────┐                              │
│                    │   Cross-Domain ML   │                              │
│                    │   (Fraud + Marketing│                              │
│                    │    + Base Features) │                              │
│                    └─────────────────────┘                              │
│                                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{testing-strategies}{%
\section{Testing strategies}\label{testing-strategies}}

Reliable Feature Store operations depend on tests that go beyond ``the
job finished.'' This guide's repository includes a detailed plan in
\textbf{\texttt{\_internal\_development/TESTING\_STRATEGY.md}} (pytest,
Quarto execution, CI). The patterns below are the minimum bar for
advanced deployments.

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Helpers and canonical constants:}
\href{_code/testing_strategies.py}{\texttt{\_code/testing\_strategies.py}}
\end{quote}

\hypertarget{unit-tests-for-feature-logic}{%
\subsection{1. Unit tests for feature
logic}\label{unit-tests-for-feature-logic}}

Test \textbf{DataFrame or Snowpark transformations in isolation}: build
small fixtures (or sampled tables from
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA}), run the same logic
your FeatureView uses, and assert \textbf{row counts, column names, and
values}---including naming conventions (\texttt{ORDER\_CNT},
\texttt{TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM}, \texttt{LAST\_ORDER\_TS}).

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pytest}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.snowpark.functions }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ col}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ test\_user\_order\_aggregates\_schema\_and\_totals(order\_stats\_df):}
    \CommentTok{"""order\_stats\_df: result of GROUP BY USER\_ID on ORDERS{-}like input."""}
\NormalTok{    cols }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ order\_stats\_df.columns}
    \ControlFlowTok{assert} \StringTok{"USER\_ID"} \KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ cols}
    \ControlFlowTok{assert} \StringTok{"ORDER\_CNT"} \KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ cols}
    \ControlFlowTok{assert} \StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM"} \KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ cols}
\NormalTok{    row }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ order\_stats\_df.}\BuiltInTok{filter}\NormalTok{(col(}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{) }\OperatorTok{==} \DecValTok{42}\NormalTok{).collect()}
    \ControlFlowTok{assert}\NormalTok{ row[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{][}\StringTok{"ORDER\_CNT"}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{==} \DecValTok{3}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{pit-correctness-tests-no-future-leakage}{%
\subsection{2. PIT correctness tests (no future
leakage)}\label{pit-correctness-tests-no-future-leakage}}

After \texttt{generate\_dataset}, assert that \textbf{feature view
timestamps never exceed} the spine's event time for the same row.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.snowpark.functions }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ col}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ test\_no\_future\_leakage(fs, test\_spine, fv):}
\NormalTok{    dataset }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fs.generate\_dataset(}
\NormalTok{        spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{test\_spine,}
\NormalTok{        features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[fv],}
\NormalTok{        spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"EVENT\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        include\_feature\_view\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    )}
\NormalTok{    df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ dataset.read.to\_snowpark\_dataframe()}
    \ControlFlowTok{assert}\NormalTok{ df.}\BuiltInTok{filter}\NormalTok{(col(}\StringTok{"FV\_TS"}\NormalTok{) }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}}\NormalTok{ col(}\StringTok{"EVENT\_TS"}\NormalTok{)).count() }\OperatorTok{==} \DecValTok{0}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Extend this pattern with \textbf{spot checks} on known entities and
times (golden spines) and with \textbf{multiple FeatureViews} joined on
the same spine.

\hypertarget{schema-validation}{%
\subsection{3. Schema validation}\label{schema-validation}}

Before or after \texttt{register\_feature\_view}, assert that outputs
match an \textbf{expected schema}: column set, types, and (where your
contracts require it) order. Options include:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{DESCRIBE\ FEATURE\ VIEW\ MY\_FV\$V01} compared to a checked-in
  manifest
\item
  Queries against \texttt{INFORMATION\_SCHEMA.COLUMNS} for
  \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE}
\item
  API metadata from
  \texttt{fs.get\_feature\_view(name="USER\_ORDER\_FV",\ version="V01")}
  where available
\end{itemize}

Keep \textbf{one manifest} (YAML/JSON) as the source of truth shared by
registration scripts and tests.

\hypertarget{freshness-and-quality-hooks}{%
\subsection{4. Freshness and quality
hooks}\label{freshness-and-quality-hooks}}

Combine the above with \textbf{operational checks} (lag, null rates) as
in Chapter 11---those belong in monitoring as well as in \textbf{smoke
tests} after deploy.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ test\_feature\_freshness():}
\NormalTok{    lag }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ get\_feature\_lag(}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}\NormalTok{)}
    \ControlFlowTok{assert}\NormalTok{ lag }\OperatorTok{\textless{}}\NormalTok{ timedelta(hours}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{)}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ test\_feature\_quality():}
\NormalTok{    null\_rate }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ get\_null\_rate(}\StringTok{"USER\_ORDER\_FV"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM"}\NormalTok{)}
    \ControlFlowTok{assert}\NormalTok{ null\_rate }\OperatorTok{\textless{}} \FloatTok{0.01}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-10}{%
\section{Best practices}\label{best-practices-10}}

\hypertarget{design-for-scale}{%
\subsection{1. Design for scale}\label{design-for-scale}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Partition features by update frequency (version V01 per registration)}
\NormalTok{fast\_features\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"FAST\_FEATURES\_FV"}\NormalTok{, refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"5 minutes"}\NormalTok{, ...)}
\NormalTok{slow\_features\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SLOW\_FEATURES\_FV"}\NormalTok{, refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 day"}\NormalTok{, ...)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{manage-complexity}{%
\subsection{2. Manage complexity}\label{manage-complexity}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Document feature dependencies (clickstream sources)}
\FunctionTok{features}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{  }\FunctionTok{USER\_ORDER\_FV}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{depends\_on}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.USERS}
\AttributeTok{    }\FunctionTok{consumers}\KeywordTok{:}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ churn\_model}
\AttributeTok{      }\KeywordTok{{-}}\AttributeTok{ ltv\_model}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{automate-testing-in-ci}{%
\subsection{3. Automate testing in CI}\label{automate-testing-in-ci}}

Run \textbf{pytest} (unit + PIT + schema contracts) on every change to
feature definitions; gate deploys on green builds. See \textbf{Testing
strategies} above and
\texttt{\_internal\_development/TESTING\_STRATEGY.md}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-10}{%
\section{Common pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-10}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-over-engineering}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1:
Over-engineering}\label{pitfall-1-over-engineering}}

\textbf{Problem}: Complex architecture for simple use case.

\textbf{Solution}: Start simple, add complexity as needed.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-inconsistent-patterns}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Inconsistent
patterns}\label{pitfall-2-inconsistent-patterns}}

\textbf{Problem}: Each team implements features differently.

\textbf{Solution}: Establish organization-wide standards (including
\texttt{V01} versioning and clickstream FQNs).

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-no-testing}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: No testing}\label{pitfall-3-no-testing}}

\textbf{Problem}: Feature issues discovered in production.

\textbf{Solution}: CI/CD with \textbf{unit}, \textbf{PIT}, and
\textbf{schema} tests, plus operational freshness checks.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-11}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-11}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4737}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5263}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Pattern
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Use Case
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Streaming / low latency} & Near real-time features (Dynamic
Table, staging, or native streaming when available) \\
\textbf{Multi-FS} & Domain isolation \\
\textbf{Multi-region / DR} & Replication, clones, per-region online
tables \\
\textbf{External FV} & dbt / Iceberg integration \\
\textbf{CI/CD} & Automated deployments with \texttt{V01} versions \\
\textbf{Testing} & Unit logic, PIT leakage checks, schema contracts \\
\textbf{Object features} & Embeddings, JSON \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{next-steps-12}{%
\section{Next steps}\label{next-steps-12}}

Continue to \protect\hyperlink{migration-guide}{Chapter 13: Migration
Guide} for guidance on migrating from other Feature Store platforms.

\hypertarget{migration-guide}{%
\chapter{Migration Guide}\label{migration-guide}}

Migrating to Snowflake Feature Store from other platforms

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-13}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-13}}

This chapter provides guidance for teams migrating to Snowflake Feature
Store from other platforms, \textbf{primarily Tecton}. It covers
terminology mapping, migration strategies, and common patterns.

Examples follow the \textbf{clickstream} sample layout: database
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO}, Feature Store schema
\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE}, source schema \texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA}
(tables such as \texttt{EVENTS}, \texttt{SESSIONS}, \texttt{ORDERS},
\texttt{USERS}, \texttt{PRODUCTS}), warehouse \texttt{FS\_DEV\_WH}.
Register FeatureViews with version strings in \textbf{\texttt{V01}}
format (for example
\texttt{fs.register\_feature\_view(...,\ version="V01")}).

\hypertarget{learning-objectives-12}{%
\section{Learning Objectives}\label{learning-objectives-12}}

After completing this chapter, you will be able to:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Map terminology from other Feature Stores to Snowflake
\item
  Plan a phased migration approach
\item
  Migrate feature definitions and pipelines
\item
  Validate migrated features
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{why-migrate-to-snowflake-feature-store}{%
\section{Why Migrate to Snowflake Feature
Store?}\label{why-migrate-to-snowflake-feature-store}}

\hypertarget{key-benefits}{%
\subsection{Key Benefits}\label{key-benefits}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4091}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5909}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Benefit
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Unified Platform} & Features, training, inference all in
Snowflake \\
\textbf{Native Integration} & Uses Snowflake objects (DTs, Views, Hybrid
Tables) \\
\textbf{Zero Infrastructure} & No separate serving infrastructure
needed \\
\textbf{Enterprise Security} & Inherits Snowflake RBAC and governance \\
\textbf{Cost Efficiency} & No data movement, unified compute \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{sec-terminology}{%
\section{Terminology Mapping}\label{sec-terminology}}

\hypertarget{tecton-snowflake}{%
\subsection{Tecton → Snowflake}\label{tecton-snowflake}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/terminology_mapping.py}{\texttt{\_code/terminology\_mapping.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3077}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4231}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2692}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Tecton
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Snowflake
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Notes
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Feature View & FeatureView & Registered with
\texttt{register\_feature\_view}; use \texttt{version="V01"} (or
\texttt{V02}, \ldots) \\
Entity & Entity & Same concept; join keys align with spine columns \\
Batch Feature View & FeatureView (Dynamic Table) & Set
\texttt{refresh\_freq} to a \textbf{period} (e.g.~\texttt{"1\ hour"}) or
\textbf{CRON} string \\
On-Demand Feature View & FeatureView (View) & Omit
\texttt{refresh\_freq} or set \texttt{refresh\_freq=None}; query-time
computation \\
Feature Service & \texttt{generate\_training\_set()} /
\texttt{generate\_dataset()} & No separate service object: pass spine +
list of FeatureViews (see Chapter 10) \\
Online Store & Online Feature Table (Hybrid Table) & Enable with
\texttt{OnlineConfig}; freshness via \texttt{target\_lag} \\
Offline Store & Feature Store schema &
e.g.~\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.FEATURE\_STORE}; materialized batch
features live in Dynamic Tables there \\
Data Source & Source table or view &
e.g.~\texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS} \\
Transformation & FeatureView query (\texttt{feature\_df}) & Snowpark
DataFrame / SQL vs Tecton Python decorators \\
Backfill & \texttt{fs.refresh\_feature\_view(fv)} & Triggers refresh
outside the scheduled \texttt{refresh\_freq} \\
TTL & \texttt{refresh\_freq} / \texttt{target\_lag} & \textbf{Offline}
lag ↔ Dynamic Table \texttt{refresh\_freq}; \textbf{online} freshness ↔
\texttt{OnlineConfig.target\_lag} (not a single global TTL) \\
\texttt{get\_historical\_features} & \texttt{generate\_training\_set()}
/ \texttt{generate\_dataset()} & Snowpark DataFrame vs versioned Dataset
(Parquet); same PIT semantics \\
\texttt{get\_online\_features} & \texttt{get\_online\_features} &
Retrieve from Online Feature Table \\
Spine & Spine DataFrame & Entity keys + PIT timestamp column passed as
\texttt{spine\_timestamp\_col} \\
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{feast-snowflake-abbreviated}{%
\subsection{Feast → Snowflake
(abbreviated)}\label{feast-snowflake-abbreviated}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3889}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.6111}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Feast
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Snowflake
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Feature Store (registry) & Feature Store schema + platform metadata \\
Feature View & FeatureView \\
Online Store & Online Feature Table (Hybrid Table) \\
Offline Store & Feature Store schema \\
Feature Service & \texttt{generate\_training\_set()} /
\texttt{generate\_dataset()} \\
\texttt{get\_historical\_features} & \texttt{generate\_training\_set()}
/ \texttt{generate\_dataset()} \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{migration-approach}{%
\section{Migration Approach}\label{migration-approach}}

\hypertarget{three-phase-migration}{%
\subsection{Three-Phase Migration}\label{three-phase-migration}}

\begin{verbatim}
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                        MIGRATION WORKFLOW                               │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                         │
│  Phase 1: ASSESSMENT          Phase 2: MIGRATION       Phase 3: VALID  │
│  ┌───────────────────┐       ┌─────────────────────┐   ┌────────────┐  │
│  │                   │       │                     │   │            │  │
│  │ • Inventory       │       │ • Recreate entities │   │ • Compare  │  │
│  │   existing        │──────▶│ • Port feature defs │──▶│   outputs  │  │
│  │   features        │       │ • Setup pipelines   │   │ • Validate │  │
│  │ • Map terminology │       │ • Migrate consumers │   │   PIT      │  │
│  │ • Plan phases     │       │                     │   │ • Cutover  │  │
│  │                   │       │                     │   │            │  │
│  └───────────────────┘       └─────────────────────┘   └────────────┘  │
│                                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{phase-1-assessment}{%
\subsection{Phase 1: Assessment}\label{phase-1-assessment}}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Inventory existing features}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    List all Feature Views/Groups
  \item
    Document entities and join keys
  \item
    Identify refresh frequencies (map to \texttt{refresh\_freq} /
    \texttt{target\_lag})
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Map to Snowflake concepts}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Use terminology mapping table
  \item
    Identify gaps or differences
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Plan migration order}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Start with simple features
  \item
    Group by model dependency
  \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\hypertarget{phase-2-migration}{%
\subsection{Phase 2: Migration}\label{phase-2-migration}}

\begin{quote}
📁 \textbf{Full code:}
\href{_code/migration_utils.py}{\texttt{\_code/migration\_utils.py}}
\end{quote}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Example: Migrating a Tecton batch Feature View to Snowflake (clickstream ORDERS)}

\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.ml.feature\_store }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ FeatureStore, FeatureView, Entity}

\CommentTok{\# Tecton (original)}
\CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{@batch\_feature\_view(}
\CommentTok{    entities=[user\_entity],}
\CommentTok{    feature\_table=user\_features,}
\CommentTok{    schedule=timedelta(hours=1),}
\CommentTok{)}
\CommentTok{def user\_purchase\_fv(user\_txns):}
\CommentTok{    return user\_txns.groupby(\textquotesingle{}USER\_ID\textquotesingle{}).agg(}
\CommentTok{        total\_spend=(\textquotesingle{}AMOUNT\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}sum\textquotesingle{}),}
\CommentTok{        order\_count=(\textquotesingle{}ORDER\_ID\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}count\textquotesingle{}),}
\CommentTok{    )}
\CommentTok{"""}

\CommentTok{\# Snowflake (migrated) — FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS uses TOTAL\_AMT, ORDER\_ID, ORDER\_TS}
\NormalTok{user\_purchase\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ session.sql(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    SELECT}
\StringTok{        USER\_ID,}
\StringTok{        SUM(TOTAL\_AMT) AS ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM,}
\StringTok{        COUNT(ORDER\_ID) AS ORDER\_CNT,}
\StringTok{        MAX(ORDER\_TS) AS LAST\_ORDER\_TS}
\StringTok{    FROM FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS}
\StringTok{    GROUP BY USER\_ID}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{user\_purchase\_fv }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ FeatureView(}
\NormalTok{    name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER\_PURCHASE\_FV"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    entities}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_entity],}
\NormalTok{    feature\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_purchase\_df,}
\NormalTok{    timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LAST\_ORDER\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    refresh\_freq}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"1 hour"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    desc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"USER purchase aggregates from CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.ORDERS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{fs.register\_feature\_view(feature\_view}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{user\_purchase\_fv, version}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"V01"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{phase-3-validation}{%
\subsection{Phase 3: Validation}\label{phase-3-validation}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ snowflake.snowpark }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ functions }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ F}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ validate\_migration(}
\NormalTok{    source\_features,}
\NormalTok{    snowflake\_features,}
\NormalTok{    entity\_cols: }\BuiltInTok{list}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{) }\OperatorTok{{-}\textgreater{}} \BuiltInTok{dict}\NormalTok{:}
    \CommentTok{"""Compare features between source platform and Snowflake (Snowpark DataFrames)."""}

\NormalTok{    comparison }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ source\_features.join(}
\NormalTok{        snowflake\_features,}
\NormalTok{        on}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{entity\_cols,}
\NormalTok{        how}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"full\_outer"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    )}

\NormalTok{    mismatches }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ comparison.}\BuiltInTok{filter}\NormalTok{(}
\NormalTok{        F.col(}\StringTok{"source\_ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM"}\NormalTok{) }\OperatorTok{!=}\NormalTok{ F.col(}\StringTok{"sf\_ORDER\_TOTAL\_AMT\_SUM"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    ).count()}

\NormalTok{    total }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ comparison.count()}
    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ \{}
        \StringTok{"total\_rows"}\NormalTok{: total,}
        \StringTok{"mismatches"}\NormalTok{: mismatches,}
        \StringTok{"match\_rate"}\NormalTok{: (}\DecValTok{1} \OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{ mismatches }\OperatorTok{/}\NormalTok{ total) }\OperatorTok{*} \DecValTok{100} \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ total }\ControlFlowTok{else} \FloatTok{0.0}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    \}}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{platform-specific-guides}{%
\section{Platform-Specific Guides}\label{platform-specific-guides}}

\hypertarget{tecton-migration}{%
\subsection{Tecton Migration}\label{tecton-migration}}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{Priority}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

Tecton migration is prioritized given Databricks Online Tables EOL.

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Key differences to handle:}
\CommentTok{\# 1. Feature definitions use SQL/Snowpark (feature\_df) vs Tecton Python transformations}
\CommentTok{\# 2. Online serving uses Hybrid Tables + OnlineConfig.target\_lag vs Tecton\textquotesingle{}s online store}
\CommentTok{\# 3. Offline scheduling uses FeatureView refresh\_freq vs Tecton\textquotesingle{}s schedule parameter}
\CommentTok{\# 4. Backfill / ad{-}hoc refresh: fs.refresh\_feature\_view(fv)}
\CommentTok{\# 5. Training data: fs.generate\_training\_set() (Snowpark DF) or fs.generate\_dataset() (ML Dataset)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{feast-migration}{%
\subsection{Feast Migration}\label{feast-migration}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Key differences:}
\CommentTok{\# 1. Feature Store is a Snowflake schema + platform objects vs external registry + plugins}
\CommentTok{\# 2. Online store is Online Feature Table (Hybrid Table) vs Redis/DynamoDB}
\CommentTok{\# 3. No separate Feature Service — use generate\_training\_set() / generate\_dataset() with spine + FVs}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{best-practices-11}{%
\section{Best Practices}\label{best-practices-11}}

\hypertarget{migrate-incrementally}{%
\subsection{1. Migrate Incrementally}\label{migrate-incrementally}}

\begin{verbatim}
Week 1: Entities + 2-3 simple FeatureViews
Week 2: Remaining batch features
Week 3: Online serving setup
Week 4: Consumer cutover
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{run-in-parallel}{%
\subsection{2. Run in Parallel}\label{run-in-parallel}}

Operate both systems during migration:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Historical / training: compare Snowpark path (generate\_training\_set) and Dataset path (generate\_dataset) as needed}
\NormalTok{source\_features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ tecton\_client.get\_historical\_features(...)}
\NormalTok{sf\_training\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ snowflake\_fs.generate\_training\_set(}
\NormalTok{    spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{training\_spine,}
\NormalTok{    features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_purchase\_fv],}
\NormalTok{    spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{)}
\CommentTok{\# Or: sf\_dataset = snowflake\_fs.generate\_dataset(..., version="V01") for Parquet{-}backed ML Dataset workflows}

\NormalTok{validate\_migration(source\_features, sf\_training\_df, entity\_cols}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{"USER\_ID"}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{validate-pit-correctness}{%
\subsection{3. Validate PIT
Correctness}\label{validate-pit-correctness}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Ensure point{-}in{-}time retrieval produces same results}
\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ test\_pit\_correctness(spine, source\_fs, snowflake\_fs):}
\NormalTok{    source\_result }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ source\_fs.get\_historical\_features(spine)}
\NormalTok{    sf\_df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ snowflake\_fs.generate\_training\_set(}
\NormalTok{        spine\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{spine,}
\NormalTok{        features}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[user\_purchase\_fv],}
\NormalTok{        spine\_timestamp\_col}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"SESSION\_START\_TS"}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    )}
\NormalTok{    assert\_dataframes\_equal(source\_result, sf\_df)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{common-pitfalls-11}{%
\section{Common Pitfalls}\label{common-pitfalls-11}}

\hypertarget{pitfall-1-big-bang-migration}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 1: Big Bang
Migration}\label{pitfall-1-big-bang-migration}}

\textbf{Problem}: Migrating everything at once causes extended outages.

\textbf{Solution}: Phased migration with parallel operation.

\hypertarget{pitfall-2-skipping-validation}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 2: Skipping
Validation}\label{pitfall-2-skipping-validation}}

\textbf{Problem}: Subtle differences in feature values undetected.

\textbf{Solution}: Comprehensive output comparison.

\hypertarget{pitfall-3-ignoring-timestamp-semantics}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 3: Ignoring Timestamp
Semantics}\label{pitfall-3-ignoring-timestamp-semantics}}

\textbf{Problem}: Different interpretation of event time vs.~processing
time.

\textbf{Solution}: Document and align timestamp semantics.

\hypertarget{pitfall-4-confusing-ttl-with-a-single-knob}{%
\subsection{❌ Pitfall 4: Confusing TTL with a Single
Knob}\label{pitfall-4-confusing-ttl-with-a-single-knob}}

\textbf{Problem}: Tecton TTL maps to different Snowflake controls for
offline vs online paths.

\textbf{Solution}: Set \texttt{refresh\_freq} for Dynamic Table
materialization and \texttt{OnlineConfig.target\_lag} for online sync
independently; align both with product freshness SLAs.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{summary-12}{%
\section{Summary}\label{summary-12}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3684}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.6316}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Phase
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Activities
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Assessment} & Inventory, terminology mapping, planning \\
\textbf{Migration} & Recreate entities, port definitions
(\texttt{feature\_df}), register with \texttt{V01}, setup pipelines \\
\textbf{Validation} & Compare outputs (\texttt{generate\_training\_set}
/ \texttt{generate\_dataset}), validate PIT, cutover \\
\end{longtable}

\part{Appendix A: Sample Data}

\hypertarget{sample-data-1}{%
\chapter{Sample Data}\label{sample-data-1}}

Clickstream dataset generator and public ML datasets

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-14}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-14}}

This appendix documents the sample data used throughout the Feature
Store Implementation Guide:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Clickstream Dataset} - A synthetic e-commerce dataset
  generated specifically for this guide
\item
  \textbf{Public ML Datasets} - Standard datasets (Iris, Titanic, etc.)
  for simple examples
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Recommended: Streamlit Data Manager}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

For first-time setup and interactive data management, we recommend using
the \textbf{Streamlit Data Manager} app. It provides a visual interface
for all data operations with guided workflows.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\BuiltInTok{cd}\NormalTok{ data\_manager/}
\BuiltInTok{export} \VariableTok{SNOWFLAKE\_CONNECTION\_NAME}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{your\_connection}
\ExtensionTok{streamlit}\NormalTok{ run app.py}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\textbf{\protect\hyperlink{streamlit-data-manager}{📖 Full Streamlit App
Documentation →}}

\end{tcolorbox}

\hypertarget{clickstream-dataset}{%
\section{Clickstream Dataset}\label{clickstream-dataset}}

\hypertarget{quick-start-1}{%
\subsection{Quick Start}\label{quick-start-1}}

You can manage sample data using either the \textbf{Streamlit UI}
(interactive) or \textbf{CLI tools} (scriptable).

\section{Streamlit UI (Recommended)}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\BuiltInTok{cd}\NormalTok{ data\_manager/}

\CommentTok{\# Set Snowflake connection}
\BuiltInTok{export} \VariableTok{SNOWFLAKE\_CONNECTION\_NAME}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{your\_connection}

\CommentTok{\# Launch the UI}
\ExtensionTok{streamlit}\NormalTok{ run app.py}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

The UI provides:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  📊 \textbf{Overview} - View current data status
\item
  📥 \textbf{Initial Load} - Generate and load synthetic data\\
\item
  🔄 \textbf{Incremental Generator} - Manage continuous data generation
\item
  🌿 \textbf{Development Branch} - Create sampled dev environments
\item
  📚 \textbf{Public Datasets} - Load standard ML datasets
\item
  📈 \textbf{Monitoring} - Track task and DT executions
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\protect\hyperlink{streamlit-data-manager}{See detailed
walkthrough with screenshots →}}

\section{CLI Tools}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\BuiltInTok{cd}\NormalTok{ generator/}

\CommentTok{\# Set Snowflake connection}
\BuiltInTok{export} \VariableTok{SNOWFLAKE\_CONNECTION\_NAME}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{your\_connection}

\CommentTok{\# Step 1: Initial load (scale 0.01 = \textasciitilde{}1K users)}
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ main.py }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}scale}\NormalTok{ 0.01 }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}output}\NormalTok{ snowflake}

\CommentTok{\# Step 2 (Optional): Deploy continuous generation}
\BuiltInTok{cd}\NormalTok{ snowflake\_native}
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ deploy.py }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}start}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section{Python API}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ data\_manager.core }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ DataManager}

\NormalTok{dm }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ DataManager()}
\NormalTok{dm.}\ExtensionTok{connect}\NormalTok{()}

\CommentTok{\# Initial load}
\NormalTok{result }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ dm.run\_initial\_load(scale}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.01}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Loaded: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{result}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{row\_counts}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Create dev branch}
\NormalTok{result }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ dm.create\_dev\_branch(}\StringTok{"MY\_DEV\_DB"}\NormalTok{, sample\_pct}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{required-privileges-1}{%
\subsection{Required Privileges}\label{required-privileges-1}}

The data loading scripts require specific Snowflake privileges depending
on your use case.

\hypertarget{minimum-privileges-using-existing-database}{%
\subsubsection{Minimum Privileges (Using Existing
Database)}\label{minimum-privileges-using-existing-database}}

If you have an existing database and just need to create schemas and
tables:

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Privilege & Object & Purpose \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{USAGE} & Warehouse & Execute queries \\
\texttt{USAGE} & Database & Access the database \\
\texttt{CREATE\ SCHEMA} & Database & Create CLICKSTREAM\_DATA schema \\
\texttt{CREATE\ TABLE} & Schema & Create data tables \\
\texttt{CREATE\ STAGE} & Schema & Upload Parquet files (bulk load) \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Grant minimum privileges to a role (canonical guide names shown)}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{USAGE} \KeywordTok{ON}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE FS\_DEV\_WH }\KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ my\_role;}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{USAGE} \KeywordTok{ON} \KeywordTok{DATABASE}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO }\KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ my\_role;}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{CREATE} \KeywordTok{SCHEMA} \KeywordTok{ON} \KeywordTok{DATABASE}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO }\KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ my\_role;}

\CommentTok{{-}{-} After schema creation, grant table privileges}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{ALL} \KeywordTok{ON} \KeywordTok{SCHEMA}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_DATA }\KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ my\_role;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{full-setup-creating-new-database}{%
\subsubsection{Full Setup (Creating New
Database)}\label{full-setup-creating-new-database}}

For the complete setup including database creation:

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Privilege & Object & Purpose \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{CREATE\ DATABASE} & Account & Create FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO
database \\
\texttt{USAGE} & Warehouse & Execute queries \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Grant full setup privileges}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{CREATE} \KeywordTok{DATABASE} \KeywordTok{ON} \KeywordTok{ACCOUNT} \KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ my\_role;}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{USAGE} \KeywordTok{ON}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE FS\_DEV\_WH }\KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ my\_role;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{incremental-generator-additional}{%
\subsubsection{Incremental Generator
(Additional)}\label{incremental-generator-additional}}

To deploy and run the Snowflake-native incremental generator:

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Privilege & Object & Purpose \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{CREATE\ PROCEDURE} & Schema & Create stored procedure \\
\texttt{CREATE\ TASK} & Schema & Create scheduled task \\
\texttt{EXECUTE\ TASK} & Account & Allow task execution \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Grant incremental generator privileges (admin schema for generator objects)}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{CREATE} \KeywordTok{PROCEDURE} \KeywordTok{ON} \KeywordTok{SCHEMA}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_ADMIN }\KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ my\_role;}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{CREATE}\NormalTok{ TASK }\KeywordTok{ON} \KeywordTok{SCHEMA}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_ADMIN }\KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ my\_role;}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{EXECUTE}\NormalTok{ TASK }\KeywordTok{ON} \KeywordTok{ACCOUNT} \KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ my\_role;}

\CommentTok{{-}{-} After task creation, grant operate privilege}
\KeywordTok{GRANT}\NormalTok{ OPERATE }\KeywordTok{ON}\NormalTok{ TASK incremental\_data\_task }\KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ my\_role;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Using a Custom Database}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

If you don't have \texttt{CREATE\ DATABASE} privilege, use the
\texttt{-\/-database} flag to specify an existing database:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ main.py }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}scale}\NormalTok{ 0.01 }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}database}\NormalTok{ MY\_EXISTING\_DB }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}schema}\NormalTok{ MY\_SCHEMA }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}output}\NormalTok{ snowflake}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{Recommended: Create a Dedicated Role}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

For production use, create a dedicated role with only the required
privileges:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} See Appendix B: Environment Setup for the full security model}
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Quick start: run scripts/01\_dba\_setup.sql (Appendix B)}

\CommentTok{{-}{-} Or manually create a role:}
\KeywordTok{CREATE} \KeywordTok{ROLE} \ControlFlowTok{IF} \KeywordTok{NOT} \KeywordTok{EXISTS}\NormalTok{ FS\_ADMIN\_ROLE;}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{USAGE} \KeywordTok{ON}\NormalTok{ WAREHOUSE FS\_DEV\_WH }\KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ FS\_ADMIN\_ROLE;}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{CREATE} \KeywordTok{DATABASE} \KeywordTok{ON} \KeywordTok{ACCOUNT} \KeywordTok{TO} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ FS\_ADMIN\_ROLE;}
\KeywordTok{GRANT} \KeywordTok{ROLE}\NormalTok{ FS\_ADMIN\_ROLE }\KeywordTok{TO} \FunctionTok{USER}\NormalTok{ my\_user;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\end{tcolorbox}

\hypertarget{incremental-generation}{%
\subsection{Incremental Generation}\label{incremental-generation}}

For Dynamic Table and Online Feature testing we need an incremental data
generator to show the evolution of the feature store data through
feature pipelines over time. This can be deployed using the following
SQL commands:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Start continuous generation (every minute)}
\KeywordTok{ALTER}\NormalTok{ TASK FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_ADMIN.INCREMENTAL\_DATA\_TASK }\KeywordTok{RESUME}\NormalTok{;}

\CommentTok{{-}{-} Monitor}
\KeywordTok{SELECT} \OperatorTok{*} \KeywordTok{FROM}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_ADMIN.GENERATION\_STATUS;}

\CommentTok{{-}{-} Stop when done}
\KeywordTok{ALTER}\NormalTok{ TASK FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_ADMIN.INCREMENTAL\_DATA\_TASK }\KeywordTok{SUSPEND}\NormalTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Note: Leaving these executing will continue to generate data and update
the feature store data over time, but will incur costs for the compute
resources used to generate the data. When you are done with the testing,
you can suspend the task by running the following SQL command:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{ALTER}\NormalTok{ TASK FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO.CLICKSTREAM\_ADMIN.INCREMENTAL\_DATA\_TASK }\KeywordTok{SUSPEND}\NormalTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

You can resume the task at anytime when you want to continue testing and
it will continue to generate data and update the feature store data over
time, filling in the gaps where data was not generated. The first task
iteration after a suspension will start from the last batch timestamp,
and continue to generate data and update the feature store data over
time. This initial execution will be slower than subsequent executions
as it will need to catch up and apply more data.

\hypertarget{loading-public-datasets}{%
\subsection{Loading Public Datasets}\label{loading-public-datasets}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\BuiltInTok{cd}\NormalTok{ public\_datasets/}

\CommentTok{\# List available datasets}
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ load\_datasets.py }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}list}

\CommentTok{\# Load specific dataset}
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ load\_datasets.py penguins}

\CommentTok{\# Load all datasets}
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ load\_datasets.py all}

\CommentTok{\# Full dataset (no sampling) for large datasets}
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ load\_datasets.py nyc\_taxi }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}full}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Small datasets can also be loaded inline using \texttt{FROM\ VALUES}
clauses for self-contained code snippets.

\hypertarget{development-database-subset-tool}{%
\section{Development Database Subset
Tool}\label{development-database-subset-tool}}

Create development database ``branches'' from production data with
filtered subsets using Dynamic Tables.

\hypertarget{quick-start-2}{%
\subsection{Quick Start}\label{quick-start-2}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\BuiltInTok{cd}\NormalTok{ database\_subset/}

\CommentTok{\# Create development database (10\% sample)}
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ deploy.py create }\DataTypeTok{\textbackslash{}}
    \AttributeTok{{-}{-}prod{-}db}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO }\DataTypeTok{\textbackslash{}}
    \AttributeTok{{-}{-}dev{-}db}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\_DEV }\DataTypeTok{\textbackslash{}}
    \AttributeTok{{-}{-}sample{-}pct}\NormalTok{ 10 }\DataTypeTok{\textbackslash{}}
    \AttributeTok{{-}{-}warehouse}\NormalTok{ FS\_DEV\_WH}

\CommentTok{\# Check status}
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ deploy.py status }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}dev{-}db}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\_DEV}

\CommentTok{\# Suspend Dynamic Tables (cost savings)}
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ deploy.py suspend }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}dev{-}db}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\_DEV}

\CommentTok{\# Resume Dynamic Tables}
\ExtensionTok{python}\NormalTok{ deploy.py resume }\AttributeTok{{-}{-}dev{-}db}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\_DEV}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{key-features}{%
\subsection{Key Features}\label{key-features}}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Same Object Names}: All schemas/tables have identical names
  below database level
\item
  \textbf{Environment Switching}: Change \texttt{USE\ DATABASE} to
  switch between DEV and PROD
\item
  \textbf{Real-time Sync}: Dynamic Tables automatically refresh from
  production
\item
  \textbf{Referential Integrity}: Cascading filters maintain FK
  relationships
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{multi-environment-setup}{%
\subsection{Multi-Environment Setup}\label{multi-environment-setup}}

\begin{verbatim}
FEATURE_STORE_DEMO (Production)             FEATURE_STORE_DEMO_DEV (Development)
└── CLICKSTREAM_DATA                     └── CLICKSTREAM_DATA
    ├── USERS (100K)                        ├── USERS (10K - 10% sample)
    ├── SESSIONS (500K)                     ├── SESSIONS (~50K)
    └── EVENTS (4.4M)                       └── EVENTS (~440K)
\end{verbatim}

See \texttt{database\_subset/README.md} for complete documentation.

\hypertarget{streamlit-data-manager}{%
\chapter{Streamlit Data Manager}\label{streamlit-data-manager}}

Interactive UI for managing sample data

\hfill\break

\hypertarget{overview-15}{%
\section{Overview}\label{overview-15}}

The \textbf{Clickstream Data Manager} is a Streamlit application that
provides an interactive interface for all data management tasks. It's
the recommended way to set up sample data for the first time, as it
guides you through each step with visual feedback.

\begin{figure}

\includegraphics[width=2.60417in,height=\textheight]{appendices/A_sample_data/data_manager/ui_images/streamlit_sidebar.png} \hfill{}

\caption{Streamlit Sidebar}

\end{figure}

\hypertarget{features}{%
\subsection{Features}\label{features}}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4000}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.6000}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Page
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Purpose
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
📊 Overview & Dashboard showing current data status \\
📥 Initial Load & Generate and load synthetic clickstream data \\
🔄 Incremental Generator & Manage continuous data generation task \\
🌿 Development Branch & Create sampled dev environments with Dynamic
Tables \\
📚 Public Datasets & Load standard ML datasets \\
📈 Monitoring & Track task and Dynamic Table refresh history \\
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{quick-start-3}{%
\section{Quick Start}\label{quick-start-3}}

\hypertarget{prerequisites-2}{%
\subsection{Prerequisites}\label{prerequisites-2}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Install dependencies}
\ExtensionTok{pip}\NormalTok{ install streamlit pandas}

\CommentTok{\# Optional: for TOML parsing (auto{-}detects connections)}
\ExtensionTok{pip}\NormalTok{ install tomli  }\CommentTok{\# Python \textless{} 3.11}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{launch-the-app}{%
\subsection{Launch the App}\label{launch-the-app}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\BuiltInTok{cd}\NormalTok{ Snowflake\_FeatureStore\_Implementation\_Guide/appendices/A\_sample\_data/data\_manager/}

\CommentTok{\# Option 1: Set connection via environment variable}
\BuiltInTok{export} \VariableTok{SNOWFLAKE\_CONNECTION\_NAME}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{your\_connection}
\ExtensionTok{streamlit}\NormalTok{ run app.py}

\CommentTok{\# Option 2: Select connection in the UI (if connections.toml exists)}
\ExtensionTok{streamlit}\NormalTok{ run app.py}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

The app will open in your browser at \texttt{http://localhost:8501}.

\hypertarget{connecting-to-snowflake}{%
\section{Connecting to Snowflake}\label{connecting-to-snowflake}}

The sidebar provides two connection methods:

\hypertarget{named-connection-recommended}{%
\subsection{Named Connection
(Recommended)}\label{named-connection-recommended}}

If you have \texttt{\textasciitilde{}/.snowflake/connections.toml}
configured, the app will automatically discover your connections:

\begin{figure}

{\centering \includegraphics[width=3.125in,height=\textheight]{appendices/A_sample_data/data_manager/ui_images/streamlit_sidebar_connections_dropdown.png}

}

\caption{Connection Dropdown}

\end{figure}

Select your connection from the dropdown. The app shows connection
details (account, user) to help you identify the right one.

\hypertarget{manual-credentials}{%
\subsection{Manual Credentials}\label{manual-credentials}}

Alternatively, enter credentials directly:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Account (e.g., \texttt{xy12345.us-east-1})
\item
  User
\item
  Password
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{common-settings}{%
\subsection{Common Settings}\label{common-settings}}

Regardless of connection method, you can override:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Warehouse} - Compute warehouse to use
\item
  \textbf{Database} - Target database (default:
  \texttt{FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO})
\item
  \textbf{Schema} - Target schema (default: \texttt{CLICKSTREAM\_DATA})
\end{itemize}

Click \textbf{Connect} to establish the connection. The status indicator
will show 🟢 when connected.

\hypertarget{page-walkthroughs}{%
\section{Page Walkthroughs}\label{page-walkthroughs}}

\hypertarget{overview-16}{%
\subsection{📊 Overview}\label{overview-16}}

The Overview page shows the current state of your data:

\begin{figure}

{\centering \includegraphics[width=0.8\textwidth,height=\textheight]{appendices/A_sample_data/data_manager/ui_images/streamlit_overview_dataloaded.png}

}

\caption{Overview Dashboard}

\end{figure}

\textbf{Key metrics displayed:}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Total tables and row counts
\item
  Visitor and event counts
\item
  Bar chart visualization of table sizes
\item
  Detailed table breakdown
\end{itemize}

Use this page to verify data was loaded correctly or to check current
data volumes.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{initial-load}{%
\subsection{📥 Initial Load}\label{initial-load}}

Generate and load synthetic clickstream data into your
\textbf{Production database}.

This page creates the foundational clickstream data model that serves as
the source for all feature engineering examples in this guide. The
Production database contains the complete e-commerce dataset with
visitors, sessions, events, orders, and supporting dimension tables.

\begin{figure}

{\centering \includegraphics[width=0.8\textwidth,height=\textheight]{appendices/A_sample_data/data_manager/ui_images/streamlit_initial_load.png}

}

\caption{Initial Load Page}

\end{figure}

\textbf{Configuration options:}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2667}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4333}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3000}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Option
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Default
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Scale Factor & Controls data volume (0.01 = 1K users, 1.0 = 100K users)
& 0.01 \\
Loading Method & \texttt{simple} (in-memory) or \texttt{bulk} (Parquet
files) & simple \\
Target Database & Where to create the data & FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO \\
Target Schema & Schema for data tables & CLICKSTREAM\_DATA \\
Date Range & Historical date range for generated data & 2022-01-01 to
yesterday \\
\end{longtable}

\textbf{Scale guide:}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}llllll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Scale & Users & Sessions & Events & Orders & Use Case \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
0.01 & \textasciitilde1K & \textasciitilde5K & \textasciitilde50K &
\textasciitilde250 & Development \\
0.1 & \textasciitilde10K & \textasciitilde50K & \textasciitilde500K &
\textasciitilde2.5K & Testing \\
1.0 & \textasciitilde100K & \textasciitilde500K & \textasciitilde5M &
\textasciitilde25K & Full scale \\
\end{longtable}

Click \textbf{Generate \& Load Data} to start. The page shows progress
and final row counts.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{incremental-generator}{%
\subsection{🔄 Incremental Generator}\label{incremental-generator}}

Transform your Production database into a \textbf{live, continuously
updating dataset}.

This page deploys and manages a Snowflake-native incremental data
generator that simulates real-time e-commerce traffic. Once started, the
generator continuously adds new sessions, events, and orders to your
Production database at a refresh frequency of your choosing. This
enables testing of:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Dynamic Tables that react to new data
\item
  Streaming feature pipelines
\item
  Point-in-time correct feature retrieval
\item
  Real-time feature serving scenarios
\end{itemize}

\begin{figure}

{\centering \includegraphics[width=0.8\textwidth,height=\textheight]{appendices/A_sample_data/data_manager/ui_images/streamlit_incremental_load.png}

}

\caption{Incremental Generator Page}

\end{figure}

\textbf{Status section shows:}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Task state (🟢 RUNNING / 🟡 SUSPENDED / ⚪ NOT DEPLOYED)
\item
  Sessions per batch
\item
  Orders per batch
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Controls:}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5000}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5000}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Button
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Action
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
▶️ Start Task & Resume the incremental generation task \\
⏹️ Stop Task & Suspend the task (stops generating data) \\
🚀 Deploy Generator & Deploy the stored procedure and task (first time
setup) \\
\end{longtable}

\textbf{Configuration updates:}

Adjust sessions/orders per batch and click \textbf{Update Config} to
change generation rate.

\textbf{Recent Executions:}

Shows the last 10 batch executions with timestamps, row counts, and
duration.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-warning-color}{\faExclamationTriangle}\hspace{0.5em}{Cost Consideration}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-warning-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-warning-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

The incremental generator runs on a schedule and consumes compute
resources. Remember to \textbf{Stop Task} when not actively testing to
avoid unnecessary costs.

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{development-branch}{%
\subsection{🌿 Development Branch}\label{development-branch}}

Create and maintain a \textbf{live subset of Production data} in a
separate Development database.

This page creates a Development database branch that automatically stays
synchronized with your Production database using Dynamic Tables. The
branch contains a sampled subset of visitors (and all their related
sessions, events, and orders), making it ideal for:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Cost-effective development and testing with smaller data volumes
\item
  Isolated experimentation without affecting production
\item
  Testing feature pipelines with realistic, live-updating data
\item
  Validating Dynamic Table refresh behavior
\end{itemize}

As new data flows into Production (via the Incremental Generator), the
Development branch automatically receives the corresponding subset based
on your sample percentage.

\begin{figure}

{\centering \includegraphics[width=0.8\textwidth,height=\textheight]{appendices/A_sample_data/data_manager/ui_images/streamlit_dev_branch.png}

}

\caption{Development Branch Page}

\end{figure}

\textbf{Create New Branch:}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2667}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4333}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3000}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Option
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Description
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Default
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Production Database & Source database to sample from &
FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO \\
Development Database & New database name to create &
FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\_DEV \\
Sample Percentage & \% of visitors to include & 10\% \\
DT Refresh Lag & How often Dynamic Tables refresh & 1 HOUR \\
\end{longtable}

\textbf{Refresh Lag Options:}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Option & Use Case \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
1 MINUTE & Real-time testing, demos \\
10 MINUTES & Active development \\
15 MINUTES & Development with moderate refresh \\
30 MINUTES & Standard development \\
1 HOUR & Default, balanced cost/freshness \\
2 HOURS & Lower cost, less frequent updates \\
6 HOURS & Minimal cost, batch-style refresh \\
\end{longtable}

\textbf{How it works:}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Creates a new database with identical schema structure
\item
  Samples visitors at the specified percentage
\item
  Creates Dynamic Tables that automatically sync from production
\item
  Maintains referential integrity (related sessions, events, orders
  follow the sampled visitors)
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Manage Existing Branch:}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Load Branch Status} - View current config and DT states
\item
  \textbf{Suspend DTs} - Pause refresh (cost savings when not in use)
\item
  \textbf{Resume DTs} - Resume automatic refresh
\item
  \textbf{Update Refresh Rate} - Change the target lag for all Dynamic
  Tables
\item
  \textbf{Drop Branch} - Delete the development database
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Adjusting Refresh Frequency:}

After creating a branch, you can change how frequently the Dynamic
Tables refresh:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Enter the branch database name
\item
  Select a new target lag from the dropdown
\item
  Click \textbf{⚡ Update Refresh Rate}
\end{enumerate}

This updates all Dynamic Tables in the branch to use the new refresh
interval.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Environment Switching}, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, rightrule=.15mm, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, left=2mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, breakable, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, opacitybacktitle=0.6, colback=white, coltitle=black, leftrule=.75mm]

Development branches use identical object names below the database
level. Switch environments by changing \texttt{USE\ DATABASE}:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{{-}{-} Production}
\KeywordTok{USE} \KeywordTok{DATABASE}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO;}
\KeywordTok{SELECT} \OperatorTok{*} \KeywordTok{FROM}\NormalTok{ CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.}\KeywordTok{EVENTS} \KeywordTok{LIMIT} \DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{;}

\CommentTok{{-}{-} Development (10\% sample)}
\KeywordTok{USE} \KeywordTok{DATABASE}\NormalTok{ FEATURE\_STORE\_DEMO\_DEV;}
\KeywordTok{SELECT} \OperatorTok{*} \KeywordTok{FROM}\NormalTok{ CLICKSTREAM\_DATA.}\KeywordTok{EVENTS} \KeywordTok{LIMIT} \DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{;  }\CommentTok{{-}{-} Same query!}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{monitoring}{%

Track production data generation and development branch Dynamic Table
refreshes:

\end{figure}

The Monitoring page is divided into two main sections:

\textbf{🏭 Production Data Section:}

Monitor the incremental data generator and production table statistics:

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4583}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 2\tabcolsep) * \real{0.5417}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}

\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright

\end{minipage} \\

Data Schema & Schema containing the data tables \\

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
